Prioritizing Following the Imam Over Qunut in Witr
Ruling on conflicting wajibat in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for a follower when the imam bows before the follower finishes qunut, and apply the principle of balancing conflicting wajibat.

Core Idea
When two wajibs conflict in prayer, the obligation of following the imam takes precedence over the qunut.

In the witr prayer, the follower is required to recite the qunut and also to follow the imam in actions. What happens when the imam bows before the follower has finished the qunut? This lesson explains how the Hanafi school resolves this conflict, emphasizing that following the imam is a stronger obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
Recognize the two wajib acts: reciting qunut and following the imam in bowing. The imam bows before the follower completes the qunut.
2
Assess the risk
If the follower fears missing the ruku' with the imam, he must follow immediately. If not, he may complete the qunut and then join.
Fear of missing means the imam is about to rise from ruku'.
3
Apply the precedence rule
Following the imam is prioritized because neglecting it would nullify the obligation of mutaba'ah, which is a stronger wajib.
The qunut can be omitted if necessary.
4
Consider the imam omitting qunut
If the imam himself omits the qunut, the follower still performs it if he can do so without missing the ruku'; otherwise, he follows.
Combine both obligations as much as possible.
5
Generalize the principle
This case illustrates the broader Hanafi rule that when wajibat conflict, the more essential one (mutaba'ah) takes precedence.
Similar rulings apply to other conflicts in prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ركعَ الإمام قبل فراغ المقتدي من قراءة القنوتِ، أو قبل شروعه فيه، وخاف فَوْتَ الرّكوعِ ) مع الإمام (تابع إمامَهُ)؛ لأن اشتغاله به يفوت واجب المتابعة، فتكون أولى، وإن لم يخف فوت المشاركة في الركوع، يقنت جمعاً بين واجبين، ولو تَرَكَ الإمامُ القنوت، يأتي به المؤتم إن أمكنه مشاركة الإمام في الركوع)؛ بجمعه بين الواجبين بحسب الإمكان، (وإلا ) بـأن لم يمكنه المشاركة (تَابَعَهُ)؛ لأن متابعته أولى، وقدمنا ما يفعله المقتدي إذا تركه الإمام ونظائره
And if the imam bows before the follower finishes reading the qunut, or before he begins it, and he fears missing the bowing with the imam, he follows his imam; because his preoccupation with it would miss the obligatory following, so following is more important. If he does not fear missing participation in the bowing, he performs qunut to combine both obligations. And if the imam leaves the qunut, the follower performs it if he can participate with the imam in the bowing, by combining both obligations as much as possible. Otherwise, if he cannot participate, he follows him, because his following is more important. We have already mentioned what the follower does when the imam leaves it and similar cases.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage details the follower's duty when the imam bows before the follower has finished or begun the qunut in witr. The follower must weigh two obligations: completing the qunut (wajib) and following the imam in bowing (also wajib). Since following the imam is a stronger obligation, if the follower fears missing the ruku' with the imam, he should immediately go into ruku' with him, even if it means omitting the qunut. If there is no risk of missing the ruku' (e.g., the imam is slow), the follower should complete the qunut and then join the ruku'. If the imam himself omits the qunut, the follower should still perform it if he can do so without missing the ruku'. If he cannot, he follows the imam.

Key Terms
المتابعة (al-mutaba'ah): The obligation of the follower to follow the imam in the actions of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the follower do if the imam bows while the follower is still reciting the qunut in witr and he fears missing the ruku'?
A) Continue reciting the qunut and then join the ruku' late
B) Immediately follow the imam into ruku'
C) Stop praying and restart the rak'ah
D) Make a gesture to the imam to wait

Key Takeaway
The follower must prioritize following the imam over completing the qunut if there is a risk of missing the ruku'.

Latecomer Catching the Imam in Third Ruku' of Witr
Ruling on latecomer catching imam in witr third rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a latecomer who catches the imam in the third rak'ah ruku' of witr and explain why he does not repeat qunut.

Core Idea
Catching the imam in the third ruku' of witr legally catches the qunut – no repetition.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in witr prayer: a latecomer joins the imam when he is already bowing in the third rak'ah. Since qunut is recited in the third rak'ah before ruku', catching the imam in ruku' means he has effectively caught the qunut by legal ruling. Therefore, he should not perform qunut again when he completes his missed rak'ahs. The passage also notes a minority view equating this case with doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the latecomer joins the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah of witr.
2
Apply the principle of catching a rak'ah
In Hanafi fiqh, catching the imam in ruku' means you have caught that rak'ah.
3
Extend the principle to qunut
Since qunut is an integral part of the third rak'ah, catching the ruku' legally catches the qunut.
4
Derive the ruling
The latecomer does not repeat qunut in his own completed rak'ahs.
5
Note the variant opinion
Abu al-Fadl equates this case to doubt, implying sajda al-sahw, but the majority view prevails.
Refer to the sajda al-sahw chapter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أدرك الإمام في ركوع الثالثة منَ الوِتْرِ، كانَ مُدْرِكَاً للقُنوتِ) حكماً، فلا يأتي بـه فـيـمـا سـبـق بـه). قـال الكمال : أج: ال: أجمعوا على أن المسبوق بركعتين، إذا قنت مع الإمام في الثالثة، لا يقنـت مـرة أخــرى. وعن أبي الفضل تسويته بالشاك، وسيأتي في سجود السهو، انتهى. قال الديري: لأنـه لـو قـنـت ثانياً يتكرر القنوت في محل غير مشروع.
And if he catches the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah of witr, he is considered to have caught the qunut by legal ruling, so he does not perform it in what preceded. Al-Kamal said: They agreed that the person who missed two rak'ahs, if he performs qunut with the imam in the third, he does not perform qunut again. And from Abu al-Fadl, likening him to the one in doubt, and it will come in the chapter on sajda al-sahw. End. Al-Dayri said: Because if he performed qunut a second time, it would be a repetition of qunut in a place where it is not legislated.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation of a latecomer (masbuq) who joins the witr prayer when the imam is already in the ruku' of the third rak'ah. Since the qunut is an obligatory part of the third rak'ah, catching the imam in ruku' means the latecomer has 'caught' the qunut in a legal sense. Thus, he should not perform qunut again when he completes his own missed rak'ahs. The text cites consensus among scholars that the person who missed two rak'ahs, if he performs qunut with the imam in the third, does not repeat it later.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the congregation after the imam has started the prayer.
القنوت (al-qunut): A supplication recited in the witr prayer, wajib according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a latecomer catches the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah of witr, should he perform qunut again in his own qada' rak'ahs?
A) Yes, because he missed the qunut
B) No, because he is considered to have caught it
C) Only if he was present for the qunut recitation
D) He must repeat the entire prayer

Key Takeaway
A latecomer who catches the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah of witr is considered to have caught the qunut and should not repeat it.

Witr Congregation Only in Ramadan
Ruling on performing witr in congregation only during Ramadan, and its preference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on performing witr in congregation in the Hanafi school, distinguishing between Ramadan and other months, and evaluate the conditions under which it is disliked or recommended.

Core Idea
Witr in congregation is recommended only in Ramadan; outside it is disliked if arranged by mutual calling.

This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies a common point of confusion: witr itself is wajib, but performing it in congregation carries different rulings depending on the month. In Ramadan, following tarawih practice, it is recommended; outside Ramadan, caution is advised due to the general dislike for congregational supererogatory prayers other than tarawih. The text also provides nuance on how the congregation is formed, distinguishing between mutual calling and spontaneous following.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the hukm level for performing witr in congregation in Ramadan and outside Ramadan. In Ramadan it is sunnah (recommended); outside Ramadan it is makruh tahrimi if done regularly with tada'i.
The ruling is about the congregational act, not witr itself.
2
Understand the rationale
Why is witr congregation recommended only in Ramadan? Because witr is supererogatory from one aspect, and congregation for nafl prayers other than tarawih is disliked. So caution requires leaving it outside Ramadan.
This is based on the consensus mentioned.
3
Examine the conditions of dislike
The dislike is conditional on tada'i (mutual calling). Spontaneous following of one or two is not disliked; three is disputed; four is disliked by agreement.
This nuance shows that not all forms of congregation are equal.
4
Apply the preferred view
Within Ramadan, witr in congregation is better than praying alone at the end of the night according to Qadi Khan, which is the correct view.
This is the mufta bihi position for Ramadan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُوتِرُ بجماعةٍ ) استحباباً (في رمضــان فقط )، عـلـيـه إجماع المسلمين؛ لأنه نفل من وجه، والجماعة في النفل في غير التراويح مكروهة، فالاحتياط تركها في الوتر خارج رمضان، وعن شمس الأئمة هذا إذا كان على سبيل التداعي، أمـا لـو اقـتـدى واحــد بواحد، أو اثنان بواحد، لا يكره)، وإذا اقتدى ثلاثة بواحد اختلف فيه، وإن اقتدى أربعة بواحد كــره اتفاقاً، من «الفتح»، و « التبيين ، وغيرهما ، ( وصلاته) أي: الوتر (مع الجماعة في رمضان أفضلُ منْ أدائه منفرداً آخر الليل في اختيار قاضي خان). (قَالَ) قاضي خان رحمه الله تعالى: (هُـوَ الصحيح)،
And he performs witr in congregation (recommended) only in Ramadan, upon which there is consensus of the Muslims; because it is supererogatory from one aspect, and congregation in supererogatory prayers other than tarawih is disliked, so caution is to leave it in witr outside Ramadan. From Shams al-A'imma: This is if it is by mutual calling. As for if one person follows one, or two follow one, it is not disliked. If three follow one, there is a difference. If four follow one, it is disliked by agreement. From al-Fath, al-Tabyin, and others. And his prayer, i.e., witr, with congregation in Ramadan is better than performing it alone at the end of the night in the choice of Qadi Khan. Qadi Khan said: It is the correct view.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage states two rulings: (1) Performing witr in congregation is recommended only in Ramadan, because witr is considered supererogatory from one perspective, and congregational supererogatory prayers other than tarawih are generally disliked. Therefore, to avoid dislike, witr congregation is avoided outside Ramadan. (2) Within Ramadan, praying witr in congregation is better than praying it alone at the end of the night, according to Qadi Khan's choice, which is considered the correct view. The text also discusses scenarios when it is not disliked: if one or two followers join, it's fine; three followers raise difference; four followers are disliked by consensus.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): A prayer of an odd number of rak'ahs (usually 3) performed after the night prayer, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
التداعي (al-tada'i): Mutual calling or arranging a congregation by announcement, as opposed to spontaneous following.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on witr congregation outside Ramadan when four followers join one imam?
A) Not disliked
B) Disliked by agreement
C) Recommended
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Witr in congregation is recommended only in Ramadan; outside Ramadan, it is disliked if arranged by mutual calling, with the threshold for consensus dislike at four followers.

Sajdah al-Sahw for Qunut in Witr
Ruling on prostration of forgetfulness for qunut in witr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-sahw for qunut in witr and distinguish it from takbirat al-Id based on the concept of mahall.

Core Idea
Omitting or displacing qunut in witr requires sajdat al-sahw because its place has fully passed, unlike 'Id takbirs.

In this passage, the author clarifies when sajdat al-sahw becomes wajib in witr prayer due to qunut. Many students confuse this with the case of takbirat al-Id, where the ruling differs because the 'place' of those takbirs has not fully elapsed. Understanding the distinction based on the nature of the act (wajib vs. fard) and the concept of mahall is key to applying the rule correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that qunut is a wajib part of witr prayer in the Hanafi school, and its proper place is before ruku'. When qunut is omitted or recited after ruku', the action has been displaced or omitted, triggering sajdat al-sahw.
The text states sajdah is wajib whether one recited qunut after ruku' or omitted it entirely.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the talil (reasoning) provided: because qunut is a wajib action and its proper place (mahall) has passed. The commentator explains that ruku' is fard and cannot be undone for a non-fard (qunut).
The reasoning relies on the hierarchy of rulings: fard cannot be violated for a wajib.
3
Understand the distinction with 'Id takbirs
The text contrasts qunut with takbirat al-Id. In 'Id prayer, if one forgets the extra takbirs and remembers during ruku', they may still perform them because their place extends into the ruku' motion. Qunut's place is only the standing before ruku', which is now past.
This distinction highlights the concept of mahall (place) as a determinant for whether a missed element can be made up without sacrificing a fard.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
Apply the rule: if a wajib (like qunut) is omitted or displaced from its proper place, one must perform sajdat al-sahw at the end of the prayer. Do not attempt to return to standing and undo ruku', as that would violate a fard.
This principle is consistent with the Hanafi maxim that a wajib can be compensated by sajdah but cannot override a fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ويسجد للسهو، لزوال القنوتِ عن محله الأصلي)، فسجود السهو واجب عليه، قنت بعد الرفع أو لم يقنت؛ لأنه إن قنت فقد قدم وأخر، وإن لم يقنت فلتركه الواجب أصلاً، وفرق بين هذا وبين تكبير العيد، فإنه لو تذكره في الركوع يأتي به، والوجه أن القنوت محلـه القيام المطلق وقد فات، ولا يمكن نقض الركوع؛ لأن الركوع فرض والقنوت ليس بفرض، فـلا يجوز نقضه له لأنه دونه، فأما تكبير العيد فمحله لم يفت؛ لأنه شرع في حال القيام، وفيما يجري اه، كذا في « معراج الدراية»،
And he makes sajdah al-sahw, because qunut has left its original place. So sajdah al-sahw is obligatory upon him, whether he recited qunut after the bowing or did not recite it; because if he recited, he has advanced and delayed it, and if he did not recite, it is for leaving the wajib originally. And there is a difference between this and the takbir of 'Id, for if he remembers it in ruku', he performs it. The reason is that the place of qunut is absolute standing, and it has passed, and ruku' cannot be undone because ruku' is fard and qunut is not fard, so it is not permissible to undo it for something lesser. As for takbir of 'Id, its place has not passed because it is prescribed in the state of standing and while going down, etc., as in Ma'arij al-dirayah.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talil) regarding the sajdah al-sahw for qunut in witr. The matn states that one performs sajdah al-sahw because qunut has been removed from its original place. The commentator explains that sajdah is wajib whether one recited qunut after ruku' (which is delaying it from its original place before ruku') or did not recite it at all. The underlying reason (illa) is that qunut's proper place is in the standing before ruku'. If one recites it after ruku', the action has been displaced; if omitted entirely, a wajib has been left. The commentator then distinguishes this case from takbirat al-'Id in the extra takbirs. If one forgets the takbirs and remembers them during ruku', he may perform them because their place has not entirely passed; they are still prescribed during the standing and bending motions. In contrast, qunut's place is only the standing, which has fully passed once ruku' is done. Thus, one cannot undo a fard (ruku') for a non-fard (qunut). This distinction highlights the Hanafi principle that a wajib may be compensated by sajdah al-sahw if omitted or displaced, but not by undoing a fard.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): Supplication recited in witr prayer, specifically before or after ruku' in the last rak'ah.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Two prostrations performed for forgetfulness in prayer to compensate for omissions or displacements of wajibat.
محل (mahall): The proper place or time for an action during prayer, such as qunut being in qiyam before ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is sajdah al-sahw required for qunut in witr according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only if one recites qunut after ruku'
B) Only if one omits qunut entirely
C) Both if one recites it after ruku' or omits it entirely
D) It is never required for qunut

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-sahw is wajib when qunut is omitted or displaced from its proper place in witr because qunut is a wajib action whose mahall has passed.

Follower's Obligation Regarding Qunut When Imam Bows Early or Omits Qunut
Rulings on a follower when the imam bows early or omits qunut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a follower when the imam bows early or omits qunut, and apply the priority rule between two wajib actions.

Core Idea
When two obligations conflict in prayer, following the imam (muta'aba) takes precedence over reciting qunut.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses two specific scenarios in witr prayer: when the imam bows before the follower completes qunut, and when the imam omits qunut entirely. The key principle is that both following the imam and reciting qunut are wajib, but when they conflict, following takes priority. However, if both can be fulfilled, the follower should do both.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
What is the act being ruled? It is the recitation of qunut by a follower (muqtadi) during witr prayer in congregation. The ruling involves two obligations: reciting qunut and following the imam (muta'aba).
2
Identify the two wajib actions in conflict
The follower has two duties: reciting qunut (wajib in witr) and following the imam's actions (wajib al-muta'aba). When the imam bows early while the follower is still in qunut, these duties conflict.
3
State the principle of priority
The Hanafi school rules that the obligation of following the imam takes precedence over qunut when they cannot both be fulfilled simultaneously. This is because muta'aba is a more fundamental obligation tied to the validity of the congregational prayer.
The text says: 'لأن اشتغاله به يفوت واجب المتابعة، فتكون أولى'
4
Apply to scenario 1: Imam bows early
If the imam starts ruku' before the follower finishes or starts qunut, and the follower fears missing the ruku', he must abandon qunut and follow the imam. If he does not fear missing ruku', he should complete qunut and then bow, combining both.
The condition depends on the possibility of 'musharakah' (catching ruku')
5
Apply to scenario 2: Imam omits qunut
If the imam leaves qunut (forgets or deliberately omits), the follower should recite qunut himself if he can still catch the ruku' with the imam. If he cannot, he follows the imam without qunut.
The same priority rule applies: combining if possible, otherwise following takes precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ركع الإمامُ قبل فراغ المقتدي من قراءة القنوتِ، أو قبل شروعه فيه، وخاف فَوْتَ الرّكوعِ ) مع الإمام (تابع إمامَهُ)؛ لأن اشتغاله به يفوت واجب المتابعة، فتكون أولى، وإن لم يخف فوت المشاركة في الركوع، يقنت جمعاً بين واجبين، ولو تَرَكَ الإمامُ القنوت، يأتي به المؤتم إن أمكنه مشاركة الإمام في الركوع)؛ بجمعه بين الواجبين بحسب الإمكان، (وإلا ) بـأن لم يمكنه المشاركة (تَابَعَهُ)؛ لأن متابعته أولى، وقدمنا ما يفعله المقتدي إذا تركه الإمام ونظائره
And if the imam bows before the follower finishes reciting qunut, or before he starts it, and he fears missing the ruku' with the imam, he follows his imam, because occupying himself with it [qunut] causes missing the obligatory following, so [following] takes precedence. And if he does not fear missing participation in ruku', he recites qunut to combine both obligations. And if the imam leaves the qunut, the follower recites it if he can participate with the imam in ruku', combining the two obligations as much as possible. And if not, i.e., he cannot participate, he follows him, because his following takes precedence. And we have already mentioned what the follower does if the imam leaves it and its parallels.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings for a follower (muqtadi) in witr regarding qunut. The first scenario: if the imam begins bowing before the follower has finished or even started qunut, and the follower fears that if he continues qunut he will miss the ruku' with the imam, then he must abandon qunut and follow the imam into ruku'. The reason is that following the imam (muta'aba) is an absolute obligation (wajib) while qunut in this specific situation is a lesser obligation. However, if the follower does not fear missing the ruku' (i.e., he can still complete qunut and still make ruku' with the imam), then he should read qunut and then bow, thereby fulfilling both obligations. The second scenario: if the imam entirely omits qunut (forgets or deliberately leaves it), the follower should still recite qunut himself, provided he can still catch the ruku' with the imam. Again, this combines both obligations. But if he cannot catch the ruku' while reciting qunut, he must abandon qunut and follow the imam, because the obligation of following takes precedence.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The person praying behind the imam (follower).
مشاركة (musharakah): Participation with the imam in ruku', i.e., catching the ruku' in congregation.
واجب المتابعة (wajib al-muta'aba): The obligation of following the imam in actions of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam begins ruku' while the follower is still reciting qunut, and the follower fears he will miss the ruku', what should he do?
A) Continue reciting qunut and catch ruku' afterwards
B) Abandon qunut and go to ruku' immediately
C) Recite a short qunut and then go to ruku'
D) Perform a separate prayer later

Key Takeaway
When two obligations conflict in prayer, the obligation of following the imam (muta'aba) takes precedence, but if both can be fulfilled, they should be combined.

8 min
Masbuq Catching Qunut and Congregation Witr in Ramadan
Rulings on masbuq catching qunut and congregation witr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a masbuq catching qunut in witr and explain the Hanafi position on witr congregation, including the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
A masbuq who catches imam in ruku' of third witr has legally caught qunut; witr congregation is mustahab only in Ramadan.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah covers two related witr rulings. First, it clarifies that a latecomer who joins the imam during the ruku' of the third rak'ah is legally considered to have caught qunut and does not repeat it. Second, it discusses the recommendation and conditions of praying witr in congregation, noting the consensus that it is only recommended in Ramadan, and highlights an internal Hanafi debate on whether congregation is superior to praying alone at the end of the night.

Guided Path
1
Identify the masbuq's situation
Consider a latecomer who catches the imam while he is bowing in the third rak'ah of witr. Determine the legal effect on qunut.
The passage states he is considered to have caught qunut legally.
2
Analyze the ruling on qunut repetition
Understand why the masbuq does not recite qunut again in his missed rak'ahs. The reasoning is that repeating qunut would be unlegislated.
Al-Dayri says: because it would be repetition in an unlegislated place.
3
Examine witr congregation ruling
Identify the recommended (mustahab) time for witr congregation and the disliked (makruh) status outside it. Note exceptions for small spontaneous groups.
Consensus: mustahab only in Ramadan; outside, makruh unless one or two follow spontaneously.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare Qadikhan's view (congregation better) with other Hanafi scholars (alone better). Identify the proofs each side uses.
Qadikhan cites Prophet's and 'Umar's practice; opponents cite lack of Companion consensus.
5
Determine the preponderant view
According to Fath al-Qadir and al-Burhan, Qadikhan's view (congregation better) is preferred.
The text indicates that the preponderant opinion favors congregation.

And if he catches the imam in the ruku' of the third [rak'ah] of witr, he is considered to have caught qunut, so he does not recite it in what he missed. Al-Kamal said: They agreed that the one who missed two rak'ahs, if he recites qunut with the imam in the third, he does not recite it again. And from Abu al-Fadl, he equated him with the one in doubt, and it will come in sajdah al-sahw, end. Al-Dayri said: Because if he recites qunut a second time, it would be repetition in an unlegislated place. And one prays witr in congregation, recommended, only in Ramadan, upon which there is consensus of the Muslims, because it is supererogatory in one aspect, and congregation in supererogatory prayers other than tarawih is disliked, so caution is to leave it in witr outside Ramadan. And from Shams al-A'imma, this is if it is done by gathering [al-tada'i], but if one follows another, or two follow one, it is not disliked. And if three follow one, there is disagreement; and if four follow one, it is disliked by agreement, from al-Fath and al-Tabyin etc. And his prayer, i.e., witr, in congregation in Ramadan is better than performing it alone at the end of the night, according to the choice of Qadikhan. He said: It is the correct [view]. That is, he calls people to gather for witr prayer. Because the Prophet [SAW] led Ibn Abbas in night prayer and used to wake Aisha and she prayed witr with him, and it is authentic that he [SAW] led Anas and the orphan and the old woman and prayed two rak'ahs with them, and it was supererogatory. End. And others corrected the opposite of it, which is that since congregation is permissible, it is better. And because 'Umar [RA] used to lead them in witr. And others, i.e., other than Qadikhan, corrected the opposite. He said in al-Nihaya after mentioning this: Our scholars chose that one should pray witr at home not in congregation, because the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, did not gather for witr in congregation in Ramadan as they gathered for tarawih. Because 'Umar used to lead them in it in Ramadan, and Ubayy ibn Ka'b did not lead them. And in Fath al-Qadir and al-Burhan, that which indicates the preponderance of the first [view], because the Prophet [SAW] prayed witr with them then explained the excuse for leaving it, fearing that it might be made obligatory upon us for Ramadan, and that the rightly-guided caliphs did it. And whoever delayed from congregation in it loved to pray at the end of the night, and congregation at that time is difficult, so it does not indicate that avoiding congregation is better for those who wish to pray witr at the end of the night. Note: We have mentioned that whoever prays witr before sleeping, then stands up at night and prays supererogatory, there is no dislike in it, and he does not pray witr a second time because of his statement: 'No two witrs in a night', narrated by the five except Ibn Majah. And he must leave the recommended [action] indicated by his statement: 'Make the last of your prayers at night witr.' End. And this is outside Ramadan, to combine between the virtue of congregation in witr and tahajjud at the end of the night.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics. First, the ruling on a latecomer (masbuq) who catches the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah of witr. He is considered to have caught qunut as a legal construct, so he does not need to recite qunut again in the rak'ahs he missed. Scholars agree on this. Abu al-Fadl equated this case with a person in doubt regarding qunut, which will be discussed later. The reason, as al-Dayri states, is that repeating qunut would be an innovation in an unlegislated place. Second, the ruling on praying witr in congregation. It is mustahab only in Ramadan due to consensus, as witr is part of tarawih. In other months, congregation for witr is makruh because it is a nafl prayer, and congregation for nafl outside tarawih is disliked. However, if only one or two follow an imam, it is not disliked. If three follow, there is disagreement; if four, it is makruh by agreement. There is a dispute among Hanafi scholars about whether congregation in witr is better than praying alone. Qadikhan held that congregation in Ramadan is better, citing the Prophet's practice and 'Umar's. Others, including the author of al-Nihaya, held that praying alone at home is better, based on the Companions' practice of not gathering for witr as they did for tarawih. The note at the end clarifies that if one prays witr before sleeping, one may pray nafl later but cannot repeat witr. The hadith 'No two witrs in a night' is cited.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who missed part of the prayer with the imam.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer prayed after 'isha, consisting of three rak'ahs in Hanafi school, with qunut in the third.
التداعي (al-tada'i): Calling people to gather for a prayer, specifically for witr congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on praying witr in congregation outside of Ramadan?
A) Recommended (mustahab)
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Permissible without any dislike
D) Forbidden

Key Takeaway
A masbuq who catches the imam in the ruku' of the third witr is considered to have caught qunut; witr congregation is only recommended in Ramadan, and outside it is generally disliked.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Congregational Witr in Ramadan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Witr congregation in Ramadan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on Witr congregation in Ramadan and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Congregational Witr in Ramadan: the preferred view in al-Nihayah is to pray alone, but later authorities favour congregation.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether it is better to pray Witr in congregation during Ramadan or individually at home. The earlier position, attributed to Qazi Khan, held one view, while later scholars in al-Nihayah argued for individual prayer. Others, cited from Fath al-Qadir and al-Burhan, supported congregation. We will analyze the evidence each side uses and the practical implication for the worshipper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, note that the passage corrects Qazi Khan's view, presenting a different position from al-Nihayah. The dispute is whether congregational Witr is superior or individual prayer at home.
The passage uses 'wa sahhaḥa ghayruhu khilāfah' (and another corrected contrary to him).
2
Extract the dalil for individual prayer (al-Nihayah)
The text states the Companions did not gather for Witr in Ramadan as they did for Tarawih. This is the main evidence for individual prayer.
Also, Ubayy ibn Ka'b did not lead the congregation, even though Umar did.
3
Extract the dalil for congregational prayer (Fath al-Qadir and al-Burhan)
These sources cite the Prophet's practice of praying Witr in congregation, and the fact that the rightly guided caliphs continued it.
The Prophet later left it out of fear that it would become obligatory.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the congregational argument
The author explains that the Prophet stopped congregation to avoid obligation, and the Caliphs' practice does not prove it is always better because one might want to pray tahajjud later.
This reasoning allows combining both virtues: congregation and tahajjud.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference affects whether a person should attend the mosque for Witr in Ramadan or pray at home alone.
The note adds that outside Ramadan, individual prayer is preferable to combine congregation with tahajjud.

And he corrected others contrary to it. And it is because when congregation was permissible, it was better. And because Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) used to lead them in Witr. Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage discusses the issue of praying Witr in congregation during Ramadan. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars like Qazi Khan held one view, but others corrected him. The preferred view in al-Nihayah is that it is better to pray Witr at home alone, because the Companions did not gather for it as they did for Tarawih. However, Fath al-Qadir and al-Burhan indicate the preferability of congregation based on the Prophet's practice and the Caliphs. The final note clarifies that if one has already prayed Witr before sleeping, he may pray additional nafl at night without repeating Witr, following the hadith. This is for non-Ramadan nights to get both congregation and tahajjud.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayer, typically one rak'ah.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregational prayer led by an imam.
التراويح (al-tarawih): Special night prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan.
التهجد (al-tahajjud): Voluntary night prayer performed after sleeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is mandatory.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, there is a valid difference on whether to pray Witr in congregation during Ramadan; the preferred view in al-Nihayah is to pray at home, but later authorities permit congregation.

Categories of Supererogatory Acts: Nafl and Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Definitions and hierarchical classification of supererogatory acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of nafl and sunnah, and classify the two rak'ahs before Fajr within the hierarchy of supererogatory acts.

Core Idea
Sunnah mu'akkadah is the highest category of nafl – the two rak'ahs before Fajr are persistently performed by the Prophet.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi classification of legislated acts under 'azimah into fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafil. We will define both sunnah and nafl, explain why the author uses 'nawafil' as a broader term, and then identify the first sunnah mu'akkadah: the two rak'ahs before Fajr. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for prioritizing acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish 'azimah from rukhsah
Recognize that the shari'ah divides into two categories: 'azimah (resolution) and rukhsah (concession). Under 'azimah, there are four levels in order: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafil.
This hierarchy is fundamental in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Define 'nafl' linguistically and technically
Linguistically, nafl means increase (e.g. ghanimah is called nafalah). Technically in shari'ah, nafalah is an act that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah.
The author uses 'nawafil' because it is more general than 'sunan'.
3
Define 'sunnah' in shari'ah
Sunnah is the path followed in religion without being fard or wajib. It includes the Prophet's words and actions, and there is a difference regarding the practice of the Companions.
Sunnah is divided into mu'akkadah (emphasized) and mandub (recommended).
4
Identify the first sunnah mu'akkadah
The text explicitly states: 'Sunnah mu'akkadah: two rak'ahs before Fajr.' This is the most emphasized supererogatory prayer, consistently performed by the Prophet.
This prayer is stronger than other nafl prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان النوافل
سُنَّ سَنَّةٌ مُؤكَّدةً رَكعتانِ قبل الفجر،

فصل في بيان النوافل
عبر بالنوافل دون السنن لأنَّ النفل أعم، إذ كل سنة نافلة ولا عكس، (سن) اعلم أن المشروع ا ينقسم إلى قسمين: عزيمة ورخصة، والعزيمة هي الأصل، وهي أربعة أنواع: فريضة، وواجب، وسنة، ونفل، وقد مضى الأولان وهذا لبيان السنة والنفل، وقدم السنة لأنها أقوى من النفل، وكان أقرب إلى الواجب والفرض، ثم النفل باللغة: عبارة عن الزيادة، ومنه سميت الغنيمة نفلاً؛ لأنها زائدة علـى مـا وضع له الجهاد، وهو إعلاء كلمة الله تعالى، ومنه قول لبيد : [ من الرمل ]
إنَّ تقوى ربنا خير نفل(۱)
وسمي ولد الزنا نافلة لهذا، وفي الشرع : النفل : عبارة عن فعل شيء ليس بفرض ولا واجب ولا مسنون، وقال القاضي الإمام أبو زيد رحمه الله : النوافل شرعت لجبر نقصان) تمكن في الفرض؛ لأن العبد وإن عَلَتْ رتبته لا يخلو عن تقصير (۳)، حتى أن واحداً لو قدر أن يصلي الفرائض مــن غـيـر نقصان لا يلام بترك السنن من ( الجوهرة ) و ( المستصفى»، و « الدراية»، وفيها : قال «قاضي خان» : السنة قبل المكتوبة شرعت لقطع طمع الشيطان، فإنه يقول: من لم يطعني في تــرك مـا لـم يكتب عليه، فكيف يطعني في ترك ما كتب عليه (سنة) قدمنا تفسير السنة، وهي ) ب: الطريقة مرضية كانت أو غير مرضية، وفي الشريعة هي الطريقة المسلوكة في الدين من غير افتراض ولا وجـوب. وهـي تتناول قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وفعله، وفي تناول إطلاقها سنة الصحابة خلافاً، وقال صاحب « النهاية » : هـي مـا فعله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم على طريق المواظبة ولم يتركها إلا بعذر كذا في ( التوضيح»، والسنة على قسمين: مؤكد ومندوب شرع في المؤكد فقال: (مُؤكَّدةً : رَكعتان قبل فرض ( الفجر ) وابتدأ بها مــن
Chapter on explaining the supererogatory prayers. Sunnah mu'akkadah: two rak'ahs before Fajr. Chapter on explaining the supererogatory prayers. He expressed it with nawafil rather than sunan because nafalah is more general, since every sunnah is a nafalah but not vice versa. (Sunnah) Know that the legislated acts are divided into two types: 'azimah and rukhsah. 'Azimah is the original, and it is of four types: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafil. The first two have passed, and this is to explain sunnah and nafil. He prefaced sunnah because it is stronger than nafil and closer to wajib and fard. Then nafalah in language is an expression for increase; from it ghanimah is called nafalah because it is an increase over what jihad is established for, which is uplifting the word of Allah. And from it is the saying of Labid: 'Indeed the piety of our Lord is the best nafalah.' And the child of zina is called nafalah for this reason. In shari'ah, nafalah is an expression for doing something that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah. And al-Qadi Abu Zaid (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Nawafil are legislated to compensate for deficiency that occurs in the fard, because the servant, even if his rank is high, is not free from shortcomings, so much so that if one were able to pray the fard prayers without deficiency, he would not be blamed for leaving the sunan. From al-Jawharah, al-Mustasfa, and al-Dirayah. And in them: Qazi Khan said: The sunnah before the prescribed prayer was legislated to cut off the hope of the devil, because he says: 'He who did not obey me in leaving what was not prescribed upon him, how can he obey me in leaving what was prescribed upon him?' (Sunnah) We have previously explained the sunnah, and it is, according to the (alternative: a path that is pleasing or otherwise). In shari'ah it is the path followed in religion without being fard or wajib. It includes the saying and action of the Prophet (peace be upon him). There is a difference regarding the inclusion of the sunnah of the Companions in its unrestricted application. And the author of al-Nihayah said: It is what the Messenger of Allah did in the manner of persistence and did not leave except for an excuse. This is in al-Tawdih. And the sunnah is of two types: mu'akkadah and mandub. He legislated for the mu'akkadah, saying: (Mu'akkadah: two rak'ahs before the fard of Fajr) and he started with it from...
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This is the beginning of the chapter on nawafil in the commentary. The commentator explains why the author used 'nawafil' instead of 'sunan' — because nafilah is a broader category encompassing sunnah. He then categorizes the shari'ah into 'azimah (resolution) and rukhsah (concession), and under 'azimah there are four levels: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafil. The focus here is on sunnah and nafil. He gives the linguistic and technical definition of nafilah, quoting the poet Labid and al-Qadi Abu Zaid who says nawafil compensate for deficiencies in fard. Then he defines sunnah as the path of the Prophet, with a note on whether it includes the practice of the Companions. Finally, he states that the first sunnah mu'akkadah is the two rak'ahs before Fajr, which is the strongest sunnah prayer.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): In shari'ah, an act that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah; a supererogatory act.
السنة (al-sunnah): The path followed in religion without being fard or wajib; includes the sayings and actions of the Prophet, and according to some, the practice of the Companions.

D) Witr.

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs before Fajr are the first and most emphasized sunnah mu'akkadah, forming the highest category of nafl.

The Emphasized Sunnah (Sunnah Mu'akkadah): Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib
Defines sunnah and nafil, then lists sunnah mu'akkadah prayers with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of the two rak'ahs before Fajr as sunnah mu'akkadah, explain the proofs from hadith, and identify the relied-upon position despite the intra-Hanafi difference.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs before Fajr are the strongest sunnah mu'akkadah, almost compulsory, but not wajib.

In this passage from a commentary on Nur al-Idah, the author clarifies the distinction between nafil and sunnah, then focuses on the emphasized sunnah prayers (sunnah mu'akkadah). The most important of these is the two rak'ahs before Fajr, whose ruling and proofs are discussed in detail, including an internal Hanafi difference. By the end of this lesson, you will navigate the evidence and understand why the relied-upon position treats it as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that two rak'ahs before Fajr are 'sunnah mu'akkadah'. Confirm this is the act and its hukm level.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is stronger than ordinary nafil but not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Multiple hadith are cited: the virtue of Fajr sunnah being better than the world, the Prophet's consistency, and Aisha's testimony. Identify each proof and its source.
Hadith from Muslim, Tabarani, etc.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
For the hadith 'khayr min al-dunya' (better than the world), consider how the word 'khayr' indicates superiority but not obligation, consistent with sunnah status.
In Hanafi usul, commands indicate obligation, but comparatives like 'khayr' are not imperative.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage mentions that al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that praying the Fajr sunnah sitting without excuse invalidates it, and al-Marghinani reported that Abu Hanifa considered them wajib. Understand this divergence.
Two positions: sunnah mu'akkadah (majority) and wajib (narrated from Abu Hanifa).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the school is sunnah mu'akkadah, as stated in the matn and supported by the majority. Identify the tarjih authority (e.g., the author of al-Hidayah).
The scholar becoming a reference for fatwa is allowed to leave other sunan but not the Fajr sunnah.

ركعتين سنة الفجر (٧٢٥).
Chapter on explaining the supererogatory prayers. Two rak'ahs before Fajr are an emphasized sunnah. He used 'nawafil' instead of 'sunan' because nafil is more general, as every sunnah is nafil but not vice versa. Know that legislated actions are divided into two: 'azimah (firm resolve) and rukhsah (concession). 'Azimah is the original and is of four types: fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafil. The first two have preceded, and this is to explain sunnah and nafil. He gave precedence to sunnah because it is stronger than nafil and closer to wajib and fard. Nafil linguistically means increase; hence war booty is called nafil because it is an increase over what jihad was established for, which is exalting Allah's word. From this is the saying of Labid: 'Indeed, piety towards our Lord is the best nafil.' The child of zina is called nafilah for this reason. In Sacred Law, nafil is an expression for doing something that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah. Qadi Imam Abu Zaid said: Supererogatory acts were legislated to compensate for deficiency that occurs in the fard, because the servant, even if high in rank, is not free from shortcoming. So much so that if one were able to perform the obligatory prayers without any deficiency, he would not be blamed for leaving the sunan. From al-Jawharah, al-Mustasfa, and al-Dirayah, in which Qadi Khan said: The sunnah before the obligatory prayer was legislated to cut off the hope of the devil, for he says: 'Whoever does not obey me in leaving what was not written upon him, how will he obey me in leaving what was written upon him?' We have already explained the definition of sunnah: it is a path, whether praiseworthy or not. In Sacred Law, it is the path followed in religion without obligation or necessity. It includes the sayings and actions of the Prophet. There is disagreement about whether the term 'sunnah' applies to the practice of the Companions. The author of al-Nihayah said: It is what the Messenger of Allah did in the manner of consistency and never abandoned except for an excuse. Sunnah is of two types: mu'akkadah (emphasized) and mandub (recommended). He began with the emphasized and said: 'Emphasized: two rak'ahs before the Fajr prayer.' He started with them following al-Hidayah because they are the strongest of the sunan. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that if one prays them sitting without excuse, it is not permissible. Al-Marghinani mentioned from Abu Hanifa that they are wajib. They said: The scholar, when he becomes a reference for fatwa, may leave other sunan for the people's need, except the sunnah of Fajr. Due to his saying: 'The two rak'ahs of Fajr are more beloved to me than the world and what is in it' – in another wording: 'Better than the world and what is in it' – narrated by Muslim. And his saying: 'Do not leave the two rak'ahs of Fajr, for in them are the desirable things.' And his saying: 'Do not abandon them even if horses trample you.' And the saying of Aisha: 'The Prophet prayed and supplicated, but I did not see him leave the two rak'ahs before Fajr in travel or residence, in health or sickness' – narrated by Tabarani. And her saying: 'The Messenger of Allah was not more committed to any supererogatory prayer than to the two rak'ahs before Fajr' – narrated by the two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) as in al-Burhan. 'Al-Ragha'ib' is the plural of 'raghibah', meaning abundant gift and what is desired from precious wealth. In al-Mabsut, he began with the sunnah of Zuhr because it is the first prayer in existence; the sunnah follows the fard, and the first prayer made obligatory was Zuhr – meaning the first prayer prayed after its obligation. Then they differed about which is most virtuous after the two rak'ahs of Fajr. Al-Halwani said: The two rak'ahs of Maghrib, for he never left them in travel or residence; then those after Zuhr because it is a sunnah agreed upon, unlike those before it, because it is said they are for separating the adhan and iqamah; then those after Isha; then those before Zuhr; then those before Asr; then those before Isha. And it is said: Those after Isha and those before Zuhr and after Zuhr and after Maghrib are all equal. And it is said: Those before Zuhr are such – and al-Hasan corrected this and did well, as in al-Dirayah: 'It is the most correct' – because the transmission of explicit consistency upon them is stronger than the transmission of his consistency upon others besides the two rak'ahs of Fajr. And it is an emphasized sunnah: two rak'ahs after Zuhr. We will mention that it is recommended to pray four rak'ahs after Zuhr. And it is an emphasized sunnah: two rak'ahs after Maghrib. It is recommended to lengthen the recitation in the sunnah of Maghrib. It has been narrated that he used to recite in the first of them 'The Most High' (Surah al-A'la) ...
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on Nur al-Idah, explaining the chapter on supererogatory prayers. The author begins by distinguishing between nafil and sunnah, noting that nafil is the broader category. He then outlines the four types of obligatory acts (fard, wajib, sunnah, nafil) and focuses on sunnah and nafil. The definition of nafil is given linguistically (increase) and technically (an act not fard, wajib, or sunnah). He cites a hadith that supererogatory acts compensate for deficiencies in obligatory prayers. The passage then turns to the emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), specifically the two rak'ahs before Fajr. Evidence for their strong status includes hadiths about their virtue and the Prophet's consistency. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: according to a narration from Abu Hanifa (via al-Hasan), praying them sitting without excuse is invalid, and al-Marghinani reported that Abu Hanifa considered them wajib. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that they are sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib. The author then lists other emphasized sunnah prayers: two rak'ahs after Zuhr and two after Maghrib. He also discusses the virtue of these prayers, noting scholarly differences on which is most virtuous after Fajr. The overall message is that these sunan are strongly recommended due to Prophetic practice, particularly the Fajr sunnah.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and rarely abandoned; its omission is discouraged but not sinful.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory act that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah; voluntary worship for extra reward.
عزيمة (azimah): The original, non-concessionary ruling; includes fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling of the two rak'ahs before Fajr?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Nafil

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs before Fajr are sunnah mu'akkadah—the strongest non-obligatory prayer—and should never be abandoned, even in travel.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Sunnah Mu'akkadah and Mandub Rawatib Prayers
Explanation of rawatib classification with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sunnah mu'akkadah and mandub rawatib prayers, list each category with its evidence, and identify the ikhtilaf regarding 'Asr and 'Isha prayers.

Core Idea
Not all rawatib are equal: Hanafis divide them into emphasized sunnah and recommended acts, affecting the ruling on omission.

In this passage, the author of Imdad al-Fattah explains the Hanafi classification of supererogatory prayers associated with the five daily prayers (rawatib). He distinguishes between two levels: sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) and mandub (recommended). The sunnah mu'akkadah are those the Prophet consistently performed and whose abandonment without excuse is blameworthy; the mandub are meritorious but not obligatory. We will examine the list for each category and the proofs cited, including hadith that establish the status and number of rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage first discusses sunnah mu'akkadah: two after Maghrib, two after 'Isha, four before Dhuhr, four before and after Jumu'ah (and by implication, two before Fajr). Then it discusses mandub: four before 'Asr and four before 'Isha. Note the different evidences cited for each.
The text also mentions recitation details for some prayers.
2
Analyze the proofs for sunnah mu'akkadah
For each sunnah mu'akkadah, the author provides a specific hadith or report. For example, for two after Maghrib, a hadith from Anas; for four before Dhuhr, the hadith 'Whoever leaves the four before Dhuhr, my intercession will not reach him' and the practice of Abu Ayyub; for Jumu'ah, reports from Ibn 'Abbas and 'Ali and a hadith about praying four after Jumu'ah. Identify the type of evidence (hadith) and its source.
Note the condition that the four after Jumu'ah should be prayed with one taslim.
3
Examine the proofs for mandub prayers
For 'Asr, the author cites multiple hadith encouraging four rak'ahs, but also notes a difference of opinion: some narrations mention two rak'ahs. Consequently, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and al-Quduri give a choice. For 'Isha, the recommendation is four, but there is also a report of two. Identify the ikhtilaf sources.
The text mentions that for 'Asr, the more common position in the Hanafi school is that it is mandub and four rak'ahs are preferable.
4
Understand the ruling distinction
The hanafi_position_box indicates that sunnah mu'akkadah omission is disliked (makruh), while mandub omission is not blameworthy. This affects daily practice: one should be more careful with sunnah mu'akkadah.
The mufta bihi for 'Asr is the mandub status with recommendation of four; for 'Isha, similar.
5
Identify the cross-madhhab difference
The classification of mu'akkadah vs. mandub is a Hanafi feature. Other schools may consider all rawatib simply as sunnah, with different numbers. This shows the importance of madhhab-specific rulings.

And after the ‘Isha’, and four before Dhuhr, and before Jumu‘ah, and after it. (In the first rak‘ah) there is no doubt from the Lord of the worlds [Quran 32:2] and in the second: Blessed is He in whose hand is the kingdom [Quran 67:1] — thus in al-Jawharah. And from Anas: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Whoever prays two rak‘ahs after Maghrib before speaking to anyone, reciting in the first al-Fatihah and Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun [109:1], and in the second al-Fatihah and Qul huwa Allahu ahad [112:1], his sins will be shed like a snake sheds its skin. (Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri said: Ibn al-Najjar transmitted it in his history.) And two rak‘ahs after ‘Isha’. And there is an emphasized sunnah of four rak‘ahs before Dhuhr due to his saying: Whoever leaves the four before Dhuhr, my intercession will not reach him — thus in al-Ikhtiyar. And due to the hadith of Abu Ayyub: that the Prophet used to pray four before Dhuhr when the sun passed its zenith, so Abu Ayyub al-Ansari asked him about that, and he said: The gates of heaven open at this hour, and I love that good deeds ascend for me at that hour. I said: Is there recitation in all of them? He said: Yes. I said: Do you separate them with taslim? He said: No — thus in al-Burhan. And due to his saying: There is no Muslim servant who prays twelve rak‘ahs of supererogation besides the obligatory except that Allah will build for him a house in Paradise — narrated by Muslim, and al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa’i added: four before Dhuhr, two after it, two after Maghrib, two after ‘Isha’, and two before the Fajr prayer. And there is an emphasized sunnah of four rak‘ahs before Jumu‘ah due to the saying of Ibn ‘Abbas and ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with them): The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray four before Jumu‘ah, not separating anything between them. And four after it, because the Prophet used to pray four after Jumu‘ah, making taslim at the end of them — narrated by al-Hafiz Abu ‘Abd Allah al-Ashram in al-Nasikh wa al-Mansukh, thus in al-Yanbu‘ by al-Suyuti, and due to his saying: When you pray after Jumu‘ah, pray four; but if something hurries you, pray two in the mosque and two when you return — narrated by the group except al-Bukhari. And his words (with one taslim) are related to his saying 'four', so it is a condition in four-rak‘ah prayers, and its evidence has preceded. Al-Zayla‘i said: Even if he prays them with two taslims, it is not considered as the sunnah. End. Perhaps it is conditional when there is no excuse, because it refutes what you know from his saying: 'if something hurries you'. Then he began explaining the second category, which is the mustahabb, and said: (and it is recommended) i.e., it is commendable (four rak‘ahs before ‘Asr) due to what Ibn ‘Umar narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Whoever prays four rak‘ahs before ‘Asr, the fire will not touch him — thus in al-Suhayli. And in Sharh al-Wajiz it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) said: May Allah have mercy on a person who prays four before ‘Asr. And he (peace be upon him) said: Whoever prays four before ‘Asr, they will be a shield for him from the fire — thus in al-Mabsut. And Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and al-Quduri gave the worshiper a choice between praying four or two before ‘Asr, due to differing reports. He (peace be upon him) said: The Prophet used to pray two before ‘Asr — narrated by Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi and Ahmad narrated four instead of two and said: 'May Allah have mercy on a person who prays four before ‘Asr.' End. From al-Diraya, al-Fath, and al-Burhan. And four before ‘Isha’ are recommended, as said in al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar: It is recommended to pray four before ‘Isha’, and it is said: two, and after it four, and it is said: two.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is from a sharh (commentary) on Nur al-Idah, explaining the rulings on rawatib (supererogatory prayers associated with the obligatory prayers). The author divides them into two categories: sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) and mandub (recommended, also called mustahabb). The sunnah mu'akkadah include: two rak‘ahs after Maghrib (with specific recitations mentioned in a hadith), two after ‘Isha’, four before Dhuhr, four before Jumu‘ah, and four after Jumu‘ah. The evidence for each is cited, including hadith such as the threat of withholding intercession for leaving the four before Dhuhr, the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Abu Ayyub and Ibn ‘Abbas, and the general hadith of the twelve rak‘ahs. The author notes that the four after Jumu‘ah should be prayed with one taslim (at the end) according to al-Zayla‘i, and if done with two taslims it does not count as sunnah, unless there is an excuse. The second category, mandub, includes four rak‘ahs before ‘Asr and four before ‘Isha’. For ‘Asr, there is some ikhtilaf (difference) in the reports: some narrations indicate two rak‘ahs, others four. Consequently, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and al-Quduri give the worshiper the choice. The author cites multiple hadith encouraging four before ‘Asr, emphasizing the reward. For ‘Isha’, the recommendation of four is mentioned, with an alternative view of two. Overall, the Hanafi school holds these rawatib as sunnah mu'akkadah for the first set (emphasis on consistency) and mandub for the second (less emphasis but reward).

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized supererogatory act that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged; leaving it without excuse is disliked (makruh).
مندوب (mandub): A recommended act that carries reward but whose omission is not blameworthy; also called mustahabb.
رواتب (rawatib): Supererogatory prayers that are regularly performed before or after the obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is considered a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized) rawatib prayer in the Hanafi school according to this passage?
A) Four rak'ahs before 'Asr
B) Two rak'ahs after Maghrib
C) Four rak'ahs before 'Isha
D) Four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah but with two taslims

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, rawatib prayers are divided into sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized) and mandub (recommended), with specific proofs and some ikhtilaf on number.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Recommended Prayers: Before Asr, Before and After Isha, After Maghrib
Listing mandub prayers with hadith proofs and intra-madhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended number of rak'as for the mandub prayers before Asr, before Isha, after Isha, and after Maghrib, and explain the intra-madhab differences in the evidence.

Core Idea
Four rak'as before Asr and Isha, four after Isha, and six after Maghrib are recommended — but flexibility exists due to differing narrations.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists recommended prayers beyond the regular sunnah muakkadah. While the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed these occasionally, they are classified as mandub (recommended) rather than sunnah muakkadah. The commentator presents hadith evidence and notes variations within the Hanafi school, particularly for before Asr where some scholars allow two rak'as.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State each prayer time and the recommended number of rak'as as given in the matn: four before Asr, four before Isha, four after Isha, six after Maghrib.
These are all mandub (recommended), not sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil for one prayer
For before Asr, the hadith 'Whoever prays four rak'as before Asr, the Fire will not touch him' is cited. Also 'May Allah have mercy on a person who prays four before Asr.'
These ahadith indicate reward but not obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The promise of reward without threat of punishment shows the act is recommended (mandub). The command is not imperative but encouraging.
Hanafi usul: al-amr al-mujarrad an al-qarinah yufid al-wujub, but here the presence of reward without punishment indicates istihbab.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and al-Quduri allow two or four before Asr due to conflicting hadith: Abu Dawud narrates that the Prophet prayed two, while Tirmidhi and Ahmad narrate four.
The ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school, not between madhahib.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The matn and commentary recommend four but acknowledge the choice. The mufta bihi is that both are acceptable, with four being more virtuous.
The commentator does not resolve the ikhtilaf definitively.

والثالثة والرابعة الإخلاص والمعوذتين، مرة في كـــل ركعة، كذا في « الدراية»، (و) ندب (ست) ركعات ( بعد المغرب) لقوله : « مَنْ صَلَّى بَعْدَ المَغْرِبِ ستْ رَكْعَاتِ، كُتبَ مِنَ الأوَّابِينَ»، وتلا قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنَّهُ كَانَ لِلْأَوَّبِي غَفُورًا ) الامراة : ٢٥] والأواب: الذي إذا أذنب بادر إلى التوبة. وعن أبي هريرة أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: «مَنْ صَلَّى بَعْدَ المَغْرِبِ مِتْ رَكْعَاتٍ لَمْ يَتَكَلَّمَ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُنَّ بِسُوءٍ عَدَلْنَ لَهُ عِبَادَةُ اثنتي عشرة سنة ) وعن عائشة أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: «مَنْ صَلَّى بَعْدَ المَغْرِبِ عِشْرِينَ رَكْعَةً بَنَى اللَّهُ تَعَالَى لَهُ بَيْتَاً فِي الجنَّة ) ( وعن ابن عباس أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: «مَنْ صَلَّى أَرْبَعَ رَكْعَاتٍ بَعْدَ المَغْرِبِ قبل أنْ يُكَلَّمَ أَحَدًا رُفِعَتْ لَهُ في عِلْمِينَ، وَكانَ كَمَنْ أدْرَكَ لَيْلَةَ القَدْرِ في المَسْجِدِ الأَقْصَى، وَهُوَ خَيْرٌ لَهُ
With one taslim. And four before Asr and Isha are recommended. Rak'as he makes taslim at the end of them. Narrated by al-Hafiz Abu Abdillah al-Ashram in al-Nasikh wa al-Mansukh, as in al-Yanbu' by al-Suyuti. And for his saying: 'When you pray after Jumu'ah, pray four, and if something hastens you, pray two in the mosque and two when you return' narrated by the group except Bukhari. And his saying 'with one taslim' is attached to his saying 'four', so it is a restriction for the four-rak'a prayers. And its proof has preceded. And al-Zayla'i said: even if he prays them with two taslims, it is not considered valid for the sunnah. End. Perhaps it is restricted to the absence of excuse; because what you know from his saying 'if something hastens you' the hadith refutes it. Then he began explaining the second category, which is al-mustahabb, so he said: 'And recommended' i.e., recommended 'four rak'as before Asr' because of what Ibn Umar narrated that the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'Whoever prays four rak'as before Asr, the Fire will not touch him.' As in al-Suhayli, and in Sharh al-Wajiz it is narrated that the Prophet said: 'May Allah have mercy on a person who prays four before Asr.' And the Prophet said: 'Whoever prays four before Asr, it will be a shield for him from the Fire.' As in al-Mabsut. And Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and al-Quduri gave the worshiper a choice between praying four or two before Asr, due to differing hadiths. He said: 'The Prophet used to pray two before Asr' narrated by Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi and Ahmad narrated 'four' instead of two, and he said: 'May Allah have mercy on a person who prays four before Asr.' End from al-Diraya, al-Fath, and al-Burhan. 'And' recommended four before Isha because of what he said in al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar: it is recommended to pray four before Isha, and it is said two, and after it four, and it is said two. And from Aisha that the Prophet used to pray four before Isha, then four after it, then lie down. End. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit: if one performs voluntary prayer before Asr with four and before Isha with four, it is good; because the Prophet did not persist on them. End. And in Miraj al-Diraya: the four before Isha are optional, with evidence that Muhammad called it 'good' in al-Asl, and did not mention it among the regular sunnahs. End. So whoever says that no hadith has been mentioned specifically about the four before Isha, perhaps he has not seen what the author of al-Ikhtiyar said, and what we have mentioned also. 'And' recommended four after it i.e., Isha, because of what we narrated from al-Ikhtiyar and his saying: 'Whoever prays four before Zuhr, it is as if he prayed the night prayer, and whoever prays them after Isha, it is like them of Laylat al-Qadr.' And in Fawaid al-Rustaghfani: one recites after Fatiha in the first Ayat al-Kursi three times, in the second Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad three times, in the third Qul A'udhu bi Rabbi al-Falaq three times, in the fourth Qul A'udhu bi Rabbi al-Nas three times. And in al-Multaqat: in the second, third, and fourth, al-Ikhlas and al-Mu'awwidhatayn once in each rak'a. As in al-Diraya. 'And' recommended six rak'as after Maghrib for his saying: 'Whoever prays six rak'as after Maghrib will be recorded among the awwabin.' And he recited the verse: 'Indeed, He is ever Forgiving to the returning [to Him].' And al-Awwab is one who hastens to repentance when he sins. And from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet said: 'Whoever prays six rak'as after Maghrib without speaking evil in between them, it will be equivalent to twelve years of worship.' And from Aisha that the Prophet said: 'Whoever prays twenty rak'as after Maghrib, Allah will build a house for him in Paradise.' And from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said: 'Whoever prays four rak'as after Maghrib before speaking to anyone, it will be raised for him in Illiyin, and he will be like one who reached Laylat al-Qadr in al-Aqsa Mosque, and it is better for him.'
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah deals with recommended (mandub) prayers beyond the regular sunnah rawatib. The commentator first concludes the discussion on the four-rak'a sunnah of Jumu'ah (previous section) and then moves to the second category: mustahabb (recommended). He states that four rak'as before Asr are recommended, citing multiple hadiths: 'Whoever prays four before Asr will not be touched by the Fire,' and similar narrations. However, he notes that Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and al-Quduri gave the worshiper a choice between two and four rak'as before Asr, due to conflicting narrations: some say the Prophet prayed two, others four. The commentator does not explicitly choose one view but presents both. Then he discusses four rak'as before Isha, citing hadith that the Prophet prayed four before Isha and four after, then lay down. He notes that al-Muhit says it is 'good' because the Prophet did not persist, and Miraj al-Diraya says it is optional (mukhayyar), as Muhammad in al-Asl called it 'good' but did not list it among the regular sunnahs. For after Isha, four rak'as are recommended, with a hadith promising reward like Laylat al-Qadr. Additionally, he mentions recommended recitations for these four rak'as: Ayat al-Kursi three times in first rak'a, Surah al-Ikhlas three times in second, and al-Falaq and al-Nas three times in third and fourth respectively (or once per rak'a in another view). Finally, he discusses six rak'as after Maghrib, citing multiple hadiths: one equates it to twelve years of worship, another to building a house in Paradise for twenty rak'as, and a third for four rak'as after Maghrib. The commentator does not resolve the differences but presents the range of narrations, showing that various numbers are reported, with six being the most commonly cited for the 'awwabin' prayer. Throughout, the commentary follows the matn's structure, expanding with proofs and intra-madhhab differences.

Key Terms
مندوب (mandūb): A recommended act; performance is rewarded, omission is not sinful. Synonym of mustahabb.
سنة راتبة (sunnah rātibah): Regular sunnah prayers that the Prophet consistently performed, like before and after fard prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, how many rak'as are recommended after Maghrib according to the primary hadith cited?
A) Two rak'as
B) Four rak'as
C) Six rak'as
D) Twenty rak'as

Key Takeaway
The mandub prayers before Asr, Isha, after Isha, and after Maghrib are recommended with specific numbers, but flexibility is allowed due to differing authentic narrations.

Four Rak'ahs Before Isha: Recommended, Not Confirmed
Establishing the recommendation of four rak'ahs before Isha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the four rak'ahs before Isha and identify the proof that establishes it as recommended but not muakkadah.

Core Idea
The four rak'ahs before Isha are recommended, not confirmed sunnah, because the Prophet's practice lacked persistence.

Many Muslims are familiar with the regular sunnah prayers (rawatib) that accompany the obligatory prayers. However, the four rak'ahs before Isha occupy a different category: they are recommended but not stressed. In this lesson, we will examine the Hanafi position, the evidence from the Prophet's practice, and why it is classified as optional.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Hukm
Determine what the passage rules on: the four rak'ahs before Isha. Identify the hukm level according to the Hanafi school.
The passage states it is 'mukhayyar' (optional) and 'hasan' (good).
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the primary evidence: the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's practice of praying four before Isha, four after, then lying down.
The dalil is a hadith (āḥād).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The Prophet's action shows it is legislated, but the lack of persistence (muwāẓabah) lowers it from muakkadah to mandūb.
The key is the absence of consistent practice, not the hadith itself.
4
Note the Clarification from Later Works
Understand how Al-Muhit and Miraj al-Diraya confirm the ruling: the four before Isha are not among the rawatib, as Imam Muhammad did not list them in Al-Asl.
This is an expansion of the original proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعده، وست بعد المغرب.. عائشة و أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كَانَ يُصَلِّي قَبْلَ العِشَاءِ أَرْبَعَاً، ثمَّ يُصَلِّي بَعْدَهَا أَرْبَعَاً ثم يَضْطَجِعُ انتهى. وذكر في المحيط : إن تطوع قبل العصر بأربع، وقبل العشاء بأربع فحسن؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يواظب عليها، انتهى. وفي معراج الدراية : والأربع قبل العشاء مخير فيها، بدليل أن محمداً سماه في الأصل حسناً، ولم يذكرها من السنن الرواتب. انتهى. فمن قال أنه لم يذكر في خصوص الأربع قبل العشاء حديث لعله لم يطلع على ما قاله صاحب الاختيار، وما ذكرناه أيضاً،
And after it, and six after Maghrib... Aisha that he (peace be upon him) used to pray before Isha four, then after it four, then lie down. End. And it is mentioned in Al-Muhit: If one prays voluntary before Asr four, and before Isha four, it is good, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not persist on them. End. And in Miraj al-Diraya: The four before Isha are optional, evidenced by Muhammad calling them good in Al-Asl, and not mentioning them among the regular sunnahs. End. So whoever says that no hadith is mentioned specifically about the four before Isha, perhaps he has not seen what the author of Al-Ikhtiyar said, and what we also mentioned.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling for four rak'ahs before Isha. The author quotes the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet used to pray four before Isha and four after, then lie down. However, this is not a confirmed sunnah (muakkadah) because the Prophet did not persistently perform it. The text from Al-Muhit states that it is 'good' (hasan) to pray four before Asr and before Isha, but not obligatory. From Miraj al-Diraya, it is clarified that the four before Isha are optional (mukhayyar), as Imam Muhammad called them 'good' in Al-Asl and did not include them among the regular sunnahs (al-sunan al-rawatib). Therefore, the ruling is that it is recommended (mandub) but not a stressed sunnah. The passage also responds to a potential objection that no specific hadith exists for these four, citing that the author of Al-Ikhtiyar did mention it.

Key Terms
مخير (mukhayyar): Optional; the worshiper may choose to pray it or leave it without sin.
السنن الرواتب (al-sunan al-rawatib): The confirmed regular sunnah prayers that the Prophet consistently performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the four rak'ahs before Isha NOT considered a muakkadah sunnah?
A) Because the hadith of Aisha is weak.
B) Because the Prophet did not persist on them.
C) Because they are fard instead.
D) Because they are not mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The four rak'ahs before Isha are recommended (mandub) but not a confirmed sunnah, as the Prophet's practice lacked persistence and Imam Muhammad did not include them among the rawatib.
