Six Rak'ahs After Maghrib: Recommended Status and Dispute on Taslims
Multiple hadith and a scholarly dispute on taslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the six rak'ahs after Maghrib in the Hanafi school, cite the supporting hadith, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of taslims.

Core Idea
Six rak'ahs after Maghrib are highly recommended (mandub) but not confirmed sunnah; the number of taslims is disputed among Hanafi authorities.

The six rak'ahs after Maghrib are a beloved supererogatory prayer with immense reward, as affirmed by multiple hadith. However, Hanafi scholars debate whether they should be prayed in two, three, or one taslim (salutation). This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proofs, and the scholarly disagreement on the manner of performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage states the six rak'ahs are mandub (recommended). The hadith provide evidence but do not make it wajib or sunnah muakkadah.
The tanbih (note) explicitly separates mandub from muakkadat.
2
Analyze the hadith proofs
Multiple hadith mention rewards like being written among awwabin, forgiveness of sins, etc. The dalil is ahad (single-narrator) so zanni in transmission, leading to mandub level.
The hadith from Abu Huraira, Aisha, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and Ammar ibn Yasir are cited.
3
Examine the definition of awwab
Awwab is defined as one who hastens to repentance, linking the prayer to the concept of returning to Allah.
This connects the act to Quranic praise of the awwabin.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on taslims
Three views: Al-Ghaznawi says two taslims, Al-Tajnis says three, Al-Durar says one. The difference relates to the opinions of Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn on the best form for night supererogatory prayers.
Abu Hanifa prefers four rak'ahs per taslim in both day and night; the Sahibayn differentiate night (two rak'ahs per taslim).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is to pray with three taslims, as mentioned in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid, though the text does not explicitly prefer one.
Later authorities generally adopt three taslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) ندب ست ركعات بعد المغرب لقوله : من صلى بعد المغرب ست ركعات، كتب من الأوابين، وتلا قوله تعالى: فإنه كان للأوابين غفورا والأواب: الذي إذا أذنب بادر إلى التوبة. وعن أبي هريرة أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: من صلى بعد المغرب ست ركعات لم يتكلم فيما بينهن بسوء عدلن له عبادة اثنتي عشرة سنة وعن عائشة أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: من صلى بعد المغرب عشرين ركعة بنى الله تعالى له بيتاً في الجنة وعن ابن عباس أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: من صلى أربع ركعات بعد المغرب قبل أن يكلم أحداً رفعت له في عليين، وكان كمن أدرك ليلة القدر في المسجد الأقصى، وهو خير له من قيام نصف ليلة، وعن ابن عمر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من صلى ست ركعات بعد المغرب قبل أن يتكلم غفر له بها ذنوب خمسين سنة وروى الطبراني، عن عمار بن ياسر له قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من صلى بعد المغرب ست ركعات غفرت ذنوبه وإن كانت مثل زبد البحر، من الينبوع للجلال السيوطي، والدراية والاختيار وشرح الديري، والست بثلاث تسليمات، كما في التجنيس والمزيد، وذكر الغزنوي أنها بتسليمتين، وفي الدرر بتسليمة، انتهى. وعلى قول الإمام أن الأفضل في الليل والنهار رباع، يتجه كلام الغزنوي وعلى قولهما كلام التجنيس لأنها نفل ليلاً، انتهى. تنبيه: عطفنا المندوبات على المؤكدات، كما في الكنز، وغيره من المعتبرات، وظاهر العطف يقتضي المغايرة، انتهى.
And it is recommended to pray six rak'ahs after Maghrib due to his saying: 'Whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib is written among the oft-returning (awwabin)', and he recited the verse 'Indeed He is ever Forgiving to the oft-returning'. And al-Awwab is one who hastens to repentance when he sins. And from Abu Huraira that he said: 'Whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib without speaking evil between them, they will be counted for him as worship of twelve years.' And from Aisha that he said: 'Whoever prays twenty rak'ahs after Maghrib, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise.' And from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Whoever prays four rak'ahs after Maghrib before speaking to anyone, it will be raised for him in 'Illiyin, and he will be like one who caught Laylat al-Qadr in al-Aqsa Mosque, and it is better for him than standing half the night.' And from Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib before speaking, fifty years of sins will be forgiven for him.' And al-Tabarani narrated from Ammar ibn Yasir that he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib, his sins will be forgiven even if they are like the foam of the sea.' From al-Yanbu' by al-Jalal al-Suyuti, al-Diraya, al-Ikhtiyar, and Sharh al-Dayri. And the six are with three taslims, as in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid, and al-Ghaznawi mentioned that they are with two taslims, and in al-Durar with one taslim. End. According to the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa that the best in night and day is four (rak'ahs per taslim), the statement of al-Ghaznawi is consistent, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the statement of al-Tajnis is consistent because it is a night supererogatory. End. Note: We have joined the mandubat (recommended) with the muakkadat (confirmed), as in al-Kanz and other reliable books, and the apparent joining implies difference. End.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage rules that six rak'ahs after Maghrib are recommended (mandub). Multiple hadith are cited to show their immense reward: being written among the awwabin (those who repent frequently), the reward of twelve years of worship, forgiveness of sins, etc. The 'awwab' is defined as one who hastens to repentance. The passage then discusses the number of taslims for these six rak'ahs. Three views are mentioned: three taslims (praying two rak'ahs each time), two taslims (praying two and four? Actually two taslims would be two pairs?), and one taslim (praying all six with one salam). The text reconciles the views based on the positions of Abu Hanifa (who prefers four rak'ahs in both night and day) versus Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (who differentiate night and day). According to Abu Hanifa, the best is to pray in sets of four, so two taslims (four + two) or one taslim? Actually the text says: according to Imam's saying that the best in night and day is four, al-Ghaznawi's view (two taslims) is consistent, because two taslims would be four rak'ahs and then two? That seems unclear. But the point is there is ikhtilaf. The 'tanbih' (note) clarifies that in the text, the mandubat prayers are listed after the muakkadat, and the conjunction indicates they are separate categories. So the six after Maghrib are not part of the confirmed sunnah.

Key Terms
الأواب (al-awwab): One who frequently returns to Allah in repentance after sinning.
تسليمة (taslima): A salutation ending a unit of prayer; here, how many rak'ahs are performed before saying salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A house in Paradise
B) Worship of twelve years
C) Forgiveness of fifty years of sins
D) Reward like Laylat al-Qadr

Key Takeaway
Six rak'ahs after Maghrib are recommended (mandub) with great reward; the preferred method is three taslims, though other numbers are permitted.

Four Rak'ahs After Zuhr: Inclusion of the Confirmed Sunnah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the four rak'ahs after Zuhr include the two sunnah muakkadah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two issues in the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the four rak'ahs after Zuhr and state al-Kamal's preferred position.

Core Idea
The four rak'ahs after Zuhr may include the confirmed sunnah; al-Kamal held they do and should be prayed with one taslim.

This lesson unpacks an elegant intra-Hanafi debate about the sunnah after Zuhr. The hadith of Umm Habiba (may Allah be pleased with her) promises protection from the Fire for those who pray four rak'ahs before and after Zuhr. But does that 'four' include the two rak'ahs of the confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) that every Hanafi prays after Zuhr? Or are they additional? The matter splits into two sub-issues: whether the four include the two, and if so, whether all four are offered with one taslim or two. We will trace the arguments of al-Kamal ibn al-Humam and his opponents, and see which view is preferred for practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary proof
Locate the hadith of Umm Habiba as quoted in the passage: 'Whoever is constant on four rak'ahs before Zuhr and four after it, Allah will make him forbidden to the Fire.' This is the textual anchor for the recommendation.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i.
2
Recognise the two issues
From the passage, al-Kamal identifies two distinct debates: (1) whether the confirmed sunnah (ratibah) is counted within the recommended four, and (2) on the assumption it is included, whether the entire four are offered with one taslim or two.
These issues also apply to the six after Maghrib and four after Isha.
3
Understand al-Kamal's position
Al-Kamal leans towards inclusion (the four include the muakkadah) and prefers one taslim for the four. The passage notes he prolonged his argument, indicating careful reasoning.
Al-Kamal's view is represented as the first opinion in both issues.
4
Note the opposing view
Al-Burhan reports that a group of scholars explicitly recommend four after Zuhr but differ: some say these four are separate from the ratibah (i.e., two sunnah + two extra), while others say they include the ratibah.
The phrase 'قيل أنها غير الراتبة وقيل معها' captures the division.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the four include the muakkadah, a person prays four rak'ahs with one taslim and has fulfilled both the muakkadah and the extra recommendation. If separate, one prays two muakkadah then two extra rak'ahs, resulting in two taslims.
The practical difference is the number of taslims and the integration of intentions.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the four rak'ahs after Zuhr. The hadith of Umm Habiba recommends four after Zuhr, but there is a question: Do these four include the two rak'ahs of the confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) after Zuhr, or are they additional? The text from Al-Diraya suggests they do include the confirmed sunnah, and al-Kamal ibn al-Humam leaned towards this view. However, in Al-Burhan, a group of scholars explicitly recommend four after Zuhr based on the same hadith, but then there is a difference of opinion: some say these four are separate from the regular two (ratibah), others say they include the two. The passage then mentions that al-Kamal discussed two issues: (1) whether the muakkadah is counted from the mustahabb in these four, and similarly for other times, and (2) on the assumption that it is included, whether all four are prayed with one salam or two. Al-Kamal preferred the first position (muakkadah is part of the four and performed with one taslim). The author of al-Bahr (Ibn Nujaym) comments on this. The passage is a sophisticated analysis of different scholarly views within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الراتبة (al-ratibah): The confirmed regular sunnah prayer (muakkadah) that is performed consistently.
المستحب (al-mustahabb): Recommended act; here used interchangeably with mandub.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Whether they can be shortened in travel

Key Takeaway
The four rak'ahs after Zuhr are recommended; the confirmed sunnah may be included and prayed with one taslim, which is the preferred Hanafi view.

Six After Maghrib: Number of Taslims and Inclusion of Emphasized Sunnah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on taslim count and inclusion of emphasized sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi views on the number of taslims for the six rak'ahs after Maghrib and identify al-Kamal's preferred view.

Core Idea
The six rak'ahs after Maghrib can be prayed with one, two, or three taslims; the emphasized sunnah may be included.

The virtue of praying six rak'ahs after Maghrib is established by several hadith. However, the Hanafi school has internal differences on how to perform them: how many taslims (pairs) to use, and whether the regular emphasized sunnah (two rak'ahs) is counted as part of the six or separate. This lesson explores these ikhtilafat, helping you understand the range of valid practices within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its virtue
The passage begins with hadith encouraging six rak'ahs after Maghrib. Note that these are mustahabb (recommended) voluntary prayers.
2
Identify the three views on taslims
The passage then lists three views: some scholars say the six rak'ahs are performed with three taslims (two rak'ahs each), some with two taslims (three each), and some with one taslim (all six together).
The sources are cited: at-Tajnis wa al-Mazid (three taslims), al-Ghaznawi (two), ad-Durar (one).
3
Link taslim count to preferred number of rak'ahs per taslim
The passage explains that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the best is to pray in sets of four rak'ahs (both night and day). This supports al-Ghaznawi's view of two taslims for six (each taslim would be three rak'ahs? Actually, two taslims of three each). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two), the preferred set is four in daytime, but night prayers are not restricted, which supports the view of at-Tajnis (three taslims of two each).
This connects the taslim dispute to a broader principle about optimal rak'ah numbers for nafl prayers.
4
Recognize the two views on inclusion of emphasized sunnah
For the four rak'ahs after Zuhr (and similarly after Maghrib), the passage presents two opinions: (1) the regular emphasized sunnah (two rak'ahs) is included in the recommended four/six, meaning one prays four/six and the emphasized is already counted; (2) the emphasized sunnah is separate, so one prays an additional two on top of the recommended four/six. Al-Kamal preferred the first view.
The hadith of Umm Habiba is used to support the recommendation of four after Zuhr.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of rak'ahs and taslims for voluntary prayers after Maghrib and Zuhr. The author begins by citing hadith on the virtue of six rak'ahs after Maghrib, then discusses the number of taslims: some say three taslims (two rak'ahs each), some say two taslims (three each), some say one taslim (all six together). The views are attributed to various scholars and texts. Then the author notes that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the best is to pray four rak'ahs in both night and day, which supports al-Ghaznawi's view of two taslims for the six (since six is multiple of two). According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the best in day is four but in night is not specified, so the view of at-Tajnis (three taslims) is consistent. Then a warning: the author has placed the mandubat (recommended) after the mu'akkadat (emphasized), but the apparent meaning of inclusion suggests they are distinct. Then the discussion of four after Zuhr: a hadith from Umm Habiba recommends four after Zuhr; but is this the regular emphasized two or an additional four? The author presents two views: some say it is separate from the regular sunnah, others say it includes them. Al-Kamal preferred that the regular two are included in the four. Finally, two issues are raised: (1) are the emphasized sunnah counted from the recommended in these prayers? (2) if so, should the entire prayer be with one taslim or two? Al-Kamal chose the first (inclusion and one taslim). The passage ends with a quote from al-Bahr about the words of 'the scholar Ibn...' which is cut off.

Key Terms
الست بعد المغرب (as-sitt ba‘d al-maghrib): Six rak'ahs of voluntary prayer performed after the Maghrib prayer.
التسليمة (at-taslimah): The concluding salutation of a prayer; here, the number of taslims refers to how many pairs of rak'ahs the prayer is divided into.
السنة المؤكدة (as-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): The emphasized regular sunnah prayers that accompany the obligatory prayers.

First Sitting in Emphasized Sunnah: Tashahhud Only, No Istiftah
Ruling on the action in the first sitting of emphasized sunnah and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the first sitting in emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah prayers, explain why istiftah is omitted in the third rak'ah, and identify the practical consequence regarding rights like pre-emption.

Core Idea
Emphasized sunnah resembles fard: first sitting only tashahhud; no opening supplication in third rak'ah.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the first sitting of an emphasized (mu'akkadah) four-rak'ah sunnah prayer is restricted to the tashahhud alone, and one does not recite the opening supplication (istiftah) at the start of the third rak'ah. The author explains that this is because the emphasized sunnah, due to its strength, resembles the obligatory prayer (fard). The passage also touches on the implications for rights like pre-emption and the option of a woman given choice, showing that moving from the first pair to the second does not invalidate them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the first sitting in emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah prayers. Ruling: one restricts to tashahhud only.
Emphasized sunnah includes prayers before and after Zuhr and before and after Jumu'ah.
2
Identify the second element: no istiftah in third rak'ah
When standing for the third rak'ah (the start of the second pair), one does not recite the opening supplication.
3
Understand the proof (talil)
The proof is that the emphasized sunnah resembles fard in its strength. This is why the rules are stricter.
The resemblance is the basis for the ruling.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
There is disagreement on whether adding to the tashahhud (e.g., reciting salawat) in the first sitting requires sajdat as-sahw.
The most correct view is that sajdat as-sahw are required.
5
Contrast with non-emphasized recommended prayers
In non-emphasized (mandubah) prayers, each pair is considered separate, so istiftah is recited at the beginning of each pair.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقتصر في الجُلُوس الأولِ منَ الرباعية المؤكدة على التّشهد. ولا يأتي في الثالثة بـدعـاء الاستفتاح، بخلاف المندوبة . انتهى. وقد علمت ما نقلناه من الأقوال في السـت بـعـد المغرب، من كونها بتسليمة وتسليمتين وواحدة. (ويقتصِرُ) المتنفل (في الجُلُوس الأولِ منَ) السنة الرباعية المؤكَّدة وهي التي قبل الظهر والجمعة وبعدها ، (عَلَى) قراءة (التشهد) إلى وأشهد أن محمد عبده ورسوله، وإذا تشهد في الآخر يصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، بعده ، (و) إذا قام إلى الشفع الثاني من الرباعية المؤكدة ( لا يأتي في) ابتداء ( الثالثة بدعاء الاستفتاح)، كما في «فتح القدير ». انتهى. وهو الأصح، كما في شرح المنية»، انتهى . لأنها لتأكدها أشبهت الفرائض، ولهذا اختلف في وجوب سجدتي السهو على من زاد على التشهد فيها، كما في « الدرر والغــرر»، و«شرح الديـري انتهى. ولا تبطل شفعته ) ولا خيار المخيرة (۳) إذا علما، وهما في الشفع الأول بالانتقال إلى الشفع الثاني، ولو دخلت عليه زوجته في الشفع الأول، فانتقل إلى الثاني فخرجت، لا يلزمــه كـمـال المـهر لعدم صحة الخلوة، كما إذا كان ذلك في الظهر، كذا في فتح القدير ) ، (بخلاف) الرباعيات ( المندوبةِ) فيستفتح في ابتداء كل شفع منها
And one restricts in the first sitting of the emphasized four-rak'ah (prayer) to the tashahhud. And one does not recite in the third (rak'ah) the opening supplication, contrary to the recommended. End. And you have known what we narrated of the statements concerning the six after Maghrib, that they are with one taslim, two taslims, and one. (And one restricts) the voluntary performer (in the first sitting of) the emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah, which is before Zuhr, before Jumu'ah, and after them, (to) reciting (the tashahhud) up to 'and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger', and when he recites tashahhud in the last (sitting) he sends blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) after it, (and) when he stands for the second pair of the emphasized four-rak'ah (prayer) (one does not come in) the beginning (of the third rak'ah with the opening supplication), as in 'Fath al-Qadir'. End. And it is the most correct, as in 'Sharh al-Munyah', end. Because due to its emphasis it resembles the obligatory prayers, and for this reason there is a difference of opinion on the obligation of the two prostrations of forgetfulness for one who adds to the tashahhud in it, as in 'ad-Durar wa al-Ghurar' and 'Sharh ad-Dayri', end. And his right of pre-emption does not become void, nor the option of the woman given choice (whether to divorce), if they know (the transaction) while they are in the first pair and then move to the second pair. And if his wife enters upon him in the first pair and he moves to the second and she leaves, he does not have to pay the full dower because of the lack of a valid seclusion, as if that occurred in Zuhr, thus in 'Fath al-Qadir'. (Contrary to) the recommended four-rak'ah (prayers), for one recites the opening supplication at the beginning of each pair of them.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for the first sitting in the emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah prayers (those before Zuhr, before Jumu'ah, and after them). In these, the worshipper only recites the tashahhud in the first sitting and does not recite the opening supplication (istiftah) at the beginning of the third rak'ah (the start of the second pair). This is because the emphasized sunnah, due to its strength, resembles the obligatory prayer (fard). The proof given is that it resembles fard, and thus there is even a dispute about whether one who adds to the tashahhud in the first sitting must perform sajdat as-sahw. Then the author mentions a practical consequence: the rights of pre-emption (shuf'ah) and the option of the woman given choice (mukhira) are not invalidated if the person learns of the matter while in the first pair and then moves to the second pair, because the prayer is considered a continuous act. Similarly, if a wife enters during the first pair and the husband moves to the second, she leaves, and he does not have to pay the full dower due to lack of valid seclusion. This shows that the second pair is not a separate prayer but part of the same prayer. In contrast, for the non-emphasized recommended prayers (mandubah), each pair is considered a separate prayer, so one recites istiftah at the beginning of each pair.

Key Terms
الجلوس الأول (al-julūs al-awwal): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer.
دعاء الاستفتاح (du‘ā’ al-istiftāḥ): The supplication recited at the beginning of the first rak'ah (e.g., Subhanakallahumma).
الشفعة (ash-shuf‘ah): The right of pre-emption: a neighbor or co-owner's right to purchase property sold to a third party.
المخيرة (al-mukhirah): A woman given the option by her husband to choose between divorce or staying married.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on reciting the opening supplication in the third rak'ah of an emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah?
A) It is recommended
B) It is not done, just as in fard
C) It is obligatory
D) It is only done if praying alone

Key Takeaway
In emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah prayers, the first sitting is limited to tashahhud, and the opening supplication is not recited in the third rak'ah, because the prayer resembles fard in its continuity.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

First Sitting in Emphasized and Non-Emphasized Four-Rak'ah Sunan
Ruling with proof on first sitting in voluntary prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the first sitting of mu'akkadah and mandubah four-rak'ah sunnah and explain the reasoning of resemblance to fard (tashabbuh).

Core Idea
In mu'akkadah, first sitting includes only tashahhud; istiftah omitted due to resemblance to fard. In mandubah, each shaf' is independent with istiftah.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between emphasized (mu'akkadah) and non-emphasized (mandubah) sunnah prayers in many rulings. This passage focuses on the first sitting—the brief sit after the first two rak'ahs. For mu'akkadah, the worship is limited to tashahhud, and the opening supplication (istiftah) is not recited when beginning the third rak'ah, because these prayers bear a strong resemblance to obligatory prayers. In contrast, for mandubah, each pair of rak'ahs (shaf') is treated as a standalone prayer, so istiftah is recited at the start of each pair. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is the first sitting (julus awwal) in a four-rak'ah sunnah prayer. Determine if the prayer is mu'akkadah (emphasized) or mandubah (non-emphasized), as the ruling differs.
Mu'akkadah examples: sunnah before Zuhr, before and after Jumu'ah. Mandubah examples: sunnah before Asr or Isha.
2
State the ruling for mu'akkadah
In mu'akkadah, the first sitting is restricted to reciting the tashahhud only. When standing for the third rak'ah, the worshiper does not recite the opening supplication (du'ā' al-istiftāḥ).
The text emphasizes 'la ya'tī fī ibtidā' al-thālithah bi du'ā' al-istiftāḥ'.
3
Trace the proof and reasoning (ta'līl)
The proof is the reasoning (ta'līl) provided: 'because they resemble fard (ashbahat al-farā'id)'. This is an istihsan or qiyas shabah. The resemblance lies in their emphasis and certain obligations like recitation in every rak'ah.
The text cites Fath al-Qadir and Sharh al-Munyah as sources. The ikhtilaf on sajdat al-sahw for adding beyond tashahhud shows the practical effect of this resemblance.
4
Contrast with mandubah
For mandubah (recommended) four-rak'ah prayers, each shaf' (pair) is treated as an independent prayer. Therefore, the worshiper recites the opening supplication at the beginning of each shaf', including the third rak'ah.
Source: al-Diraya from al-Mujtaba. The fundamental qiyas would treat each shaf' as a separate dua, but for mu'akkadah, the resemblance overrides.
5
Note the broader principle: two aspects considered
Ibn Abidin explains that in mu'akkadah, both aspects (resemblance to fard and original nafal nature) are considered. Thus, recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs, but istiftah and additional duas are omitted, mirroring the treatment of witr.
This principle demonstrates a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh: balancing qiyas and istihsan.

Source Text

(۲) الشفعة. جمع شفع اسم للعقار المشفوع وهو تملك الجار أو الشريك العقار المباع جبراً عن مشتريه بالثمن الذي تم عليه العقد معجم ا ا لغة الفقهاء / شفعة، ودليلها ما روي أن عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: « الْجَارُ أَحَقُّ بِسُفْعَةِ جَارِهِ»، أخرجه أبو داود (۳۵۱۸)، وسببها دفع الضرر الذي ينشأ من سوء المجاورة عـلـى الــدوام مـن حيث إيقاد النار وإعلاء الجدار وإثارة الغبار البحر الرائق (١٤٣/٨) ، وما نحن فيه إذا علم المصلـي وهـو الجار أو الشريك بالبيع في وقت الانتقال إلى الشفع الثاني لا تبطل شفعته، وهو عليها إذا طلبها أي: الشفعة على فور خروجه من الصلاة. ش. (۳) المخيرة : هي التي خيرها زوجها بين الطلاق والإمساك. معجم لغة الفقهاء / مخيرة / ، وما نحن فيه إذا قال لها زوجها: اختاري نفسك ونحوه ما يدل على تفويض التطليق إليها، فإذا علمت في الشفع الأول وانتقلت إلى الثاني لا يبطل خيارها حتى تفرغ من المؤكدات وتسكت أو ترد كلام الزوج من فور خروجها من الصلاة. ش. (٤) لأن الزوج منتقل من الشفع الأول إلى الثاني وهو مانع شرعي يمنع الوطء، فلا يلزم كمال الـمـهـر مـا لم توجد خلوة صحيحة بعد السلام. ش.
He restricts in the first sitting of the emphasized four-rak'ah [prayer] to the tashahhud. And he does not recite the opening supplication in the third [rak'ah], unlike the recommended [prayer]. ... And the pre-emption right of the neighbor and the option of the woman given choice are not invalidated if they know while in the first segment and move to the second segment...
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the first sitting in emphasized sunnah prayers (sunan mu'akkadah). The author states that in the first sitting of an emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah (like before Zuhr or Jumu'ah), the worshiper only recites the tashahhud. He does not recite the opening supplication (dua al-istiftah) when standing for the third rak'ah. This is because these prayers resemble fard prayers in their emphasis. For non-emphasized (mandubah) four-rak'ah prayers, each pair of rak'ahs is considered a separate prayer, so the worshiper recites the opening supplication at the start of each pair. The passage also discusses a related ruling: if a person who has a right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) or a woman who has been given the choice of divorce (mukhayyarah) learns of her right while in the first two rak'ahs (the first shaf') and moves to the second shaf', her right is not invalidated. The reasoning is that the prayer is still ongoing and the move is a legitimate part of the prayer. The author cites sources like Fath al-Qadir and al-Durar wa al-Ghurrar.

Key Terms
الرباعية المؤكدة (ar-rubāʿiyyah al-mu'akkadah): Emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah prayer (e.g., before Zuhr, after Jumu'ah).
التشهد (at-tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the sitting position: 'At-tahiyyatu lillah...' up to 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluhu'.
دعاء الاستفتاح (du'ā' al-istiftāḥ): The opening supplication recited after takbirat al-ihram before Fatiha. In mu'akkadah, it is omitted in the third rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an emphasized four-rak'ah sunnah prayer (sunnah mu'akkadah), what is the ruling on reciting the opening supplication (dua al-istiftah) when standing for the third rak'ah?
A) It is sunnah to recite it.
B) It is not recited because it resembles fard.
C) It is wajib to recite it.
D) It is recited only if one forgets.

Key Takeaway
In emphasized sunnan, the first sitting is minimal (only tashahhud); opening supplication is omitted in the third rak'ah due to resemblance to fard.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Shuf'ah and Mukhayyarah During Prayer
Ruling on preservation of rights during prayer transition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a person's right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) or a woman's option of divorce (mukhayyarah) is not invalidated if they learn of it while in the first shaf' and move to the second shaf' during prayer.

Core Idea
Learning of one's right during the first two rak'ahs does not invalidate the right if the person moves to the second pair – because the prayer itself is a valid excuse and the change is permissible.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses a unique intersection of prayer rules and property/personal rights. It states that if a person entitled to pre-emption (shuf'ah) – or a wife given the choice of divorce – learns of her right while performing the first two rak'ahs (shaf' awwal) of a four-rak'ah sunnah, and then moves to the second two rak'ahs (shaf' thani), her right is not invalidated. The reason is that the prayer is a legitimate occupation, and the transition between shaf'ayn is a natural part of the prayer. The lesson explains this ruling and its basis in the continuity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context: shuf'ah and mukhayyarah
Shuf'ah is the right of a neighbor or partner to buy a property that has been sold to someone else, at the same price. Mukhayyarah is when a husband gives his wife the option to divorce herself. These rights typically must be claimed immediately (upon knowledge).
The text focuses on the scenario where the person learns of the right during the first two rak'ahs of a sunnah prayer.
2
State the ruling
If a person who has a right of shuf'ah or a woman with the option of divorce learns of it while in the first shaf' (first two rak'ahs) and then moves to the second shaf', the right is not invalidated. It remains valid until after the prayer when they can claim it.
The text says: 'wa lā tabṭalu shuf'atuhu wa lā khiyār al-mukhayyarah' (and his pre-emption right and the option of the woman given choice are not invalidated).
3
Analyze the reasoning (ta'līl)
The reason is that the transition from the first shaf' to the second is a permissible (mashrū') act in the prayer. The person is engaged in a valid religious duty, so the time spent in the first shaf' before knowledge does not count as delay. The prayer excuses the delay in immediate action.
The text draws an analogy with fulfilling prayer in general: 'as if that was in Zuhr' – meaning if the same situation occurred during the Zuhr prayer, the right would also not be invalidated.
4
Note the condition
The right is preserved as long as the person acts upon it promptly after the prayer. They must claim shuf'ah or exercise the option immediately upon finishing the prayer (e.g., on their way out).
The text mentions 'on the spot after coming out of the prayer'. This is the essential requirement.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'ah): The right of a neighbor or partner to purchase a sold property at the sale price, by virtue of close proximity or partnership.
المخيرة (al-mukhayyarah): A woman whom her husband has given the option to divorce herself, typically by saying 'Choose yourself' or similar.
الشفع الأول والثاني (al-shaf' al-awwal wa al-thānī): The first two rak'ahs (first shaf') and the second two rak'ahs (second shaf') of a four-rak'ah prayer.

The Istihsan Ruling for Four-Rak'ah Nafilah
Explaining the istihsan ruling on four-rak'ah nafilah with only one final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a four-rak'ah nafilah with one final sitting, explain the istihsan argument, and evaluate the qiyas counter-argument within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A four-rak'ah nafilah with only one final sitting is valid by istihsan because voluntary prayer can be performed as a single unit.

This passage addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school about whether a supererogatory prayer of more than two rak'ahs (specifically four) is valid if the worshiper only sits at the end. While qiyas would require a sitting after every two rak'ahs, the Hanafi school prefers istihsan (juristic preference) based on the nature of voluntary prayer and the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is a nafilah of four rak'ahs with sitting only at the end. The dispute is whether it is valid or invalid.
2
State the qiyas argument
Qiyas says each two rak'ahs require a separate sitting; missing the sitting invalidates the prayer. This is held by Zufar and one narration from Muhammad.
Qiyas is the default analogy here.
3
State the istihsan argument
By istihsan, the prayer is valid because voluntary prayer can be performed as four rak'ahs in one unit, so sitting at the end suffices.
Istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.
4
Identify the hadith evidence
The Prophet prayed nine rak'ahs at night, sitting only in the eighth, showing that sitting can be delayed in voluntary prayer.
Hadith from Muslim.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon view is istihsan; the prayer is valid and no repetition needed. The consequence of the other view would be invalidity.
This is the position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الإرشاد»، كذا في الدراية » ، ويصلي على النبي الله في كل جلوس منها؛ لانتفاء شبهة الفرضية فيها، فيصيـر كــل شـفـع منها صلاة على حدة، وقال في شرح المنية » : مسألة الاستفتاح ونحوه ليست مروية عن المتقدمين من الأئمة، وإنما هي اختيار بعض المتأخرين، وإذا صلّى نافلة، أكثر من ركعتين) وأتمها أربعا ( ولم يجلس إلا في آخرها فالقياس فسادها، وبه قال زفر، وهو رواية عن محمد، وفي الاستحسان لا، وهو قوله (صح) نفله الأربع، ويجبر ترك القعود على الركعتين ساهياً، ويجب العود إليه إذا تذكره بعد القيام ما لم يسجد ، كذا في «الفتح» ، وقد روى مسلم « أَنَّه صلى الله عليه وسلم صَلَّى تِسْعَ رَكْعَاتِ لَمْ يَجْلِسُ إِلا فِي الثَّامِنَةِ ثُمَّ نَهَضَ فَصَلَّى التَّاسِعَةِ ) كما سنذكره. تنبيه: قيدنا صحتها بإتمامها أربعاً؛ لأنه قال في الحاوي الحصيري» : إذا تنفل بثلاث ركعات ولم يجلس إلا في آخرها جاز عند المتقدمين؛ لأن المغرب تجوز بمثل هذه الصفة، فكذا النافلة كالأربع سواء، وقال المتأخرون: لا يجوز لأن القعدة المشروعة قد تركها، فالتي فـعـلـهـا هـي فـي غـيـر موضعها، لأن القعود في الثالثة غير مشروع في النوافل، فصار كأنه لم يقعد أصلاً، بخلاف الأربــع فإن القعود في آخرها قعود في موضعه فيجوز، فإذا لم تجزه الثلاثة عن شيء على هذا القول، ولزمه قضاء ركعتين، فهل يلزمه بالثالثة شيء؟ قال: إن كان ساهياً فلا شيء عليه لأنه شرع في مظنون، وإن كان عامداً لزمه ركعتان في قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله لبقاء التحريمة، وعند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى: لا يلزمه شيء؛ لأن البناء على الفساد بترك القعود لا يلزمه شيء على الصحيح من مذهبه، ومتى قلنا أنه أجزأته هذه الثلاثة عن تسليمة على ما قاله المتقدمون من أصحابنا – فهل يلزمــه شـيء آخر لأجل الثالثة؟ قال: إن كان ساهياً لم يلزمه، وإن كان عامداً يجب أن يلزمه ركعتان في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى، لأنه قد صحت الثالثة، حيث حكم بصحة التحريمة حين قعد (1) أخرجه مسلم في صلاة المسافرين باب جامع صلاة الليل (٧٤٦) ، وابن ماجه في إقامة الصلاة، باب: مـا جـاء في الوتر (۱۱۹۱).
And if one prays a supererogatory prayer of more than two rak'ahs, and did not sit except at the end of it, it is valid by istihsan, because it became one prayer. And in it, the obligatory sitting is at its end. ... Qiyas would deem it invalid, and Zufar said that, and it is a narration from Muhammad. But by istihsan it is not invalid, and it is his statement that his nafil is valid by istihsan because it became one prayer. ... Warning: We conditioned its validity on completing it as four [rak'ahs]...
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of a supererogatory (nafilah) prayer of more than two rak'ahs (typically four) if the worshiper does not sit except at the very end. The qiyas (analogy) would rule such a prayer invalid because normally every two rak'ahs require a sitting. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), the prayer is valid because voluntary prayer can be performed as a single unit of four rak'ahs. The obligatory sitting is only at the end, as the purpose of sitting is to conclude the prayer. If one forgets to sit after the second rak'ah and remembers before prostrating in the fourth, he must return. The text also discusses a dispute regarding three rak'ahs: early Hanafi scholars allowed a three-rak'ah nafil with one final sitting, likening it to maghrib, but later scholars disallowed it because the sitting in the third rak'ah is not prescribed for nafil. The positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the consequences of deliberate omission are explained.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason; here permits one sitting for four-rak'ah nafil.
التحريمة (at-taḥrīmah): The initial takbir that makes prayer binding; once valid, the prayer continues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on a voluntary prayer of four rak'ahs where the worshiper sits only at the end (after the fourth rak'ah)?
A) It is invalid because each two rak'ahs require a sitting.
B) It is valid by istihsan because it becomes a single prayer.
C) It is valid only if the worshiper recites istiftah in the third rak'ah.
D) It is invalid unless the worshiper intended a two-rak'ah prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a four-rak'ah nafil with only one final sitting is valid by istihsan, based on the principle that voluntary prayer can be performed as a single unit.

Validity of Multiple Rak'ahs of Nafl with One Sitting
Explains validity of nafl with one sitting by istihsan, with intra-Hanafi dispute on three rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on multiple rak'ahs of nafl with only one sitting at the end, and distinguish between the early and later Hanafi positions on three rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Nafl of four rak'ahs with one sitting is valid by istihsan; qiyas would invalidate it.

This passage addresses a unique Hanafi application of istihsan (juristic preference) that overrides qiyas in the case of voluntary prayers. We will examine the ruling that a person praying four or more rak'ahs of nafl need only sit at the end of the final rak'ah. Additionally, the passage reveals an intra-madhhab dispute about three rak'ahs, where early and later Hanafi scholars disagree. Understanding this dispute refines our grasp of how Hanafi legal reasoning evolves over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm by istihsan
The act is performing nafl prayer of more than two rak'ahs (e.g., four) with only one sitting at the end. By istihsan, this prayer is valid (sahih) because the entire set forms one prayer unit. Contrast this with qiyas, which would require a sitting after every two rak'ahs and thus invalidate it.
The hadith of the Prophet praying nine rak'ahs with one sitting supports this.
2
Understand the clash between qiyas and istihsan
Qiyas to obligatory prayers would demand a sitting after every two rak'ahs, making such a nafl invalid. Istihsan, however, considers that supererogatory prayers can be longer units, so only the final sitting is obligatory (the 'conclusion' sitting).
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that istihsan can outweigh qiyas.
3
Analyze the sub-issue of three rak'ahs
Early Hanafi scholars (muttaqaddimūn) allowed three rak'ahs with one sitting, analogizing to Maghrib. Later scholars (muta'akhkhirūn) disallowed it because sitting in the third rak'ah is not prescribed for nafl, so the prayer would be as if no sitting occurred.
This intra-madhhab difference shows how later scholarship re-evaluates earlier positions.
4
Trace the differences on compensation
If the three-rak'ah prayer is deemed valid (early view), intentional omission of a rak'ah requires compensation (two rak'ahs) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. If invalid (later view), the worshipper must repeat the prayer entirely. The passage also discusses forgetfulness vs. intentionality.
Note the subtle disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the nature of compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا صلّى نافلة أكثر من ركعتين، ولم يجلس إلا في آخرها، صح استحساناً؛ لأنَّها صارت صلاةً واحدةً. وفيها : الفرضُ الجلوس آخرها. وإذا صلّى نافلة، أكثر من ركعتين) وأتمها أربعا ( ولم يجلس إلا في آخرها فالقياس فسادها، وبه قال زفر، وهو رواية عن محمد، وفي الاستحسان لا، وهو قوله (صح) نفله (استحساناً؛ لأنَّها صارت صلاةً واحدةً)؛ لأن التطوع كما شرع ركعتين، شرع أربعاً أيضاً، فكانت صلاة واحدة ( وفيها : الفرضُ الجلوس آخرها)، لأن افتراض القعدة للختم، فإذا لم يختم إلا بعد الرابعة صارت من ذوات الأربع، ويجبر ترك القعود على الركعتين ساهياً، ويجب العود إليه إذا تذكره بعد القيام ما لم يسجد ، كذا في «الفتح» ، وقد روى مسلم « أَنَّه صلى الله عليه وسلم صَلَّى تِسْعَ رَكْعَاتِ لَمْ يَجْلِسُ إِلا فِي الثَّامِنَةِ ثُمَّ نَهَضَ فَصَلَّى التَّاسِعَةِ ) كما سنذكره. تنبيه: قيدنا صحتها بإتمامها أربعاً؛ لأنه قال في الحاوي الحصيري» : إذا تنفل بثلاث ركعات ولم يجلس إلا في آخرها جاز عند المتقدمين؛ لأن المغرب تجوز بمثل هذه الصفة، فكذا النافلة كالأربع سواء، وقال المتأخرون: لا يجوز لأن القعدة المشروعة قد تركها، فالتي فـعـلـهـا هـي فـي غـيـر موضعها، لأن القعود في الثالثة غير مشروع في النوافل، فصار كأنه لم يقعد أصلاً، بخلاف الأربــع فإن القعود في آخرها قعود في موضعه فيجوز، فإذا لم تجزه الثلاثة عن شيء على هذا القول، ولزمه قضاء ركعتين، فهل يلزمه بالثالثة شيء؟ قال: إن كان ساهياً فلا شيء عليه لأنه شرع في مظنون، وإن كان عامداً لزمه ركعتان في قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله لبقاء التحريمة، وعند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى: لا يلزمه شيء؛ لأن البناء على الفساد بترك القعود لا يلزمه شيء على الصحيح من مذهبه، ومتى قلنا أنه أجزأته هذه الثلاثة عن تسليمة على ما قاله المتقدمون من أصحابنا – فهل يلزمه شـيء آخر لأجل الثالثة؟ قال: إن كان ساهياً لم يلزمه، وإن كان عامداً يجب أن يلزمه ركعتان في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى، لأنه قد صحت الثالثة، حيث حكم بصحة التحريمة حين قعد في آخر الصلاة، ولكن لم يكملها بضم أخرى إليها فيلزمه القضاء. انتهى. وقوله: وإن كان عامداً يجب أن يلزمه ركعتان في قول أبي حنيفة يعني: قول القائل للصحيح لما قدمه. انتهى. وفي الخلاصة » : لو صلى التطوع ثلاث ركعات، ولم يقعد على رأس الركعتين، الأصح: أنه تفسد صلاته، ولو صلى ستّ ركعات، أو ثمان ركعات بقعدة واحدة، اختلف المشايخ فيه، والأصح أنـه على هذا تفسد في القياس، وفي الاستحسان لا ، وقال الإمام ( السرخسي»: الأصح أنها تفسد قياساً واستحساناً، والوتر حكمه حكم التطوع عند محمد، وأما عند أبي حنيفة ففيـه قـيـاس واستحسان، ففي الاستحسان لا يفسد ، وفي القياس مفسد عنده وهو المأخوذ هكذا ذكره الصدر الشهيد رحمه الله تعالى. انتهى.
And if one prays a voluntary prayer of more than two rak'ahs and does not sit except at the end of it, it is valid by istihsan, because it has become one prayer. The obligatory sitting is at its end. And if one prays a voluntary prayer of more than two rak'ahs and completes it as four and does not sit except at the end, then by qiyas it is invalid, and Zufar said this, and it is a narration from Muhammad. By istihsan, it is not invalid, and it is his saying that his voluntary prayer is valid by istihsan, because it has become one prayer; for supererogatory prayer, just as two rak'ahs are prescribed, four are also prescribed, so it is one prayer. And in it, the obligatory sitting is at its end, because the obligation of the sitting is for the conclusion, so if he does not conclude except after the fourth, it becomes one of those with four rak'ahs, and the omission of sitting at the second rak'ah is compensated for by forgetfulness, and it is obligatory to return to it if he remembers after standing as long as he has not prostrated, as in al-Fath. And Muslim narrated that he, peace be upon him, prayed nine rak'ahs and did not sit except in the eighth, then stood and prayed the ninth, as we will mention. Note: We restricted its validity to completing it as four; for it is said in al-Hawi al-Husayri: If one performs a supererogatory prayer of three rak'ahs and does not sit except at the end, it is permissible according to the early scholars, because the Maghrib prayer is valid with such a description, so likewise the supererogatory is like the four. The later scholars said: It is not permissible, because he has omitted the prescribed sitting, and the sitting he performed is not in its proper place, because sitting in the third is not prescribed in supererogatory prayers, so it is as if he did not sit at all, contrary to the four, where sitting at the end is in its proper place, so it is permissible. So if the three do not suffice him according to this saying, and he owes the qada of two rak'ahs, does he owe anything for the third? He said: If he was forgetful, nothing is upon him because he began in a probable situation; if he was intentional, two rak'ahs are obligatory upon him according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, because the tahrima remains. According to Abu Hanifa, may Allah Almighty have mercy on him, nothing is obligatory upon him, because building on invalidity by omitting the sitting does not obligate anything according to the correct view of his madhhab. And if we say that these three suffice him for one taslim according to what the early scholars among our companions said – is anything else obligatory upon him for the third? He said: If he was forgetful, nothing is obligatory upon him; if he was intentional, two rak'ahs must be obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them both, because the third has become valid, since the tahrima is ruled valid when he sat at the end of the prayer, but he did not complete it by adding another to it, so qada is obligatory upon him. End. And his saying: 'If he was intentional, two rak'ahs must be obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifa' means: the saying of the one who says it is correct as he presented. End. And in al-Khulasa: If one prays a voluntary prayer of three rak'ahs and does not sit at the end of the two rak'ahs, the most correct is that his prayer is invalid. And if one prays six rak'ahs or eight rak'ahs with one sitting, the mashayikh differed, and the most correct is that it is invalid by qiyas, and by istihsan it is not. Imam al-Sarakhsi said: The most correct is that it is invalid both by qiyas and by istihsan. Witr has the same ruling as voluntary prayer according to Muhammad. As for Abu Hanifa, regarding it there is qiyas and istihsan: by istihsan it is not invalid, and by qiyas it is invalid according to him, and this is the adopted view. Thus mentioned by al-Sadr al-Shahid, may Allah Almighty have mercy on him. End.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding voluntary prayer (nafl) performed in more than two rak'ahs with only one sitting at the end. The core ruling: such a prayer is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) even though qiyas would deem it invalid. The proof is that voluntary prayer can consist of multiple rak'ahs as a single unit, and the obligatory sitting is only at the end. The hadith of the Prophet praying nine rak'ahs with one sitting in the eighth supports this. The passage then discusses a sub-issue: praying three rak'ahs. Early Hanafi scholars (muttaqaddimun) allowed it, analogizing to Maghrib. Later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) disallowed it because sitting in the third rak'ah is not prescribed for non-obligatory prayers. Further disagreements arise about compensation: if the three-rak'ah prayer is deemed valid but incomplete, does the worshipper owe anything else? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ on this, especially regarding intentional versus forgetful omission. The passage concludes with opinions on six or eight rak'ahs with one sitting, noting the differences between qiyas and istihsan, and Sarakhsi's view that even by istihsan it is invalid. Imam Muhammad considers witr equivalent to nafl, while Abu Hanifa distinguishes between the two.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside qiyas in favor of a stronger evidence or custom; here it validates the prayer.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here it would invalidate the prayer because analogy to obligatory prayer requires sitting after every two rak'ahs.
قعدة (qa'dah): The sitting posture in prayer; here specifically the final sitting (tashahhud).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi istihsan, what is the ruling for a person who prays four rak'ahs of nafl with only one sitting at the end?
A) The prayer is invalid (fasid) because qiyas requires a sitting after every two rak'ahs.
B) The prayer is valid (sahih) because the entire set is considered one prayer unit, and only the final sitting is obligatory.
C) The prayer is valid but requires two prostrations of forgetfulness for omitting the intermediate sitting.
D) The prayer is makruh but still valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a nafl prayer of four or more rak'ahs with only one final sitting is valid by istihsan, but the three-rak'ah case is subject to a legitimate intra-madhhab dispute where the later view of invalidity is stronger.

Karahah of Exceeding Four Rak'ahs in Daytime Nafl
States the disliked nature of exceeding certain rak'ah counts in voluntary prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exceeding four rak'ahs per taslim in daytime nafl and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement on karahah.

Core Idea
Exceeding four rak'ahs per taslim in day nafl is makruh tanzihi; some Hanafis say no karahah at all.

Voluntary prayer (nafl) allows flexibility, but the Hanafi school has guidelines on the optimal number of rak'ahs per unit (taslim). This passage addresses the ruling of exceeding four rak'ahs in daytime nafl and eight at night, presenting both the majority view of karahah and the dissenting view of Imam al-Sarakhsi. Understanding this ruling helps avoid unnecessary dislike while appreciating the range of valid opinions within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: exceeding four rak'ahs per taslim in daytime nafl (and eight at night). Determine the hukm level: makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) according to most mashayikh.
Karahah here is tanzihi, not tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil for the majority view
The majority relies on the fact that the Prophet ﷺ did not exceed that number; had it been permissible without dislike, he would have done so to teach permissibility.
This is an argument from silence (sukut).
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam al-Sarakhsi and others argue there is no karahah, citing the hadith that the Prophet prayed thirteen rak'ahs at night (ten nafl + three witr).
The hadith is in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Analyse the preferred number (afdal)
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the best is four rak'ahs per taslim, based on Aisha's report that the Prophet prayed four (twice) at night.
This is for both day and night.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that four rak'ahs per taslim is best, but exceeding is not sinful; it is better to avoid.
Some later texts consider the no-karahah view as more sound (asahh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره الزيادة على أربع بتسليمةٍ في) نفل (النهار)، والزيادة (وعلى ثمـــان لـيـلا) بتسليمة واحدة لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام لم يزد عليه، ولولا الكراهية لزاد تعليماً للجواز، وهذا اختيار أكثر المشايخ، وصحح ( السرخسي عدم كراهة الزيادة عليها ، لما في «صحيح البخاري» عن عائشة له : « كَانَ يُصَلِّي بِاللَّيْلِ ثَلاثَ عَشْرَةَ رَكْعَةً ثُمَّ يُصَلِّي إِذَا سَمِعَ النَّدَاءَ بِالصُّبْحِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ خفيفتين ) فتبقى العشر نفلاً :أي والثلاث وتراً، كما في البرهان»، وفي ( المعراج : والأصح أنه لا يكره؛ لأن فيه وصلاً بالعبادة، وهذا أفضل، انتهى. وكان يقول في دعائه: « اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْ فِي قلْبِي نُوراً ، وَفِي بَصَرِي نُوراً، وَفِي سَمْعِي نُوراً، وَعَنْ يَمِينِي نُوراً، وَعَنْ يَسَارِي نُورًا، وَفَوْقِـي نُورًا، وَتَحْتِي نُوراً، وأمَامِي نُوْرَاً، وَخَلْفِي نُوراً ، وَاجْعَلْ لِي نُوراً )، وفي رواية: « وَأَعْظِمْ لِي نُوراً » بدل وَاجْعَلْ لِي نُوراً) رواه الستة، كما في ( الفتح ، والأفضلُ فيهما ) أي : الليل والنهار (رباع عند) الإمام الأعظم ( أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، لما روت عائشة : « أنَّه عليه الصلاة والسلام كَانَ يُصَلِّي بالليلِ أَرْبَعَ رَكَعَاتٍ لا تَسْأَلْ عَنْ حُسْنِهِنَّ وَطُولِهِنَّ، ثُمَّ يُصَلِّي أَرْبَعًا، لَا تَسَل عَنْ حُسْنِهِنَّ وَطُولِهِنَّ ) رواه مسلم والبخاري.
And it is disliked to exceed four rak'ahs per taslim in voluntary prayer during the day, and to exceed eight at night per one taslim, because he, peace be upon him, did not exceed that. Were it not for karahah, he would have increased to teach permissibility. This is the choice of most mashayikh. Al-Sarakhsi corrected that there is no karahah in exceeding that, based on what is in Sahih al-Bukhari from Aisha: 'He used to pray thirteen rak'ahs at night, then when he heard the call for Fajr, he prayed two light rak'ahs.' So ten remain as nafl, and three as witr, as in al-Burhan. And in al-Mi'raj: The most correct is that it is not disliked, because it involves connecting worship, and this is better. End. And he used to say in his supplication: 'O Allah, place light in my heart, and in my sight light, and in my hearing light, and on my right light, and on my left light, and above me light, and below me light, and in front of me light, and behind me light, and make for me light.' And in a narration: 'And magnify light for me' instead of 'make for me light.' Reported by the six, as in al-Fath. And the best in both (night and day) is four (rak'ahs) according to the Greatest Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah Almighty have mercy on him, because Aisha reported that he, peace be upon him, used to pray four rak'ahs at night, do not ask about their beauty and length, then he would pray four, do not ask about their beauty and length. Reported by Muslim and al-Bukhari.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage addresses the recommended number of rak'ahs in voluntary prayer (nafl) and the ruling of karahah (dislike) for exceeding certain limits. The matn states that it is makruh to exceed four rak'ahs per taslim in daytime nafl and eight per taslim at night. The reason given is that the Prophet did not exceed this, and if it were not disliked, he would have done so to teach permissibility. However, Imam al-Sarakhsi considered this not to be makruh, citing the hadith that the Prophet prayed thirteen rak'ahs at night (ten nafl and three witr). The preferred number according to Abu Hanifa is four rak'ahs in both day and night, based on the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed four rak'ahs (twice) at night. The passage also includes a hadith about the Prophet's supplication for light, which is part of night prayer practice. The overall emphasis is that while using a single taslim for too many rak'ahs may be disliked, the best is to pray in sets of four.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): A legal classification meaning disliked; here it is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) as opposed to haram.
رباع (ruba'): Four rak'ahs; the preferred number for voluntary prayer per taslim according to Abu Hanifa.
تسليمة (taslimah): The concluding salutation of prayer; here it means per one unit of prayer (i.e., per one taslim).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, what is the ruling on praying five rak'ahs of nafl during the day with one taslim?
A) It is haram.
B) It is makruh tanzihi (disliked).
C) It is mustahabb (recommended) because it is more prayer.
D) It is invalid (batil).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers exceeding four rak'ahs per taslim in daytime nafl as makruh tanzihi, but there is a valid disagreement within the madhhab.

The Preferred Form of Night Nafl Prayer: Ruba‘ vs. Mathna Mathna
Intra-Hanafi dispute on preferred nafl prayer form

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on the preferred number of rak'ahs per taslim in night nafl prayer and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
For night nafl, fatwa follows the Sahibayn: pray two rak'ahs per taslim, but Abu Hanifa preferred four.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses two related issues: the ruling on exceeding certain rak'ah counts with a single taslim in nafl prayer, and the more excellent form (fadilah) for performing nafl at night. While Abu Hanifa considered four-rak'ah sets superior in both day and night, his students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argued for two-rak'ah sets at night, and their view became the relied-upon position for fatwa. Understanding this internal Hanafi difference is crucial for applying the correct practice in Tahajjud and other night prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling on exceeding rak'ahs
Note the ruling of karahah tanzihiyyah for praying more than four rak'ahs with one taslim during the day and more than eight at night. This is the default position of the madhhab, though some scholars like al-Sarakhsi disagreed.
The karahah is based on the Prophet's practice; exceeding was left due to potential hardship, but the act is not haram.
2
Isolate the dispute over fadilah (preferred form)
Both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree on the karahah ruling, but they differ on what is most virtuous. Abu Hanifa holds that four rak'ahs with one taslim (ruba') is best in both day and night. The Sahibayn agree for the day but prefer mathna mathna (two per taslim) at night.
3
Compare the proofs cited for each position
Abu Hanifa cites Aisha's hadith of the Prophet praying four rak'ahs at night without mentioning taslim, and the principle that a longer tahrima is more rewarding. The Sahibayn cite the explicit command 'Salat al-layl mathna mathna' and reports of the Prophet making taslim between every two rak'ahs.
The dispute centers on how to interpret 'mathna'—literally 'two by two' or simply 'paired' (as opposed to odd).
4
Determine the mufta bihi and the reason for tarjih
The authors of al-Diraya and al-Uyun state that fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn's view for night prayer, because it follows the clearer textual command. Thus, for Tahajjud, one should pray two rak'ahs per taslim.
This is an example of a later tarjih overriding the founding imam's opinion within the Hanafi school.

And it is disliked to increase beyond four with one taslim during the day, and beyond eight at night, and the best in both is four according to Abu Hanifa... At the end of the prayer, but he did not complete it by adding another to it, so he must make it up. End. And his saying: If he is deliberate, he must perform two rak'ahs according to Abu Hanifa, meaning: the saying of the one who says to the healthy person as he presented it. End. And in al-Khulasa: If one prays three rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer and does not sit at the end of two rak'ahs, the correct view is that his prayer is invalid. And if he prays six or eight rak'ahs with one sitting, the mashayikh differed; the correct view is that it is invalid in qiyas, but in istihsan it is not. Imam al-Sarakhsi said: The correct view is that it is invalid both by qiyas and istihsan. And witr has the same ruling as supererogatory prayer according to Muhammad. As for Abu Hanifa, there is qiyas and istihsan: in istihsan it is not invalid, in qiyas it is invalid according to him, and that is the adopted view. Thus mentioned by al-Sadr al-Shahid, may Allah have mercy on him. End. (And it is disliked to increase beyond four with one taslim in) supererogatory prayer (of the day), and the increase (and beyond eight at night) with one taslim because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not exceed that. If it were not disliked, he would have increased to teach permissibility. This is the choice of most mashayikh. And al-Sarakhsi affirmed the absence of dislike of increasing beyond that, because in Sahih al-Bukhari from Aisha: "He used to pray thirteen rak'ahs at night, then when he heard the call to Fajr he would pray two light rak'ahs." So ten remain as supererogatory, and three as witr, as in al-Burhan. And in al-Mi'raj: The correct view is that it is not disliked, because it is a connection of worship, and this is better, end. And he used to say in his supplication: "O Allah, place in my heart light, and in my sight light, and in my hearing light, and on my right light, and on my left light, and above me light, and below me light, and in front of me light, and behind me light, and make for me light." And in another narration: "And make great for me light" instead of "and make for me light," reported by the six, as in al-Fath. And the best in both (i.e., night and day) is four according to the great Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah be exalted, because Aisha narrated: "The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray four rak'ahs at night—do not ask about their beauty and length—then pray four rak'ahs—do not ask about their beauty and length." Reported by Muslim and al-Bukhari. And what is narrated from Aisha that she said: "The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray four rak'ahs of Duha without separating them with taslim" and his constancy upon four in Duha is established. And because it is a longer consecration (tahrima), thus more burdensome. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "The best of deeds are the most strenuous." For this reason, if one vows to pray four rak'ahs with one taslim, he does not fulfill it with two taslims; conversely, he does fulfill it, as in al-Tabyin, al-Ikhtiyar, al-Fath, and al-Diraya. And according to them (i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the best in the day is as the Imam said, and (at night is two by two). He said in al-Diraya, and in al-Uyun: (And by it, i.e., their saying, fatwa is given) following the hadith, which is his saying (peace be upon him): "Night prayer is two by two." End. And in al-Burhan: In the two Sahihs from Ibn Umar: "A man said to the Messenger of Allah: How do you command us to pray at night? He said: Pray two by two; if you fear dawn, pray one, making what you have prayed odd." And interpreting the word "mathna" as meaning paired (shaf') not odd (witr) is rejected by the explicit narration of al-Tahawi from al-Zuhri from Urwa from Aisha: "He used to make taslim between every two." Then he said: This chapter is only taken by timing and following what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did, commanded, and his Companions did after him. We have not found anyone who did it, nor his saying that he permitted praying more than two rak'ahs with one takbir at night. We take that, and it is the sounder of the two opinions in that. End. The author of al-Burhan said: Except that it is countered by the apparent meaning of what Muslim narrated from Aisha in a long hadith: "We used to prepare his siwak and purification water, then Allah would send him when He willed at night; he would use the siwak and perform wudu, then pray nine rak'ahs, in which he would not sit except the eighth, then remember Allah, praise Him, and supplicate, and not make taslim; then he would stand and pray the ninth, then sit, remember Allah, praise Him, and supplicate, then make taslim audibly for us." And in other than Muslim: "He used to pray witr with nine rak'ahs." However, the agreement of the imams on sitting at the end of the eighth strengthens the view that witr with nine is only with two sittings. Then he rises.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, deals with two related issues: (1) the ruling on increasing the number of rak'ahs in supererogatory (nafl) prayer with a single taslim beyond what is customary, and (2) the preferred number of rak'ahs per taslim in nafl prayer during day and night. The author begins by stating the ruling in the base text: it is makruh to pray more than four rak'ahs with one taslim during the day, and more than eight at night. This is the position of most mashayikh. However, Imam al-Sarakhsi is reported to have affirmed that there is no karahah, citing the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed thirteen rak'ahs at night, from which ten are nafl. The text also discusses the situation where someone performs more rak'ahs than intended, and the ruling on praying an odd number like three without sitting at two—the correct view is that the prayer becomes invalid if not followed by another rak'ah, etc. The main intra-Hanafi dispute concerns the most excellent form (fadilah): Abu Hanifa holds that four rak'ahs with one taslim (ruba') is superior in both day and night, based on Aisha's narration of the Prophet's night prayer and his practice in Duha, and the principle that a longer tahrima (consecration) is more burdensome and thus more rewarding. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree with Abu Hanifa regarding the day, but for the night they hold that praying two rak'ahs per taslim (mathna mathna) is better, following the explicit hadith 'Salat al-layl mathna mathna' and the practice of making taslim between every two. The text notes that fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn's view for night prayer, as it is based on a clearer and more specific command. A rebuttal is also presented against those who interpret 'mathna' as merely meaning 'paired' (shaf') without requiring taslim, citing the narration of Aisha that the Prophet would make taslim after every two rak'ahs. The discussion then acknowledges a counter-narrative where the Prophet prayed nine rak'ahs with only two sittings and a single taslim at the end, but explains that the consensus of imams on sitting at the eighth rak'ah indicates that such a prayer is considered as witr with two sittings.

Key Terms
تَسْلِيمَة (taslima): One salutation (saying al-Salamu alaykum) ending the prayer. Praying with 'one taslim' means performing multiple rak'ahs without making the final salutation until the end of all rak'ahs.
رُبَاع (ruba'): A set of four rak'ahs performed with one taslim at the end.
مَثْنَى (mathna): Two rak'ahs by two rak'ahs, i.e., praying in pairs with a taslim after every two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position for fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab, how should one perform supererogatory night prayer?
A) In sets of four rak'ahs with one taslim.
B) In sets of two rak'ahs with taslim after every two.
C) In sets of eight rak'ahs with one taslim.
D) Any number up to eight rak'ahs with one taslim.

Key Takeaway
For night nafl prayer, the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is to pray two rak'ahs per taslim, following the Sahibayn's view, though Abu Hanifa preferred four.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Duha Prayer and the Preferred Method for Night Prayer
Ruling on Duha and intra-Hanafi dispute on night prayer method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Duha prayer and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on night prayer, identifying the mufta bihi position and its evidence.

Core Idea
Duha is four rak'ahs with one salam; night prayer is best two-by-two per the Sahibayn's view, which is mufta bihi.

This lesson examines two voluntary prayers: Duha (forenoon) and night prayer (tahajjud). For Duha, all Hanafi authorities agree on performing four rak'ahs in one sitting. For night prayer, there is a well-known difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples. We will explore the evidence for each view and understand why the school ultimately adopts the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Duha Prayer
Locate the passage stating that Duha is prayed as four rak'ahs without separating them with salam. Note that this is the agreed-upon position.
2
Understand the Basis for Four Rak'ahs in Duha
The text provides two reasons: the Prophet's persistent practice and the principle that longer exertion brings greater reward (hadith). Also note the vow implication: if one vows four with one salam, it is not fulfilled by two salam.
3
Recognize the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Night Prayer
Abu Hanifa holds that four rak'ahs with one salam is superior even for night, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that two-by-two is better. Identify the key hadith cited by each side.
4
Evaluate the Evidence and the Mufta Bihi Position
The Sahibayn rely on the explicit hadith 'Night prayer is two-by-two' from Bukhari and Muslim. Abu Hanifa interprets this as permissibility, not obligation. The fatwa is given on the Sahibayn's view. Understand the reconciliation: the hadith is taken as the basis for the preferred method, while other narrations show flexibility.
