وعندهما: الأفضل في الليل مَثْنَى مَثْنَى. وبه يُفْتَى..
(۱)
يُصَلِّي الضُّحَى أَرْبَعَاً وَلَا يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَهُنَّ بِسَلام ) و ثبت مواظبته على الأربع في الضحى)، ولأنـه أدوم تحريمة، فيكون أكثر مشقة، قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( أفْضَلُ الأعْمَالِ أَجْهَدُهَا » (۳)، ولهذا لو نذر أن يصلي أربعاً بتسليمة، لا يخرج عنه بتسليمتين، وعلى القلب يخرج، كمـا في « التبيين»، و الاختيار»، و«الفتح»، و « الدراية». وعندهما) أي: أبي يوسف ومحمد: (الأفضل) في النهار كما قال الإمام، و ( في الليلِ مَثْنَى مَثْنَى)، قال في « الدراية » ، وفي «العيون»: (وَبِه) أي: بقولهما (يُفْتَى) اتباعاً للحديث وهو قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « صَلاةُ اللَّيْلِ مَثْنَى مَثْنَى ) انتهى. وفي البرهان » : في «الصحيحين عن ابن عمر : « قَالَ رَجُلٌ لِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ: كَيْفَ تَأْمُرُنَا أَنْ نُصَلِّيَ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ؟ قَالَ: يُصَلِّي أَحَدُكُمْ مَثْنَى مَثْنَى ، فَإِذَا خَشِيَ الصُّبْحَ صَلَّى وَاحِدَةً، فَأَوْتَرَتْ لَهُ مَا صَلَّى مِـنْ الليل ). وتأويل لفظ مثنى بـ: شفع لا وتر ،مردود بصريح ما رواه الطحاوي، عن الزهري، عــن عروة، عن عائشة ( أَنَّهُ كَانَ يُسَلِّمُ بَيْنَ كُلِّ اثْنَتَيْنِ ) ثم قال : وهذا الباب إنما يؤخذ مــن جهـة التوقيت والاتباع؛ لما فعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأمر به وفعله أصحابه مِن بَعْدِهِ، فلم نَجِد عنهُ مَنْ فَعَلَهُ، ولا قوله أنه أباح أن يصلي في الليل بتكبيرة أكثر من ركعتين، وبذلك نأخذ وهو أصح القولين في ذلك. انتهى. قال صاحب «البرهان»: إلا أنه يرد عليه ظاهر ما أخرجه مسلم من حديث عائشة في حديث طويل قالت: « كُنَّا نُعِدُّ لَهُ سِوَاكَهُ وَطَهُورَهُ، فَيَبْعَتُهُ اللَّهُ مَا شَاءَ أَنْ يَبْعَثَهُ مِنْ اللَّيْلِ، فَيَتَسَوَّكُ وَيَتَوَضَّأُ، وَيُصَلِّي تِسْعَ رَكَعَاتٍ لا يَجْلِسُ فِيهَا إِلا الثَّامِنَةِ، فَيَذْكُرُ اللَّهَ وَيَحْمَدُهُ، وَيَدْعُوهُ، : وَلا يُسَلِّمُ، ثُمَّ يَقُومُ فَيُصَلِّي التَّاسِعَةَ ثُمَّ يَقْعُدُ فَيَذْكُرُ اللهَ وَيَحْمَدُهُ، وَيَدْعُوهُ، ثُمَّ يُسَلِّمُ تَسْلِيمًا يُسْمِعُنَا " وهو في غير مسلم: «كَانَ يُوْتِرُ بِتِسْعِ رَكَعَاتٍ ) إلا أنَّ اتفاق الأئمة على القـعــود عـلـى (V) ثُمَّ يَنْهَضٌ
(1) أخرجه أبو يعلى في مسنده (۳۳۰/۷). (۲) أخرجه مسلم في صلاة المسافرين باب استحباب الضحی (۷۱۹)، وابن ماجه في إقامة الصلاة، باب ما جاء في صلاة الضحى (۱۳۸۱). (۳) أخرجه ابن خزيمة في صحيحه (٢٦١/٢)، بلفظ: « أدومها». (٤) أخرجه البخاري في الوتر، باب ما جاء في الوتر (۹۹۰) ، ومسلم في صلاة المسافرين باب: صلاة الليل مثنى مثنی (٧٤٩).
(٥) أخرجه مسلم في صلاة المسافرين وقصرها باب صلاة الليل مثنى مثنى والوتر واحدة (٧٤٩)، وابن ماجه في إقامة الصلاة والسنة فيها، باب ما جاء في صلاة الليل ركعتين (۱۳۲۰).
(٦) أخرجه الطحاوي في شرح معاني الآثار (٣٣٦/١). (۷) أخرجه مسلم في صلاة المسافرين باب جامع صلاة الليل (٧٤٦). (۸) أخرجه أبو داود في الصلاة، باب: في صلاة الليل (١٣٥١)، والنسائي في قيام الليل، باب: كيف الوتر بتسع (۱۷۲۰).
- ٤٠٨ -
And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the best in night prayer is two-by-two. And according to it fatwa is given. (1) He prays Duha as four and does not separate between them with salam. And his persistence on four in Duha is established, and because it is longer in tahrīmah, thus it is more strenuous. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The best deeds are the most strenuous' (3). For this reason, if one vows to pray four with one salam, he does not fulfill it by two salam, but the opposite he fulfills, as in al-Tabyīn, al-Ikhtiyār, al-Fatḥ, and al-Dirāyah. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the best in day prayer is as the Imam said, and in night prayer two-by-two. He said in al-Dirāyah and al-‘Uyūn: 'And according to it (i.e., their statement) fatwa is given' following the hadith which is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Night prayer is two-by-two' end. In al-Burhān: In the two Sahihs from Ibn 'Umar: 'A man asked the Messenger of Allah: How do you command us to pray at night? He said: Pray two-by-two, and when you fear the dawn, pray one, making it witr for what you prayed of the night.' And the interpretation of the word 'mathnā' as even (shaf‘) not odd (witr) is rejected by the explicit narration of al-Ṭaḥāwī from al-Zuhrī from ‘Urwa from ‘Ā’ishah: 'He used to make taslīm between every two.' Then he said: This chapter is only taken from timing and following; for what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did and commanded and his Companions did after him, we did not find anyone doing it contrary to that, nor his statement that he permitted praying at night with one takbīr more than two rak‘ahs, and with that we take, and it is the sounder of the two opinions in that. End. The author of al-Burhān said: Except that it is objected by the apparent meaning of what Muslim narrated from ‘Ā’ishah in a long hadith: 'We used to prepare his siwāk and water for purification, then Allah would send him to wake when He willed at night, so he would use siwāk and perform wudu, and pray nine rak‘ahs, not sitting in them except the eighth, so he would remember Allah and praise Him and supplicate, and not make taslīm, then stand and pray the ninth, then sit and remember Allah and praise Him and supplicate, then make taslīm loud enough for us to hear.' And in other than Muslim: 'He used to pray witr with nine rak‘ahs' except that the agreement of the imams upon sitting at the head of each pair, due to what we narrated as evidence for its abrogation, or that it was from his specific qualities. End. I say: The intent of al-Ṭaḥāwī was not the absolute negation of existence, rather the existence of what is not contradictory, restrictive, or abrogated, and what is narrated in Muslim is possible to indicate validity if done, not the recommendation of the act. Hence he said in al-Ikhtiyār: 'Night prayer is two rak‘ahs with one salam, or four, or six, or eight – all of that is narrated in his tahajjud.' End. And the discussion is about clarifying the best. And the investigator Ibn al-Humām answered their evidence: That the wording of the hadith either means 'mathnā' regarding virtue compared to four, or regarding permissibility compared to odd, and preferring one requires a preponderant, and his practice occurred in both ways, but we rationally see the increased virtue of four as it is more strenuous on the soul due to the length of its restriction in the station of service, and we see the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Your reward is according to your exertion.' So we ruled that the second meaning is intended, i.e., permissibility: it is permissible to pray by twos, not one or three. End summary.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, addresses two voluntary prayers: Duha (forenoon) and night prayer (tahajjud). The author first states the matn that one prays Duha as four rak'ahs without separating them with salam. The commentary explains that this is because the Prophet persistently performed four, and because a longer single unit (tahrimah) causes more exertion, which is better according to the hadith 'The best deeds are the most strenuous.' If one vows to pray four rak'ahs with one salam, he must do so; if he prays with two salam (i.e., two sets of two), it does not fulfill the vow. Conversely, if he vows to pray four rak'ahs with two salam, he can do it with one salam as well, since it is more difficult. Then the passage turns to night prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, the best for night prayer is also four with one salam, but according to his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the best is to pray two-by-two (i.e., each pair with a separate salam). The fatwa is given on the students' view because of the explicit hadith 'Night prayer is two-by-two.' The author then delves into a detailed discussion of the evidence, including the hadith from Ibn Umar commanding two-by-two, and a counter-argument from the practice of Aisha describing the Prophet praying nine rak'ahs (eight plus one) with only one taslim at the end. The author reconciles by noting that the hadith about two-by-two indicates permissibility, not obligation, and that the Prophet's practice of praying nine in one sitting is either abrogated or a special characteristic of his. The final ruling is that for night prayer, praying two-by-two is superior according to the mufta bihi view, but one may also pray four, six, or eight with one salam, as all are narrated. The key is that night prayer is prayed in even numbers, and the witr closes it.

Key Terms
ضحى (ḍuḥā): The forenoon, mid-morning; refers to the voluntary prayer performed after sunrise until noon.
مثنى (mathnā): Two-by-two; in pairs; indicates that each two rak'ahs constitute a unit with a separate salam.
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The opening takbīr (Allahu Akbar) that makes the prayer begin; extended metaphorically to the entire prayer session starting with takbīr.
شفع (shaf‘): Even number; in context, it refers to pairs of rak'ahs as opposed to odd (witr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, what is the preferred method for night prayer?
A) Four rak'ahs with one salam throughout the night
B) Two rak'ahs with a salam after every two rak'ahs
C) Single rak'ahs throughout the night
D) Three rak'ahs with one salam for the entire night

Key Takeaway
Duha is prayed as four rak'ahs with one salam; for night prayer, the preferred Hanafi method is two-by-two (mufta bihi), though other methods are valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Superiority of Night Prayer and Its Legal Status
Ruling and proof for night prayer's superiority and legal status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on night prayer (tahajjud) and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement regarding its obligation for the Prophet.

Core Idea
Night prayer is superior and sunnah muakkadah; its exact status for the Prophet was debated.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes night prayer as more virtuous than day prayer, especially in the last third of the night. It then delves into a critical Hanafi legal discussion: was tahajjud obligatory (fard) or voluntary (nafl) for the Prophet? This debate affects whether it is sunnah or mustahabb for the Ummah. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that night prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) for us.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its virtue
The act is night prayer (tahajjud). The passage states it is more virtuous than day prayer, particularly in the last third of the night. This is proven by Quranic verses and hadith.
The virtue is based on the effort of leaving sleep.
2
Locate the Quranic and hadith proofs
The passage cites Quran: 'Their sides forsake their beds' (al-Sajdah 32:16) and 'Indeed, the rising at night is more effective' (al-Muzzammil 73:6). Also hadith: 'Your reward is according to your exertion' and the narration about the Prophet's character being the Quran.
These proofs establish the lofty station of night prayer.
3
Trace the dispute about the Prophet's obligation
Scholars differed: one group held it was fard upon the Prophet based on the imperative 'قم' in al-Muzzammil. Another group said it was nafl based on the verse calling it 'nafl' in al-Isra. The passage explains both views and the reasoning behind each.
The first group interprets 'nafl' as 'extra fard' specific to the Prophet.
4
Determine the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling for the Ummah
Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam and Sharh al-Munyah conclude that night prayer is sunnah muakkadah for the Ummah, regardless of its status for the Prophet. The passage ends with the narration from Aisha about the Prophet's character being the Quran, emphasizing his devotion.
The mufta bihi ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah, not fard.

لا ندب الفعل، ولذا قال في ( الاختيار » : وصلاة الليل ركعتين بتسليمة، أو أربع، أو ست أو ثمان وكل ذلك نقل في تهجده . انتهى. والشأن في بيان الأفضل، وأجاب المحقق « ابن الهمام عن دليلهما بـ : أن لفظ الحديث إما مثنى في حق الفضيلة بالنسبة إلى الأربع، أو في حق الإباحة بالنسبة إلى الفرد، وترجيح أحدهما لا يكون إلا بمرجح، وقد ورد فعله على كلا النحوين، لكنا عقلنا زيادة فضيلة الأربع بأنها أكثر مشقة على النفس، بسبب طول تقييدها في مقام الخدمة، ورأيناه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : « إِنَّمَا أَجْرُكَ عَلَى قَدْرِ نَصَبِكَ ). فحكمنا بأن المراد الثاني، وهو الإباحة أي: يباح مثنى، لا واحدة أو ثلاثاً. انتهى ملخصاً (وصــلاة الـلـيـل) خصوصاً في الثلث الأخير منه أفضلُ منْ صلاةِ النّهار)؛ لأنه اشق على النفس، وقد قال تعالى: ﴿ نَتَجَافَى جُنُوبُهُمْ عَنِ الْمَضاجِيع [التاة : ١٦] الآية، وقال تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ نَاشِئَةَ الَّيْلِ [الم : ٦] الآية، ولكونه وقـت التجلي وعرض الإحسان هل من داع، هل من مستغفر ، هل من مسترزق، فأما صفتها فقد قال في «شرح المنية»: إنها مستحبة، وقلنا مثله كما سنذكره، ولكن قال ( الكمال بن الهمام» : بقي أن صفة صلاة الليل في حقنا السنية، والاستحباب يتوقف على صفتها في حقه ، فإن كانت في حقـه فـرضـاً فـهي مندوبة في حقنا، لكن الأدلة القولية فيها إنما تفيد الندب، والمواظبة الفعلية، ليسـت عـلـى تـطـوع؛ ليكون سنة في حقنا وإن كان تطوعاً فسنة لنا، وقد اختلف العلماء في ذلك فذهب طائفة إلى أنها فرض عليه، وعليه كلام الأصوليين من مشايخنا تمسكوا فيه بقوله تعالى: وَ الَّيْلَ إِلَّا قَلِيلًا ﴾ [المزمك : ٢] وقالت طائفة: تطوع لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِنَ الَّيْلِ فَتَهَجَّدْ بِهِ نَافِلَة [الإسراء : ٧٩] والأولــون قالوا: لا منافاة لأن المراد بالنافلة الزائدة أي زائدة على ما فُرض على غيرك أي تهجد فرضاً زائداً لك على ما فرض على غيرك، وربما يعطي التقييد بالمجرور ذلك فإنه إذا كان الفعل المتعارف يكون كذلك له ولغيره، وأسند عن مجاهد، والحسن، وأبي أمامة أن تسميتها نافلة باعتبار كونها في حقه ، عاملة في رفع الدرجات، (1) أخرجه الحاكم في المستدرك (٦٤٤/١).
And night prayer is better than day prayer. The head of every pair; because we narrated evidence for its abrogation, or that it is from his special characteristics. End. I say: Al-Tahawi's intent was not the absolute negation of existence, but rather the existence of what is not contradictory, restrictive, or abrogated. And what is narrated in Muslim is possible to indicate validity if done, not recommendation of the act. Hence he said in al-Ikhtiyār: 'Night prayer is two rak'ahs with one salam, or four, or six, or eight – all of that is narrated in his tahajjud.' End. And the discussion is about clarifying the best. And the investigator Ibn al-Humām answered their evidence: That the wording of the hadith either means 'mathnā' regarding virtue compared to four, or regarding permissibility compared to odd, and preferring one requires a preponderant, and his practice occurred in both ways, but we rationally see the increased virtue of four as it is more strenuous on the soul due to the length of its restriction in the station of service, and we see the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Your reward is according to your exertion.' So we ruled that the second meaning is intended, i.e., permissibility: it is permissible to pray by twos, not one or three. End summary. And night prayer, especially in the last third of it, is better than day prayer; because it is more strenuous on the soul, and Allah Almighty said: 'Their sides forsake their beds' [al-Sajdah 32:16] the verse, and He said: 'Indeed, the rising at night' [al-Muzzammil 73:6] the verse, and because it is a time of divine manifestation and offering of beneficence: Is there a supplicant? Is there a seeker of forgiveness? Is there a seeker of provision? As for its ruling, he said in Sharh al-Munyah: It is mustahabb (supererogatory), and we have said the same as we will mention. But al-Kamal ibn al-Humām said: There remains that the ruling of night prayer for us is sunnah, and its recommendation depends on its ruling for him (the Prophet). If it was fard for him, then it is mandūb (recommended) for us, but the verbal evidences only indicate recommendation, and the continual practice is not on a voluntary basis to be sunnah for us; if it was voluntary, then it is sunnah for us. And the scholars differed on this: a group held it was fard upon him, and upon this is the speech of the usuliyyūn among our mashāyikh, holding onto His statement: 'Stand the night except for a little' [al-Muzzammil 73:2]. And another group said: voluntary, based on His statement: 'And from the night, pray with it as additional (nafl) for you' [al-Isrā' 17:79]. The first group said: There is no contradiction because 'nafl' means extra, i.e., extra to what was fard on others; meaning tahajjud is an additional fard for you beyond what was fard on others. And perhaps the restriction with the preposition indicates that, because if the verb is customary, it would be so for him and others. And it is narrated from Mujāhid, al-Hasan, and Abū Umāmah that its being called nafl is because in his case it acts to raise degrees, unlike others where it acts to expiate sins. But in Muslim, Abū Dāwūd, and al-Nasā'ī from Sa'īd ibn Hishām: I said to 'Ā'ishah: 'O Mother of the Believers, tell me about the character of the Messenger of Allah.' She said: 'Do you not recite the Quran?' I said: 'Yes.' She said: 'Then the character of the Prophet of Allah was the Quran.' He said: 'I intended to stand and not ask anyone.'
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage begins with the matn stating that night prayer is superior to day prayer, particularly the last third of the night. The commentary provides proofs from the Quran, such as 'Their sides forsake their beds' (Surah al-Sajdah) and 'Indeed, the rising at night is more effective' (Surah al-Muzzammil), and from hadith about the merits of night prayer. The author notes that night prayer is more strenuous because it involves leaving one's sleep, hence greater reward. The passage then discusses the legal status of night prayer (tahajjud) for the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and for the Ummah. According to Sharh al-Munyah, night prayer is mustahabb (supererogatory) for us. However, al-Kamal ibn al-Humam raises a subtle point: whether it is sunnah or mustahabb depends on whether it was fard or nafl for the Prophet. If it was fard for him, then for us it is mandub (recommended); if it was nafl for him, then for us it is sunnah. The scholars differed: some held it was fard for the Prophet based on 'Stand the night except a little' (al-Muzzammil), interpreting it as an obligation. Others held it was voluntary (nafl) based on 'And from the night, pray with it as additional' (al-Isra), taking the word 'nafl' to mean supererogatory. The first group argues that 'nafl' here means 'extra fard', i.e., an additional obligation specific to the Prophet. The author mentions that some earlier scholars (Mujahid, Hasan al-Basri, Abu Umamah) held that it is called nafl because for the Prophet it raises degrees, while for others it expiates sins. The passage concludes with a hadith from Aisha describing the Prophet's character as the Quran, implying his perfect devotion. The overall Hanafi position is that night prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) for the Ummah, regardless of its exact status for the Prophet.

Key Terms
تهجد (tahajjud): Night prayer; specifically the voluntary prayer performed after waking from sleep during the late night.
نافلة (nāfilah): Additional or supererogatory act of worship; in the context of night prayer, it indicates that it is voluntary.
الثلث الأخير (al-thuluth al-ākhir): The last third of the night, considered the most virtuous time for night prayer and supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on night prayer (tahajjud) for the Muslim Ummah?
A) It is fard (obligatory)
B) It is sunnah muakkadah (highly recommended)
C) It is makruh (disliked)
D) It is haram (prohibited)

Key Takeaway
Night prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) for the Ummah, with immense virtue, especially in the last third of the night, and its obligation for the Prophet remains a debated but settled intra-Hanafi issue.

Long Standing vs. Many Prostrations: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on preference between long standing and many prostrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on long standing vs many prostrations, explain the proofs for both views, and apply Abu Yusuf's distinction.

Core Idea
Long standing in prayer is generally superior, but Abu Yusuf’s distinction reconciles conflicting evidence.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: is it better to prolong standing (with recitation) or to increase prostrations? The majority holds that long standing is superior due to the combination of the pillar of standing with the virtue of recitation. However, a transmission from Imam Muhammad argues that many prostrations are better, citing hadiths on the merits of prostration. Abu Yusuf resolves the tension by considering whether one has a fixed nightly recitation. This lesson will guide you through the proofs, the disagreement, and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine what is being compared: prolonged standing (with recitation) versus many prostrations (through additional rak'ahs). Both are voluntary acts; the question is which is more meritorious.
This is not about validity but about preference (afdaliyyah).
2
Examine the Hanafi proof for long standing
Locate the primary hadith: 'The best prayer is long qunut' (meaning standing). Also understand the rational argument: standing includes recitation (better than tasbih) and combines two pillars (qiyam and qira'ah), while prostration is only one pillar plus tasbih.
Note that 'qunut' here is interpreted as standing, not supplication.
3
Examine the opposing proof
Identify the hadiths favoring many prostrations: 'Upon you be many prostrations', 'Help me against yourself by many prostrations', and 'The closest a servant is to his Lord is while prostrating'. Also note the argument that prostration is the utmost humility.
These hadiths are considered general encouragements, not necessarily indicating superiority.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi conflict
Recognize that Imam Muhammad, in a transmission in al-Mujtaba, held the opposite view. Also note that Imam Ahmad abstained from judgment due to conflicting evidence. This shows that even within the school there was divergence.
The majority view (long standing better) is from Zahir al-Riwayah, but the alternative is from a weaker transmission.
5
Apply Abu Yusuf's distinction
Understand the reconciliation: if one has a fixed nightly recitation (wird of recitation), then it is better to increase the number of rak'ahs (many prostrations); otherwise, long standing is better. This distinction is accepted as the mufta bihi.
This distinction harmonizes the proofs by considering the context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

عَنْ شَيْءٍ حَتَّى أَمُوتَ ثُمَّ بَدَا لِي فَقُلْتُ: أَنْبِئِينِي عَنْ قِيَامِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ، فَقَالَتْ: أَلَسْتَ تَقْرَأْ يَا أَيُّهَا الْمُزَّمِّلُ قُمِ اللَّيْلَ إِلا قَلِيلاً؟ قُلْتُ: بَلَى، قَالَتْ: فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى افْتَرَضَ قِيَامَ اللَّيْلِ فِي أَوَّلِ هَذِهِ السُّورَةِ فَقَامَ نَبِيُّ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَصْحَابُهُ حَوْلاً وَأَمْسَكَ اللَّهُ خَاتِمَتَهَا اثْنَيْ عَشَرَ شَهْراً فِي السَّمَاءِ، حَتَّى أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ فِي آخِرِ هَذِهِ السُّورَةِ التَّخْفِيفَ فَصَارَ قِيَامُ اللَّيْلِ تَطَوُّعاً بَعْدَ فَرِيضَةٍ ، ثم قال الكمال: فهذا يقتضي أنــه نسخ وجوبه عنه انتهى. أي: فيكون سنة في حقنا، وطول القيام في الصلاة ليلاً أو نهاراً (أحب من كثرة السجود)؛ لقوله : (أَفْضَلُ الصَّلاةِ طُولُ القُنوتِ (٢) أي: القيام، ولأن القراءة تكثر بطول القيام، وبكثرة الركوع والسجود يكثر التسبيح، والقراءة أفضل منه، واجتماع ركني القراءة والقيام أفضل؛ لأنهما من أجزاء الصلاة، فكان أفضل من اجتماع ركن السجود مع سنة التسبيح، كما في « التبيين»، و« البرهان»، وقال في «البحر » : وهكذا نقل الطحاوي عن محمد في «شرح الآثار»، وصححه في « البدائع » ، ونقل في المجتبى ) عن محمد خلافه، وهـو : أن كثرة الركوع والسجود أفضل لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام للسائل : ( عَلَيْكَ بِكَثرَةِ السُّجُودِ " ، ولآخر : ( أعْنِي عَلَى نَفْسِكَ بكثرة السجود ، وقوله : ( أَقْرَبُ مَا يَكُونُ العَبْدُ مِنْ رَبِّهِ وَهُوَ سَاجد ) ولأن السجود غاية التواضع والعبودية، ولتعارض الأدلة توقف الإمام أحمد في هذه المسألة ولم يحكم فيها بشيء، وفصل أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى فقال: إذا كان له ورد من الليل بقراءة من القرآن، فالأفضل أن يكثر عدد الركعات، وإلا فطول القيام أفضل، لأن القيام في الأول لا يختلف، ويضم إليه زيـادة الركوع والسجود. والله أعلم.

And long standing is more beloved than many prostrations. (1) From a thing until I die, then it occurred to me, so I said: Inform me about the standing of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. She said: Do you not recite 'O you who wraps himself [in clothing], arise [to pray] the night except for a little'? I said: Yes. She said: Indeed Allah the Exalted made standing at night obligatory at the beginning of this surah, so the Prophet of Allah ﷺ and his companions stood for a year, and Allah withheld its conclusion for twelve months in the heaven, until Allah revealed at the end of this surah the lightening, so standing at night became voluntary after being obligatory. Then al-Kamal said: This necessitates that its obligation was abrogated from him — end. That is, it becomes sunnah in our regard. And long standing in prayer, whether by night or day, (is more beloved than many prostrations) because of his ﷺ saying: 'The best prayer is long qunut (i.e. standing).' And because recitation increases with long standing, and with many bowings and prostrations, glorification increases, and recitation is better than it, and the combination of the two pillars of recitation and standing is better because they are parts of the prayer, so it is better than the combination of the pillar of prostration with the sunnah of glorification, as in al-Tabyin and al-Burhan. And in al-Bahr it is said: Thus al-Tahawi transmitted from Muhammad in Sharh al-Athar, and he corrected it in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Mujtaba it is transmitted from Muhammad the opposite: that many bowings and prostrations are better because of his ﷺ saying to the questioner: 'Upon you be many prostrations', and to another: 'Help me against yourself by many prostrations', and his saying: 'The closest that a servant is to his Lord is while he is prostrating', and because prostration is the utmost humility and servitude. Due to the conflicting evidences, Imam Ahmad remained silent in this matter and did not judge anything. And Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, made a distinction: if one has a nightly portion of recitation from the Quran, then it is better to increase the number of rak'ahs; otherwise, long standing is better, because standing in the first is not different, and one adds to it an increase of bowing and prostration. And Allah knows best. (2) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Prayer of Travelers, Chapter: The Best Prayer is Long Qunut (756), and al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: What Has Come About Long Standing in Prayer (387). (3) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: The Virtue of Prostration and Encouragement Upon It (488), and Ibn Majah in the Book of Establishing Prayer, Chapter: What Has Come About Long Standing in Prayer (1423) with the wording: 'Upon you be prostrations'. (4) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: The Virtue of Prostration and Encouragement Upon It (489), and Abu Dawud in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: The Time of the Prophet's Night Prayer (1320). (5) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: What is Said in Bowing and Prostration (482), and Abu Dawud in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: Supplication in Bowing and Prostration (875). - {1. -

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the superior action in prayer: prolonged standing (qiyam) vs. many prostrations (sujud). The author begins by stating the prominent Hanafi position: long standing is more beloved (أحب) than many prostrations. He substantiates this with the hadith that 'the best prayer is long qunut' (i.e., standing), and by rational argument: standing combines recitation (which is superior to tasbih) with the pillar of standing, both being integral parts of the prayer. The combination of two pillars (standing and recitation) is thus more excellent than the combination of one pillar (prostration) with a sunnah act (tasbih). He quotes al-Tabyin and al-Burhan in support. Then he notes that al-Tahawi transmitted from Imam Muhammad in Sharh al-Athar, and corrected it in al-Bada'i', that the same view (long standing is better) is the correct one. However, in al-Mujtaba, a contrary view is transmitted from Imam Muhammad: that many bowings and prostrations are better, based on hadiths encouraging much prostration ('Upon you be many prostrations', etc.) and the notion that prostration is the epitome of humility. Due to the conflicting evidences, Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal expressed no preference. Abu Yusuf distinguished between two cases: if one has a fixed nightly recitation, then increasing the number of rak'ahs (thus performing more prostrations) is better; otherwise, long standing is better. This reconciliation is accepted in the school. The passage ends with 'Wa Allahu a'lam'.

Key Terms
طول القيام (tawl al-qiyam): Prolonged standing in prayer, especially the duration of recitation.
كثرة السجود (kathrat al-sujud): Increasing the number of prostrations, often through additional rak'ahs.
القنوت (al-qunut): Here it means standing (qiyam), not the supplication.
التسبيح (al-tasbih): Glorification of Allah, specifically the dhikr recited during bowing and prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which is generally considered more virtuous: lengthy standing (qiyam) or many prostrations (sujud)?
A) Many prostrations
B) Lengthy standing
C) Both are equal
D) Depends on the time of day

Key Takeaway
Though both actions are virtuous, the Hanafi school generally considers long standing (with recitation) superior to many prostrations, with Abu Yusuf's distinction providing a practical reconciliation.

Tahiyyat al-Masjid: Ruling, Substitution, and Intention
Explaining the ruling of Tahiyyat al-Masjid and related details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tahiyyat al-Masjid, identify what prayers substitute for it, and explain the Hanafi position on combined intention and the effect of sitting.

Core Idea
Tahiyyat al-Masjid is a sunnah fulfilled by any prayer upon entry; sitting does not waive it.

Entering the mosque is an act of worship, and the Shari'ah prescribes a greeting for the mosque's Lord through prayer. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on Tahiyyat al-Masjid, how it can be substituted, and the nuances regarding intention and sitting based on the classical commentaries of Nur al-Idah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that Tahiyyat al-Masjid is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) consisting of two rak'ahs, to be performed upon entering the mosque before sitting.
The hadith uses an imperative form, but Hanafis interpret it as recommendation due to other evidence.
2
Understand the substitution principle
Any obligatory prayer (fard) or any voluntary prayer performed upon entry, even without specific intention for tahiyyah, suffices as the greeting. The purpose is to honor the mosque's Lord.
This is based on the concept that the act of prayer itself achieves the intended glorification.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on combined intention
If one intends both the greeting and an obligatory prayer simultaneously, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider it valid for both; Imam Muhammad holds that it does not count as the greeting.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) follows Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
4
Examine the ruling on sitting
If one sits before praying, the sunnah is still recommended; it is not lost by sitting. However, praying before sitting is better, based on the hadith of Abu Dharr.
This differs from some other scholars who hold it is only valid before sitting.

Chapter: On the Greeting of the Mosque, the Duha Prayer, and Reviving the Nights, etc. The greeting of the mosque is recommended with two rak'ahs before sitting. And performing the obligatory prayer substitutes for it, and every prayer that one performs upon entering without intending the greeting (suffices). Chapter: On the Greeting of the Mosque, the Duha Prayer, and Reviving the Nights, etc. (The greeting of the mosque is recommended) with two rak'ahs that one prays at a non-disliked time (before sitting) because of his ﷺ saying: 'When one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.' And that they be at a non-disliked time, we mentioned its reasoning in its place. (And performing the obligatory prayer substitutes for it) said al-Zayla'i. (And likewise every prayer that one performs) i.e., does (upon entering without intending the greeting) because it is for glorifying it and its sanctity, and any prayer one prays achieves that, as in al-Bada'i'. If one intends the greeting along with the obligatory prayer, then apparently from what is in al-Muhit and others, it is valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to Muhammad, he does not enter into the prayer. And they said: if he intends to enter the Zuhr and the supererogatory, it is permitted for the obligatory according to Abu Yusuf, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa, and according to Muhammad, he does not enter. And it is not lost by sitting according to us, but it is better to do it before sitting because of what we narrated. And likewise, the generality of scholars said: he prays it as he entered, and some said: he sits then stands to pray it. And we only say that it is not waived by sitting because of what Ibn Hibban narrated in his Sahih from Abu Dharr, he said: 'I entered the mosque and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was sitting alone, and he said: O Abu Dharr, indeed the mosque has a greeting, and its greeting is two rak'ahs, so stand and pray them.' So I stood and prayed them. End. The author of al-Bahr said: If he enters repeatedly, two rak'ahs in the day suffice him. And in al-Burhan it is said: It is recommended that when entering the mosque he say: 'O Allah, open for me the doors of Your mercy', and when leaving: 'O Allah, I ask You of Your bounty', due to the Prophet ﷺ commanding it, narrated by Muslim. (1) Meaning: the greeting of the Lord of the mosque, because greeting is only for the owner of the place, not the place. And the Sacred Mosque is excepted, for its greeting is tawaf. (2) Meaning: If he enters the mosque after Fajr or Asr, he does not perform the greeting, but rather glorifies, declares His oneness, and sends blessings upon the Prophet, for then he fulfills the right of the mosque. (3) Narrated by al-Bukhari in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: When he enters the mosque, let him pray two rak'ahs (444), and Muslim in the Book of Travelers' Prayer, Chapter: Recommending the Greeting of the Mosque with Two Rak'ahs (714). (4) Narrated by Ibn Hibban in his Sahih (2/76), and al-Haythami in Mawrid al-Zam'an (1/52). (5) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Travelers' Prayer, Chapter: What to say when entering the mosque (713), and Abu Dawud in the Book of Prayer, Chapter: On what a man says when entering the mosque (465). - 411 -
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This section explains the ruling and details of Tahiyyat al-Masjid (greeting the mosque). It begins by stating that the greeting of the mosque is recommended (sunnah) with two rak'ahs before sitting. The evidence is the well-known hadith: 'When one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.' The Hanafi school interprets this as a recommendation, not an obligation. However, these two rak'ahs should be performed at a time when prayer is not disliked (e.g., not after Fajr or Asr). Next, the author notes that if one enters the mosque and immediately prays the prescribed obligatory prayer (e.g., Zuhr), that suffices for the greeting, even without separate intention. Similarly, any prayer performed upon entry, without specifically intending the greeting, fulfills the sunnah because the purpose is to honor the mosque. If one intends both the greeting and an obligatory prayer simultaneously (i.e., as a combined intention), the text reports a difference within the Hanafi school: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two), the prayer is valid for both; according to Imam Muhammad, the prayer is not considered as the greeting (the intention does not make him enter the prayer for greeting). This is a nuanced point. The author then emphasizes that the greeting is not waived by sitting first; if one sits initially, they may still stand and pray it, though it is better to pray before sitting. The proof is the hadith of Abu Dharr where the Prophet ﷺ instructed him to pray two rak'ahs after he had already sat. Additionally, if one enters the mosque multiple times, two rak'ahs once a day suffices. Finally, the passage recommends supplications upon entering and leaving the mosque. Two important exceptions are noted in the footnotes: first, the greeting is for the Lord of the mosque, not the building; second, in the Sacred Mosque (Makkah), the greeting is performed by tawaf (circumambulation). Also, if one enters during a disliked time (after Fajr/Asr), one should instead engage in dhikr and salawat.

Key Terms
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): Two rak'ahs of prayer performed upon entering a mosque as a greeting and honor to the mosque's Lord.
ينوب عنها (yanubu 'anha): It substitutes for it; meaning the obligatory prayer takes the place of the greeting sunnah.
نية التحية (niyyat al-tahiyya): Intention of performing the greeting prayer.
لا تفوت بالجلوس (la tafut bil-julus): The opportunity to perform Tahiyyat al-Masjid is not lost by sitting; one can still pray it after sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following correctly describes the substitution (niyabah) for Tahiyyat al-Masjid?
A) Only the two rak'ahs of Fajr can substitute.
B) Any obligatory prayer performed upon entry suffices, but a voluntary prayer does not.
C) Any prayer (obligatory or voluntary) performed upon entry, even without specific intention, suffices.
D) Only a prayer with specific intention for tahiyyah substitutes.

Key Takeaway
Tahiyyat al-Masjid is a sunnah muakkadah; any prayer upon entry suffices, and sitting does not nullify it, though praying before sitting is best.

The Ruling of Tahiyyat al-Masjid (Greeting the Mosque)
Stating the ruling of tahiyyat al-masjid with proofs and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tahiyyat al-masjid, explain the evidence, and apply the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining intention.

Core Idea
The greeting of the mosque is a sunnah fulfilled by any prayer; sitting does not nullify it, and combining intention is valid per the majority.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the sunnah of greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid) — a two-rak'ah prayer upon entering. It presents the primary proof from hadith and clarifies key sub-issues: substitution by any prayer, the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining intentions, and the effect of sitting. The text also notes exceptions and recommended supplications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tahiyyat al-masjid. The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). The passage uses 'sunn' to indicate this.
In Hanafi, sunnah mu'akkadah is a recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'When one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.' (Bukhari and Muslim). The Hanafi school interprets the command as recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
Other schools consider it wajib; the difference stems from usul al-fiqh on amr.
3
Understand the substitution principle
Any prayer (fard or nafl) performed upon entering suffices for the greeting, because the purpose is glorification of the mosque.
This is based on the principle that the underlying purpose is achieved by any prayer.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
If one intends tahiyya together with fard, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is valid; Muhammad says it is not. The relied-upon position is the majority view.
The dispute hinges on whether the lesser act (tahiyya) is absorbed into the greater (fard).
5
Note the effect of sitting
Sitting does not nullify the sunnah; it can be prayed afterwards, but it is better to pray before sitting. Proof: hadith of Abu Dharr.
The Prophet ﷺ was sitting when Abu Dharr entered, yet he instructed him to stand and pray.

Source Text

(1) أي: تحية رب المسجد، لأن التحية إنما تكون لصاحب المكان لا للمكان، ويستثنى المسجد الحرام فإن تحيت الطواف. ط.
(٢) أي: إذا دخل المسجد بعد الفجر أو العصر لا يأتي بالتحية، بل يسبح ويهلل ويصـلـي عـلـى النبي ، فإنـه حينئذ يؤدي حق المسجد. ط.
(۳) أخرجه البخاري في الصلاة، باب : إذا دخل المسجد فليركع ركعتين (٤٤٤) ، ومسلم في صلاة المسافرين، باب: استحباب تحية المسجد بركعتين (٧١٤).
(٤) أخرجه ابن حبان في صحيحه (٧٦/۲)، والهيثمي في موارد الظمآن (٥٢/١).
(0) أخرجه مسلم في صلاة المسافرين، باب ما يقول إذا دخل المسجد (۷۱۳)، وأبو داود في الصلاة، باب: فيما يقوله الرجل عند دخول المسجد (٤٦٥).
Chapter: On greeting the mosque, Salat al-Duha, reviving the nights, and others. The greeting of the mosque is sunnah with two rak'ahs before sitting. Performing the obligatory prayer substitutes for it, and any prayer he performs upon entering without intending the greeting (suffices). Chapter on greeting the mosque, Salat al-Duha, reviving the nights, and others. (The greeting of the mosque is sunnah) with two rak'ahs that one prays in non-reprehensible time (before sitting); due to his ﷺ saying: 'When one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.' (3) And that they be in a non-reprehensible time, we have mentioned its reasoning in its place. (And performing the obligatory prayer substitutes for it) stated by al-Zayla'i. (And) likewise, any prayer he performs (i.e., does) (upon entering without intending the greeting); because it is for glorifying and honoring it, and any prayer he prays achieves that, as in al-Bada'i'. So if he intends the greeting with the obligatory prayer, the apparent ruling in al-Muhit and others is that it is valid according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to Muhammad he is not entering into the prayer. For they said: If he intends to enter into the noon prayer and supererogatory, then it is permissible for the obligatory prayer according to Abu Yusuf, and that is a narration from Abu Hanifa, and according to Muhammad he is not entering. And it is not missed by sitting according to us, but it is better to do it before sitting due to what we narrated. And likewise, the majority of scholars said he prays it as he entered, but some said: He sits then stands to pray it. And we only say that it is not nullified by sitting because of what Ibn Hibban narrated in his Sahih from Abu Dharr: 'I entered the mosque and there was the Messenger of Allah ﷺ sitting alone. He said: O Abu Dharr, indeed the mosque has a greeting and its greeting is two rak'ahs, so stand and pray them. So I stood and prayed them.' (4) End. The author of al-Bahr said: If he enters repeatedly, two rak'ahs per day suffice him. And in al-Burhan: It is recommended that he say upon entering the mosque: 'O Allah, open for me the doors of Your mercy,' and upon exiting: 'O Allah, I ask You of Your bounty,' due to the Prophet's ﷺ command to do so; narrated by Muslim. (1) Meaning: greeting the Lord of the mosque, because greeting is only for the owner of the place, not the place. And the Sacred Mosque is excepted, for its greeting is tawaf. (2) Meaning: If he enters the mosque after Fajr or Asr, he does not do the greeting, but rather glorifies, says la ilaha illa Allah, and sends blessings on the Prophet ﷺ; for then he fulfills the right of the mosque. (3) Narrated by Bukhari in Salat, Chapter: When one enters the mosque, let him pray two rak'ahs (444), and Muslim in Salat al-Musafirin, Chapter: Recommendation of greeting the mosque with two rak'ahs (714). (4) Narrated by Ibn Hibban in his Sahih (2/76) and al-Haythami in Mawrid al-Zam'an (1/52). (5) Narrated by Muslim in Salat al-Musafirin, Chapter: What one says when entering the mosque (713), and Abu Dawud in Salat, Chapter: What one says when entering the mosque (465).
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) on the sunnah of greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid). The author begins by stating that it is sunnah to pray two rak'ahs upon entering a mosque before sitting, in a non-reprehensible time. The primary proof is the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: 'When one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.' The commentary then addresses several sub-issues. First, performing an obligatory prayer (fard) upon entering suffices for the greeting, and similarly any prayer (whether fard or nafl) fulfills it, as stated in al-Bada'i'. The author then discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: if one intends both the greeting and the obligatory prayer together, according to Abu Hanifa (in one narration) and Abu Yusuf it is valid, while according to Muhammad it is not; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the former. Next, the sitting does not nullify the sunnah; it is simply better to pray before sitting, proven by the hadith of Abu Dharr from Ibn Hibban where the Prophet ﷺ explicitly told him to stand and pray even though he (the Prophet) was sitting. Additionally, if one enters the mosque multiple times, two rak'ahs once per day suffice. Finally, recommended supplications upon entering and exiting are mentioned. The passage is a classic example of a Hanafi sharh expanding on a concise matn, providing proofs and clarifying the school's position on a commonly encountered practice.

Key Terms
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): The greeting of the mosque; a two-rak'ah prayer offered upon entering a mosque to honor it, before sitting.
سُنَّ (sunn): Passive verb meaning 'it is sunnah' – a preferred act that is not fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sunnah is nullified and cannot be made up.
B) The sunnah is not missed; he can pray it later, but it is better to pray before sitting.
C) The sunnah becomes incumbent (wajib) upon him.
D) He must repeat his entry.

Key Takeaway
The greeting of the mosque is a flexible sunnah that can be fulfilled by any prayer, and the mufta bihi position permits combining intention with an obligator prayer.

Recommended Prayers After Wudu and Duha (Forenoon Prayer)
Stating the recommendation of two rak'ahs after wudu and the ruling of Duha prayer with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for two rak'ahs after wudu and for Duha prayer, identify their proofs, and explain the minimum rak'ahs for Duha according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Two rak'ahs after wudu promise Paradise; Duha is recommended with a minimum of four rak'ahs.

This lesson covers two recommended prayers: the two rak'ahs after performing wudu (before the water dries) and the Duha (forenoon) prayer. The author presents hadith proofs and clarifies the Hanafi position on the minimum number of rak'ahs for Duha, which is four, contrary to common assumptions that two suffice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two recommended acts and their rulings
Read the first part about two rak'ahs after wudu, then the part about Duha prayer. Note that both are described with 'nudiba' (it is recommended).
The ruling level is mandub (recommended).
2
Locate the dalil (proof) for each act
For the two rak'ahs after wudu, the text cites the hadith from Muslim. For Duha, it cites the hadith from A'isha in Muslim and the hadith from al-Tabarani.
These are ahad hadith, so zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyze how the proof indicates recommendation (wajh al-dalalah)
The hadith for two rak'ahs after wudu promises Paradise, indicating strong reward. For Duha, the Prophet's consistent practice of four rak'ahs and the virtue hadiths show encouragement.
The imperative form or explicit promise is not present; rather, the wording indicates desirability.
4
Note the ikhtilaf regarding Duha's minimum
The text says 'ala al-rajih' (on the most correct view), indicating that there is a difference of opinion. Some scholars consider Duha as merely permissible or with a different minimum.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the practical outcome for Duha
The rajih view is that Duha is recommended with a minimum of four rak'ahs, up to twelve. The time is from sunrise to zenith.
If one prays only two rak'ahs with intention of Duha, it is not considered the specific sunnah but a general nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونُدِبَ رَكعتان، بعد الوضوء، قبلَ جَفَافِهِ) لقوله : «مَا مِنْ مُسْلِمٍ يَتَوَضَّأُ فَيُحْسِنُ وُضُوءَهُ، ثُمَّ يَقُومُ فَيُصَلِّي رَكْعَتَيْنِ يُقْبِلُ عَلَيْهِمَا بِقَلْبِهِ، إِلا وَجَبَتْ لَهُ الْجَنَّةُ » ( رواه مسلم، كذا في «البرهان». وندب صلاة الضحى على الراجح ، (وَ) هي: (أربع ركعات؛ لما رويناه قريباً عن عائشة : « أنـه عـلـيـه الصلاة والسلام كَانَ يُصَلِّي الضُّحَى أَرْبَعَاً ولا يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَهُمَا بِسَلام ) (۳)، ولما في «صحيح مسلم» عن عائشة أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كَانَ يُصَلِّي الضُّحَى أَرْبَعَ رَكْعَاتٍ، وَيَزِيدُ مَا شَاءَ ) فلذا قلنا : ندب أربع (فصاعداً) إلى اثنتي عشرة ركعة؛ لما روي الطبراني في ( الكبير»، عن أبي الدرداء قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( مَنْ صَلَّى الضُّحَى رَكْعَتَينِ لَمْ يُكتب مِنَ الغَافِلينَ، وَمَنْ صَلَاهَا سِنَّا كُفـي ذلِكَ اليوم، وَمَنْ صَلَّى ثمانيةٌ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ مِنَ القَانِتِينَ، وَمَنْ صَلَّى اثنتي عَشْرَةَ رَكْعَةً بَنَى اللَّهُ لَهُ بَيْنَا فِي الجَنَّةِ، وَمَا مِنْ يَومٍ وليلةٍ إلا لله مِنْ يَمنُ بِهِ عَلَى عِبَادِهِ وصَدَقة، ومَا مِنَّ الله عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ أَفْضَلَ مِنْ أَنْ يُلْهِمَهُ ذِكْرَهُ » ) قال المنذري : ورواته ثقات، كذا في ( البحر» (في) وقـت (الضحى)، وابتداؤه مـن ارتفاع الشمس إلى زوالها.
And it is recommended to pray two rak'ahs after wudu, before it dries, due to his saying: 'There is no Muslim who performs wudu and does it well, then stands and prays two rak'ahs, turning his heart to them, except that Paradise becomes obligatory for him' (narrated by Muslim, as in al-Burhan). And Duha prayer is recommended according to the most correct view, and it is four rak'ahs; because we recently narrated from A'isha: 'He (peace be upon him) used to pray Duha four rak'ahs and did not separate them with salutation' (3), and because in Sahih Muslim from A'isha that he (peace be upon him) used to pray Duha four rak'ahs and increase as he wished. Therefore we said: four (and above) are recommended, up to twelve rak'ahs; because al-Tabarani narrated in al-Kabir from Abu al-Darda' that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever prays Duha two rak'ahs will not be written among the heedless; whoever prays it four (or six?) will be sufficed that day; whoever prays eight, Allah writes him among the devout; whoever prays twelve rak'ahs, Allah builds for him a house in Paradise. There is no day or night but Allah bestows something upon His servants and charity, and Allah has not bestowed upon any of His servants anything better than that He inspires him with His remembrance.' Al-Mundhiri said: Its narrators are reliable, as in al-Bahr. And the time of Duha: its beginning is from the rising of the sun to its zenith.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents two separate recommended acts: (1) praying two rak'ahs after completing wudu, before the water dries, based on a hadith in Muslim that promises Paradise for it; (2) the Duha (forenoon) prayer. The author states that Duha is recommended (mandub) on the rajih (preferred) view of the Hanafi school. Its minimum is four rak'ahs, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as narrated by A'isha, and one may increase up to twelve rak'ahs based on the hadith from al-Tabarani. The time of Duha is from sunrise to zenith. The passage combines proof from hadith and establishes the quantity within the Hanafi school. It does not discuss the ruling for those who pray less than four (e.g., two), though the hadith mentions two rak'ahs rewards; the minimum for proper Duha is four as per the school.

Key Terms
الضحى (al-duha): The forenoon; a time for a recommended prayer that starts after sunrise (after the sun has risen approximately the length of a spear) until zenith.
ندب (nudiba): Passive verb 'it is recommended' – indicating a mandub or mustahabb act, one that is rewarded if done but not sinful if omitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Four rak'ahs

D) Twelve rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
Two rak'ahs after wudu and Duha prayer (minimum four) are recommended acts with strong hadith proofs, and the Hanafi school's minimum for Duha is four rak'ahs.

Duha Prayer: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling and proofs for Duha prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Duha prayer, identify its minimum and maximum rak'ahs, and cite the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Duha prayer is recommended with a minimum of four rak'ahs, based on the Prophet's practice.

This passage from Imdād al-Fattāḥ explains the ruling for Duha (forenoon) prayer. The author clarifies that the preponderant view in the Hanafi school is that it is recommended (mandūb), not obligatory, and its minimum is four rak'ahs. He supports this with hadith from ʿĀʾishah and encourages additional rak'ahs up to twelve based on a hadith from Abū al-Dardāʾ. We will examine the proofs and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening phrase 'wa nudiba' and 'ala al-rajih'. This tells you the hukm level: recommended (mandub). Note that it is not a confirmed sunnah.
Hanafi: Duha is sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Determine the minimum rak'ahs
The text states 'arba'a raka'at' and correlates it with the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed four. This fixes the minimum at four.
Contrary to some who assume two.
3
Examine the primary dalil
Look at the hadith from Aisha about the Prophet praying four without separating with taslim. This indicates the recommended number.
The phrase 'wa la yafsilu baynahuma bi salam' suggests continuity.
4
Examine the secondary proof
The hadith from Abu al-Darda mentions rewards for 2, 6, 8, and 12 rak'ahs. This shows the upper limit of twelve is encouraged.
Al-Mundhiri graded the narrators trustworthy.
5
Note the time
The time for Duha is from sunrise (after it has fully risen) to zawal (zenith). This is a condition for validity.
Hanafi: from sunrise to zawal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونُدِبَ صلاة الضحى على الراجح ، (وَ) هي: (أربع ركعات؛ لما رويناه قريباً عن عائشة : « أنـه عـلـيـه الصلاة والسلام كَانَ يُصَلِّي الضُّحَى أَرْبَعَاً ولا يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَهُمَا بِسَلام )، ولما في «صحيح مسلم» عن عائشة أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كَانَ يُصَلِّي الضُّحَى أَرْبَعَ رَكْعَاتٍ، وَيَزِيدُ مَا شَاءَ ) فلذا قلنا : ندب أربع (فصاعداً) إلى اثنتي عشرة ركعة؛ لما روي الطبراني في ( الكبير»، عن أبي الدرداء قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( مَنْ صَلَّى الضُّحَى رَكْعَتَينِ لَمْ يُكتب مِنَ الغَافِلينَ، وَمَنْ صَلَاهَا سِنَّا كُفـي ذلِكَ اليوم، وَمَنْ صَلَّى ثمانيةٌ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ مِنَ القَانِتِينَ، وَمَنْ صَلَّى اثنتي عَشْرَةَ رَكْعَةً بَنَى اللَّهُ لَهُ بَيْنَا فِي الجَنَّةِ، وَمَا مِنْ يَومٍ وليلةٍ إلا لله مِنْ يَمنُ بِهِ عَلَى عِبَادِهِ وصَدَقة، ومَا مِنَّ الله عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ أَفْضَلَ مِنْ أَنْ يُلْهِمَهُ ذِكْرَهُ » ) قال المنذري : ورواته ثقات، كذا في ( البحر). (في) وقـت (الضحى)، وابتداؤه مـن ارتفاع الشمس إلى زوالها.
And Duha prayer is recommended on the preponderant view, and it is: four rak'ahs, due to what we narrated recently from Aisha that he (peace be upon him) used to pray Duha four rak'ahs and did not separate them with salams, and due to what is in Sahih Muslim from Aisha that he used to pray Duha four rak'ahs and increase as he wished. Therefore we said: four are recommended, and more up to twelve rak'ahs, due to what al-Tabarani narrated in al-Kabir from Abu al-Darda that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever prays Duha two rak'ahs is not written among the heedless; whoever prays it six rak'ahs, it suffices him that day; whoever prays eight rak'ahs, Allah writes him among the devout; whoever prays twelve rak'ahs, Allah builds for him a house in Paradise; and there is no day or night except that Allah has charity which He bestows upon His servants, and Allah has not bestowed upon any of His servants anything better than inspiring him with His remembrance.' Al-Mundhiri said: its narrators are trustworthy, as in al-Bahr. (The time of Duha) its beginning is from the rising of the sun to its zenith.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling and proofs for Duha prayer. The author first notes that Duha prayer is recommended (mandub) on the preponderant view. He then clarifies its minimum: four rak'ahs, based on Aisha's hadith that the Prophet ﷺ prayed four without separating with a salām (i.e., two pairs of two connected). Another hadith from Muslim shows he prayed four and increased as he wished, establishing flexibility. The upper limit is given as twelve rak'ahs, supported by a hadith from Abu al-Darda (graded trustworthy by al-Mundhiri) enumerating rewards for different numbers. The time for Duha is from sunrise (after its complete rising) until zenith (zawal). In Hanafi fiqh, Duha is a recommended sunnah (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) with this range.

Key Terms
الضحى (al-duha): The forenoon; time after sunrise until before noon (zawal).
على الراجح (ala al-rajih): On the preponderant view; the stronger opinion in the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of rak'ahs for Duha prayer according to this text?
A) Two
B) Four
C) Six
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
Duha prayer is a recommended sunnah with a minimum of four rak'ahs and maximum of twelve, based on authentic hadith.

Night Prayer (Tahajjud) and Its Merit
Ruling on night prayer with virtues and minimum recommendation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on night prayer in the Hanafi school and identify the textual proofs that establish its recommendation.

Core Idea
Night prayer is an emphasized sunnah, rewarded immensely, and even a short prayer after Isha counts.

Night prayer, known as tahajjud or qiyam al-layl, is a deeply meritorious act in the Hanafi school. This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentary presents the ruling as recommended (mandub) and cites powerful Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths to motivate the believer. Despite a hesitation reported from al-Kamal about whether it is an emphasized sunnah or merely supererogatory, the predominant position is that it is a sunnah muakkadah. The passage also clarifies that any voluntary prayer after Isha, even before sleep and as brief as milking a goat, constitutes night prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
The author states 'wa nudiba' (and it is recommended). Determine the hukm level from the context: is it sunnah, nafl, or wajib? Note the mention of hesitation from al-Kamal.
The term 'nudiba' indicates mandub, but the hadith 'alaykum' suggests emphasis.
2
Locate the dalil (proofs)
The passage cites Quran 32:16-17, a hadith from Sahih Muslim, and another from al-Tabarani. Identify each source and its relevance.
The Quranic verse promises hidden rewards; the hadith commands night prayer as the practice of the righteous.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The Quran praises those who leave their beds, indicating virtue. The hadith uses 'alaykum' (upon you), which in Hanafi usul implies recommendation, not obligation. The minimum mentioned (length of milking a goat) shows even a little suffices.
The imperative style in the hadith is interpreted as recommendation due to lack of evidence for obligation.
4
Consider the minimum recommendation
The author quotes al-Jawhara that the minimum one should perform at night is eight rak'ahs, but the hadith indicates any amount is beneficial. Understand the distinction between the ideal and the sufficient.
Eight rak'ahs is a recommended target, not a condition for validity.
5
Note the timing and scope
The commentary states that voluntary prayer after Isha before sleep is considered night prayer. This shows that tahajjud need not be performed after waking up; it includes qiyam al-layl at any time after Isha.
This counters a common misunderstanding that night prayer is only after midnight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونُدِبَ صلاة الليل خصوصاً آخره، وأقـل مـا ينبغي أن يتنـفــل بالليل ثماني ركعات، كذا في «الجوهرة» وفضلها أكثر من أن يحصر؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَا تَعْلَمُ نَفْسٌ مَّا أُخْفِيَ لَهُم مِّن قُرَةٍ أَعْيُنِ ﴾ [السجدة: ۱۷]، للذين نَتَجَافَى جُنُوبُهُمْ عَنِ الْمَضَاجِي ﴾ [السجدة: ١٦]. وفي «صحيح مسلم» قال : ( عَلَيْكُم بِصَلاة الليل ، فإِنَّهُ دَابُ الصَّالحينَ قَبْلَكُمْ، وقربَةٌ إلى رَبِّكُم، ومُكَفِّرَةٌ للسَّيِّئاتِ، وَمَنْهَاةٌ عن الإثْمِ ) ()، وفي (الجوهرة) قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( مَنْ أطال قيام الليلِ خَفَّفَ اللهُ عَنْهُ يَومَ القِيَامَةِ » ). انتهى. وفي ( الطبراني ) مرفوعاً: «لا بُدَّ مِنْ صَلاةِ اللَّيْلِ، وَلَوْ قَدْرَ حَلْبٍ شَاةٍ، وَمَا كَانَ بَعْدَ صَلاةِ العِشَاءِ فَهُوَ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ » (٣) انتهى. وهو يفيد أن هذه السنة تحصل بالتنفل بعد صلاة العشاء قبـل النوم، قاله صاحبه, وقدمنا عن الكمال التردد في تهجد الليل هو سنة في حقنـا أم تطوع.
And night prayer is recommended, especially its last part, and the minimum that one should perform for voluntary prayer at night is eight rak'ahs, as in al-Jawhara. Its virtue is beyond enumeration due to His saying: 'No soul knows what has been hidden for them of comfort for eyes' [Sajdah 32:17] for those 'whose sides forsake their beds' [Sajdah 32:16]. And in Sahih Muslim he said: 'Upon you is night prayer, for it is the practice of the righteous before you, a means of closeness to your Lord, expiation for sins, and a deterrent from sin.' And in al-Jawhara he said: 'Whoever prolongs standing at night, Allah will lighten his standing on the Day of Resurrection.' End. And in al-Tabarani as marfu': 'Night prayer is indispensable, even if it is the length of milking a goat, and whatever is after Isha prayer is from the night.' End. This indicates that this sunnah is attained by performing voluntary prayer after Isha before sleep, according to its author. And we have previously mentioned from al-Kamal the hesitation (tatarrud) whether tahajjud is sunnah for us or just nafl (supererogatory).
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage discusses the night prayer (tahajjud/qiyam al-layl). The author states it is recommended (mandub), especially the latter part of the night. He also mentions a minimum of eight rak'ahs from al-Jawhara, but notes that even a little (like milking a goat) is valuable. The proofs include the Quranic verses from Surah al-Sajdah promising unseen rewards for those who pray at night, and several hadiths emphasizing its merit: it was the practice of the righteous, expiates sins, and brings closeness to Allah. The author notes an ikhtilaf (cited from al-Kamal) whether tahajjud is a sunnah (emphasized) or just a nafl (supererogatory) for the ummah. The phrase 'after Isha before sleep' indicates that voluntary prayers after Isha contribute to night prayer even if one sleeps before tahajjud. In Hanafi fiqh, tahajjud is generally considered sunnah (recommended), especially the witr prayer, but there is variance on its emphasis.

Key Terms
تهجد (tahajjud): Night prayer after sleeping; sometimes used synonymously with qiyam al-layl.
صلاة الليل (salat al-layl): Any voluntary prayer performed during the night after Isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith from al-Tabarani cited in the passage, what is the minimum amount of night prayer?
A) Two rak'ahs
B) Four rak'ahs
C) Eight rak'ahs
D) Even if it is the length of milking a goat

Key Takeaway
Night prayer is a highly recommended (sunnah muakkadah) act that can be as short as a few moments after Isha, with immense rewards as promised in the Quran and hadith.

Salat al-Istikhara: The Recommended Prayer for Seeking Guidance
Ruling and method of Istikhara prayer with full supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the ruling and method of Salat al-Istikhara according to the Hanafi school and apply it to a decision-making scenario.

Core Idea
Istikhara is a two-rak'ah prayer followed by a supplication; the sign to act is inner ease, not a dream.

This passage clarifies the recommended prayer of Istikhara. The source provides the full hadith and practical instructions. Understanding the correct method helps avoid misconceptions about needing extraordinary signs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the verb phrase 'nudiba' and note that it indicates recommendation (mandub/sunnah).
The ruling is sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Extract the method
Read the hadith: two rak'ahs (nafl) then the specific supplication, mentioning the need.
Combine both wordings of the dua as per author's recommendation.
3
Recognize the sign
The text says to proceed with what the heart becomes open to (sharh al-sadr), not to wait for a dream.
This is the practical outcome after Istikhara.
4
Note the repetition
The hadith from Anas recommends repeating the Istikhara seven times.
Repetition is recommended but not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونُدِبَ (صلاة الاستخارة) وقد أفصحت السنة عن بيانها، قال جابر: كان رسول الله لا يعلمنا الاستخارة في الأمور كلها، كما يعلمنا السورة من القرآن يقول: « إِذَا هَمَّ أحَدُكُمْ بِالْأَمْرِ فَلْيَرْكَعْ رَكْعَتَيْنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ الْفَرِيضَةِ، ثُمَّ لِيَقُلْ اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَسْتَخِيرُكَ بِعِلْمِكَ، وَاسْتَقْدِرُكَ بِقُدْرَتِكَ، وَأَسْأَلُكَ مِنْ فَضْلِكَ الْعَظِيمِ، فَإِنَّكَ تَقْدِرُ وَلا أَقْدِرُ، وَتَعْلَمُ وَلَا أَعْلَمُ، وَأَنْتَ عَلامُ الْغُيُوبِ، اللَّهُمَّ إِنْ كُنْتَ تَعْلَمُ أَنَّ هَذَا الأَمْرَ خَيْرٌ لِي فِي دِينِي وَمَعَاشِي وَعَاقِبَةِ أَمْرِي - أَوْ قَالَ عَاجِلِ أمْرِي وَآجِلِهِ - فَاقْدُرْهُ لِي وَيَسِّرْهُ لِي، ثُمَّ بَارِكْ لِي فِيهِ، وَإِنْ كُنْتَ تَعْلَمُ أَنَّ هَذَا الْأَمْرَ شَرٌّ لِي فِي دِينِي وَمَعَاشِي وَعَاقِبَةِ أَمْرِي - أَوْ قَالَ عَاجِلَ أمْرِي وَآجِلِهِ - فَاصْرِفْهُ عَنِّي وَاصْرِفْنِي عَنْهُ وَاقْدُرْ لِي الْخَيْرَ حَيْثُ كَانَ، ثُمَّ رْضِنِي بِهِ، قَالَ: وَيُسَمِّي حَاجَتَهُ ) رواه الجماعة إلا مسلماً، وينبغي أن يجمـع بـيـن الـروايـتـيـن فيقول: وعاقبة أمري وعاجله وآجله، والاستخارة في الحج والجهاد وجميع أبواب الخير، تحمل على تعيين الوقت لا على نفس الفعل، وإذا استخار مضى لما ينشرح له صدره، وينبغي أن يكررهــا سبع مرات؛ لما روى ابن السني عن أنس قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( يا أنس إِذَا هَمَمْتَ بِأَمْرِ فَاسْتَخِر رَبَّكَ فِيهِ سَبْعَ مَرَّاتٍ، ثُمَّ انْظُر إلى الذي يسبق إلى قلبك فإنَّ الخير فِيهِ ).
And (Salat al-Istikhara) is recommended, and the Sunnah has clearly explained it. Jabir said: The Messenger of Allah used to teach us Istikhara in all matters as he taught us a surah of the Quran, saying: 'When one of you is concerned about a matter, let him pray two rak'ahs other than the obligatory prayers, then say: O Allah, I seek Your guidance through Your knowledge, and I seek Your power through Your power, and I ask You from Your great bounty, for You have power and I have none, and You know and I know not, and You are the Knower of the unseen. O Allah, if You know that this matter is good for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair (or: in the immediate and future of my affair), then decree it for me and make it easy for me, then bless me in it; and if You know that this matter is evil for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair (or: in the immediate and future of my affair), then turn it away from me and turn me away from it, and decree for me good wherever it be, then make me satisfied with it.' He said: 'And he should name his need.' (Narrated by al-Jama'ah except Muslim). And one should combine both narrations and say: 'and the outcome of my affair, its immediate and future.' Istikhara for Hajj, Jihad, and all doors of good is to be understood as determining the timing, not the action itself. When one makes Istikhara, he should proceed with what his heart becomes open to. And he should repeat it seven times due to what Ibn al-Sunni narrated from Anas: the Messenger of Allah said: 'O Anas, when you intend a matter, ask your Lord for guidance in it seven times, then look at what comes first to your heart, for goodness lies in it.'
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling and complete method for Salat al-Istikhara (prayer for seeking guidance). It is recommended (mandub) when a person is uncertain about a decision. The hadith from Jabir (agreed upon except Muslim) details the prayer: two rak'ahs (non-obligatory) followed by a specific supplication. The supplication asks Allah to choose what is good for one's religion, livelihood, and end. There are variant wordings; the author recommends combining 'in the outcome of my affair, immediate and future.' The text clarifies that for obligatory acts like Hajj and Jihad, Istikhara is about the timing, not whether to do them. After Istikhara, one should act on whatever their heart inclines towards (sharh al-sadr). Additionally, repeating the Istikhara seven times is recommended, based on a hadith from Ibn al-Sunni. In the Hanafi school, this prayer is considered mustahabb (recommended) and part of the established sunnah.

Key Terms
الاستخارة (al-istikhara): Seeking guidance from Allah about a matter through prayer and supplication.
انشراح الصدر (inshirah al-sadr): Expansion of the chest; a feeling of ease and openness toward a decision after Istikhara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should one do after performing Istikhara according to the text?
A) Wait for a dream
B) Consult a scholar
C) Proceed with what the heart becomes open to
D) Repeat the prayer indefinitely

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Istikhara is a recommended two-rak'ah prayer with a specific supplication; after performing it, act on what your heart is inclined to, not waiting for a dream.

Salah — Prayer

Salat al-Hajah: Prayer for Need
Ruling and method of Salat al-Hajah with dua

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Hajah and explain the evidence and its strength within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Salat al-Hajah is a recommended prayer for any need, supported by a weak hadith but accepted by Hanafi scholars.

This lesson introduces Salat al-Hajah, a prayer taught by the Prophet for when a Muslim has a specific need. We will examine its ruling, the evidence from hadith, and the Hanafi position on its weakness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that Salat al-Hajah is a two-rak'ah prayer performed after wudu when one has a need. The text states 'it is recommended' (nudiba).
The ruling in Hanafi fiqh is sunnah ghayr muakkadah (non-emphasized recommended).
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The primary evidence is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa, narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Tirmidhi, which al-Tirmidhi considered weak.
A second hadith from Uthman ibn Hunayf about a blind man also supports the practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the evidence proves the ruling)
The hadith contains commands: 'let him perform wudu... then pray two rak'ahs... then say...'. In Hanafi usul, a command indicates recommendation (nadb) unless there is evidence for obligation. The weakness of the hadith reduces the strength of the command.
Hanafi scholars consider the hadith sufficient for mustahabb but not for fard or wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Some scholars (including al-Tirmidhi) weaken the hadith and thus minimize the emphasis; others accept it as a virtuous act.
The Hanafi school accepts it as recommended (mustahabb) based on the strength of the practice and supporting narrations.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (preferred view)
Later Hanafi fatwa manuals include Salat al-Hajah as a recommended prayer. The mufta bihi is that one may pray it with the mentioned du'a.
The ruling reflects a balance between hadith weakness and established practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونُدِبَ (صَلاةُ الحاجة) وهي ركعتان. عن عبد الله بن أبي أوفى قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ حَاجَةٌ إِلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى، أوْ إِلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْ بَنِي آدَمَ، فَلْيَتَوَضًا وَلْيُحْسِن الوُضُوءَ، ثُمَّ لَيُصَلِّ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ لِيُثْن عَلَى الله وَلْيُصَلِّ عَلَى النبي ، ثُمَّ لِيَقُلْ: لا إِلَهَ إِلا اللَّهُ الْحَلِيمُ الْكَرِيمُ، سُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَرْشِ الْعَظِيمِ، الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ، أَسْأَلُكَ مُوجِبَاتِ رَحْمَتِكَ، وَعَزَائِمَ مَغْفِرَتِكَ، وَالْغَنِيمَةَ مِنْ كُلِّ بِرُ، وَالسَّلَامَةَ مِنْ كُلِّ إِثْمٍ، لَا تَدَعَ لِي ذَنْبًا إِلَّا غَفَرْتَهُ، وَلَا هَمَّا إِلا فَرَّجْتَهُ، وَلا حَاجَةٌ لَكَ فِيْهَا رِضًا إِلَّا قَضَيْتَهَا يَـا أرْحَمَ الرَّاحِمِينَ ) (۳) رواه ابن ماجه والترمذي وضعفه، وعن عثمان بن حنيف: « أَنَّ رَجُلاً ضَرِيرَ البَصَرِ أتى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: ادْعُ الله تَعَالَى أنْ يُعَافِيَنِي فَقالَ: إِنْ شِئْتَ دَعَوْتَ ، وإِنْ شِئْتَ صَبَرْتَ فَهُوَ خَيْرٌ لَكَ قال: فَادْعُهُ، فَأَمَرَهُ أَن يَتَوَضَّأَ فَيُحْسِنَ وُضُوءَهُ ويدعُوهُ بهذا الدعاء: اللهم إنِّي أَسْأَلُكَ، وَأَتَوَجَّهُ إِليكَ
And (Salat al-Hajah) is recommended, and it is two rak'ahs. From Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has a need from Allah or from any of the children of Adam, let him perform wudu and do it well, then pray two rak'ahs, then praise Allah and send blessings upon the Prophet, then say: There is no god but Allah, the Forbearing, the Generous. Glory be to Allah, Lord of the Great Throne. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. I ask You for the causes of Your mercy and the determinations of Your forgiveness, and the gain from every righteous deed, and safety from every sin. Do not leave any sin of mine unforgiven, nor any worry except that You relieve it, nor any need in which You are pleased except that You fulfill it, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' (Narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Tirmidhi, and he weakened it). And from Uthman ibn Hunayf: a blind man came to the Prophet and said: ask Allah to cure me. He said: If you wish, I will pray, and if you wish to be patient, that is better for you. He said: then pray. So he commanded him to perform wudu well and supplicate with this du'a: 'O Allah, I ask You and I turn to You...'
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for Salat al-Hajah (prayer for need). It is recommended (mandub) when a person has a need from Allah or others. The prayer is two rak'ahs preceded by wudu. After prayer, one praises Allah, sends blessings on the Prophet, and recites a specific supplication asking for mercy, forgiveness, and fulfillment of needs. The hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa (narrated by Ibn Majah and Tirmidhi, though Tirmidhi considered it weak) provides the wording. Another hadith from Uthman ibn Hunayf (related to the incident of the blind man) shows the Prophet teaching a similar practice, indicating the legitimacy of such prayers. In Hanafi fiqh, this prayer is considered mustahabb, and the du'a is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
صلاة الحاجة (salat al-hajah): A two-rak'ah prayer performed when one has a specific need, followed by a supplication.
نُدِبَ (nudiba): It is recommended (mandub).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Perform wudu
C) Give charity
D) Recite Quran

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Hajah is a recommended prayer (mustahabb) for any need, preceded by wudu and followed by a specific supplication, and is accepted despite the weak hadith.
