The Ruling and Method of Salat al-Hajah
States the recommended status and method of Hajah prayer with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Hajah and describe its prescribed method including the evidence.

Core Idea
Salat al-Hajah is a recommended two-rak'ah prayer for urgent needs, proven by two hadiths—one weak, one hasan—accepted by the Hanafi school.

In this lesson, we examine the status of Salat al-Hajah (prayer for need). While some consider the primary hadith weak, the Hanafi school upholds its recommendation due to a second stronger narration and established practice. We will explore the ruling, the method, and the reasoning behind the school's acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Salat al-Hajah; the ruling is mandub (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) per the text 'undub'.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths: first from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa (weak per Tirmidhi), second from Uthman ibn Hunayf (hasan sahih per Tirmidhi).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فليتوضا وليحسن الوضوء ثم ليصل ركعتين' indicates recommendation for fulfilling needs through prayer.
In Hanafi usul, commands after prohibitions or in encouragement are for nadb.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars reject due to weakness of first hadith; Hanafis rely on second stronger hadith and istihsan.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The school prefers the practice based on the hasan hadith and acceptance by later scholars like the author of Sharh al-Munyah.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندب صلاة الحاجة وهي ركعتان. عن عبد الله بن أبي أوفى قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ حَاجَةٌ إِلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى، أوْ إِلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْ بَنِي آدَمَ، فَلْيَتَوَضًا وَلْيُحْسِن الوُضُوءَ، ثُمَّ لَيُصَلِّ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ لِيُثْن عَلَى الله وَلْيُصَلِّ عَلَى النبي ، ثُمَّ لِيَقُلْ: لا إِلَهَ إِلا اللَّهُ الْحَلِيمُ الْكَرِيمُ، سُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَرْشِ الْعَظِيمِ، الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ، أَسْأَلُكَ مُوجِبَاتِ رَحْمَتِكَ، وَعَزَائِمَ مَغْفِرَتِكَ، وَالْغَنِيمَةَ مِنْ كُلِّ بِرُ، وَالسَّلَامَةَ مِنْ كُلِّ إِثْمٍ، لَا تَدَعَ لِي ذَنْبًا إِلَّا غَفَرْتَهُ، وَلَا هَمَّا إِلا فَرَّجْتَهُ، وَلا حَاجَةٌ لَكَ فِيْهَا رِضًا إِلَّا قَضَيْتَهَا يَـا أرْحَمَ الرَّاحِمِينَ ) رواه ابن ماجه والترمذي وضعفه، وعن عثمان بن حنيف: « أَنَّ رَجُلاً ضَرِيرَ البَصَرِ أتى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: ادْعُ الله تَعَالَى أنْ يُعَافِيَنِي فَقالَ: إِنْ شِئْتَ دَعَوْتَ ، وإِنْ شِئْتَ صَبَرْتَ فَهُوَ خَيْرٌ لَكَ قال: فَادْعُهُ، فَأَمَرَهُ أَن يَتَوَضَّأَ فَيُحْسِنَ وُضُوءَهُ ويدعُوهُ بهذا الدعاء: اللهم إنِّي أَسْأَلُكَ، وَأَتَوَجَّهُ إِليكَ بِنَبِيِّكَ مُحَمَّدٍ نبي الرَّحْمَةِ ، يا محمد إنِّي تَوَجَّهْتُ بِكَ إِلى رَبِّكَ في حَاجَتِي هَذِهِ لتُقْضَى لِي، اللهم نَشَفَعْهُ في ) قال الترمذي: حسن صحيح، كذا في شرح المنية.
And is recommended the prayer of need, and it is two rak'ahs. From Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has a need from Allah or from any human being, let him perform wudu and do it well, then pray two rak'ahs, then praise Allah and send blessings on the Prophet, then say: There is no god but Allah, the Forbearing, the Generous. Glory be to Allah, Lord of the Great Throne. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. I ask You for the means of Your mercy and the firm resolution of Your forgiveness, and the spoils of every good, and safety from every sin. Do not leave any sin of mine without forgiving it, nor any worry without relieving it, nor any need in which there is Your pleasure without fulfilling it, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' Reported by Ibn Majah and al-Tirmidhi, and he declared it weak. And from Uthman ibn Hunayf: 'A blind man came to the Prophet and said: Pray to Allah to cure me. He said: If you wish, I will pray, and if you wish, be patient, that is better for you. He said: Then pray. So he ordered him to perform wudu and do it well, and to pray with this supplication: O Allah, I ask You and I turn to You through Your Prophet Muhammad, the Prophet of mercy. O Muhammad, I turn through you to your Lord for this need of mine so that it may be fulfilled. O Allah, accept his intercession for me.' Al-Tirmidhi said: Hasan Sahih. Likewise in Sharh al-Munyah.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for Salat al-Hajah (the prayer for need). The author states that this prayer is recommended (mandub) and consists of two rak'ahs. He then provides two hadiths as evidence. The first hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa is narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Tirmidhi, though al-Tirmidhi declared it weak. It details the procedure: perform wudu properly, pray two rak'ahs, praise Allah and send blessings on the Prophet, then recite the supplication. The second hadith from Uthman ibn Hunayf is considered hasan sahih by al-Tirmidhi. It is the famous story of the blind man who was instructed to perform wudu and recite a specific supplication that is similar to the first. The author notes that this ruling is also in Sharh al-Munyah. The Hanafi school considers this prayer recommended, though some may consider the first hadith weak; the practice is supported by the second stronger hadith and general principles.

Key Terms
صلاة الحاجة (ṣalāt al-ḥājah): A prayer of two rak'ahs performed with the intention of asking Allah to fulfill a specific need.
التفريق (al-tafrīq): Not present in this passage.

Seeking Laylat al-Qadr: The Hanafi Internal Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Laylat al-Qadr with dalil naqli

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three reported Hanafi positions on Laylat al-Qadr and state the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for seeking it.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice of reviving the last ten nights is clear, but the exact night of Laylat al-Qadr remains a subject of internal Hanafi debate.

The text opens by emphasizing the strong recommendation (sunnah muakkadah) to revive the last ten nights of Ramadan, citing the Prophet's own practice. Its ultimate goal is to seek Laylat al-Qadr, whose virtue is immense. However, within the Hanafi school, there are multiple reported views on whether Laylat al-Qadr is confined to Ramadan, and if so, whether it is fixed or movable. This lesson unpacks those views and shows how the later Hanafi masters resolved the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act and its proof
The text begins by stating that reviving the last ten nights is recommended (sunnah). It provides the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's practice: when the last ten nights entered, he would stay awake, wake his family, and tighten his waist-wrapper. This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is agreed upon (Bukhari and Muslim).
2
Recognize the purpose: seeking Laylat al-Qadr
The text explains that the reason for this practice is to seek Laylat al-Qadr, which is better than a thousand months. The Quranic verse (97:3) and the hadith 'Whoever prays on Laylat al-Qadr with faith and hope for reward will have his sins forgiven' are cited.
The virtue is clear, but the exact night is debated.
3
List the three reported positions from the Hanafi school
The text reports three distinct positions: (1) Abu Hanifa in one narration: Laylat al-Qadr is not confined to Ramadan but can occur throughout the year. (2) Abu Hanifa according to al-Sarakhsi: it is in Ramadan but may advance or delay. (3) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn): it is fixed in the last ten nights of Ramadan, specifically.
These are summarized from Qadi Khan, al-Mabsut, and other sources.
4
Examine the later clarification from al-Fatawa al-Sughra
The text then cites al-Fatawa al-Sughra stating that there is no dispute among Abu Hanifa and his two companions that Laylat al-Qadr is in Ramadan. This indicates that the view confining it to Ramadan is the accepted position among the later scholars.
This resolves the apparent contradiction from the earlier narrations.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical implication
The relied-upon position is that Laylat al-Qadr is in the last ten nights of Ramadan, and it is recommended to seek it, especially on the odd nights, with the 27th being the most likely (for those unaware of the differences). The layperson is to act on the 27th, but the diligent seeker should revive all ten nights.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونُدِبَ إحياء ليالي العَشْرِ الأخير من رمضانَ)؛ لما روي عن عائشة : ( أنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ إِذَا دَخَلَ العَشْرَ الْأَخِيرَ أَحْيَا الليل، وأيقظ أهْلَهُ وَشَدَّ المِشْزَرَ ) متفق عليه، ولأحمد ومسلم ) كَانَ يَجْتَهدُ فِي العَشْرِ الأَواخِرِ مَا لَا يَجْتَهِدُ في غيره (۳) والقصد منه إحياء ليلة القدر، قال تعالى: لَيْلَةُ الْقَدْرِ خَيْرٌ مِّنْ أَلْفِ شَهْرٍ [ الفلم : : ٣] قال المفسرون: أي: قيامها والعمل فيها خير من العمل من ألف شهر خالية منها، وفي « الصحيحين»، عن أبي هريرة مرفوعاً: « مَنْ قَامَ ليلةَ القَدْرِ إِيْمَانَا وَاحْتِسَابًا غُفِرَ لَهُ مَا تَقَدَّمَ مِنْ ذَنْبِهِ ) زاد أحمد ( وَمَا تأخر » (). وقال : « تَحَرَّوْا لَيْلَةَ الْقَدْرِ فِي الْعَشْرِ الأَوَاخِرِ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ » ) متفق عليه فلذا قــال مـعـظـم الأئمة: هي مختصة بالعشر الأواخر من رمضان فتطلب فيه، وقال ابن مسعود : هي في كل السنة انتهى. وبه قال الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة في المشهور عنه ، لما قاله في ( البحر » عن «قاضي خان» أن المشهور عن أبي حنيفة أنها تدور في السنة، وقد تكون في رمضان وقد تكون في غيره، انتهى وفي المبسوط للسرخسي من الاعتكاف أن المذهب عند أبي حنيفة أنها تكون في رمضان لكن تتقدم وتتأخر، وعندهما لا تتقدم ولا تتأخر، انتهى. وفي الفتاوى الصغرى»: ليلة القدر في رمضان عندهم بلا خلاف أي عند أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، وعبارتها في الأيمان: لو ذكر أي: الحالف ليلة القدر، فإن كان لا يعرف اختلاف العلماء في ليلة القدر، فهو على ليلة السابع والعشرين من رمضان، وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث، وإن كان يعرف لا ينصرف إلى ذلك، والاختلاف فيـه معـروف
And it is recommended to revive the nights of the last ten days of Ramadan, because of what is narrated from Aisha that the Prophet, when the last ten days entered, would revive the night, wake his family, and tighten his waist-wrapper. Agreed upon. And in the narration of Ahmad and Muslim: He would strive in the last ten days as he would not strive in others. The purpose of that is to revive Laylat al-Qadr. Allah says: 'The Night of Decree is better than a thousand months.' The commentators said: meaning standing in prayer and working in it is better than working in a thousand months devoid of it. In the two Sahihs, from Abu Hurairah marfu'an: 'Whoever stands (in prayer) on Laylat al-Qadr with faith and hope for reward, his previous sins will be forgiven.' Ahmad added: 'and what is to come.' And he said: 'Seek Laylat al-Qadr in the last ten days of Ramadan.' Agreed upon. Therefore, most of the imams said: It is specific to the last ten days of Ramadan, so it is sought therein. Ibn Mas'ud said: It is in every year. End. And the great Imam Abu Hanifa in the famous report from him said that, as mentioned in al-Bahr from Qadi Khan, that the famous view from Abu Hanifa is that it revolves throughout the year, and it may be in Ramadan or outside it. End. In al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi on i'tikaf: The madhhab according to Abu Hanifa is that it occurs in Ramadan but it may be earlier or later, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it does not advance or delay. End. In al-Fatawa al-Sughra: Laylat al-Qadr is in Ramadan according to them without dispute, i.e., Abu Hanifa and his two companions. Its wording in al-Ayman: If someone swears about Laylat al-Qadr, and he is unaware of the scholars' difference on it, then it refers to the twenty-seventh night of Ramadan, and this is the view adopted by Faqih Abu al-Layth. If he is aware, then it does not refer to that, and the difference on it is well-known.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and includes an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author first states that it is recommended to revive the last ten nights of Ramadan, citing the famous hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's practice. The purpose is to seek Laylat al-Qadr. Quranic verses and hadith emphasize its virtue. The author then reports the consensus of most imams that Laylat al-Qadr is in the last ten nights of Ramadan. However, he mentions a difference: Ibn Mas'ud said it could be throughout the year. He then attributes to Imam Abu Hanifa the view that it is not confined to Ramadan (possibly from Qadi Khan). But then he also cites al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi where Abu Hanifa says it is in Ramadan but may shift, while his two companions say it is fixed. Finally, from al-Fatawa al-Sughra, there is no dispute among Abu Hanifa and his companions that it is in Ramadan, and for practical purposes, it is often taken as the 27th night for those unaware of the differences. The author presents these varying reports without definitively resolving them, showing the complexity of the issue within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
إحياء الليل (iḥyā' al-layl): Spending the night in worship, such as prayer, dhikr, and recitation of Quran.
ليلة القدر (laylat al-qadr): The Night of Decree, a night in Ramadan better than a thousand months.
شَدَّ المِشْزَرَ (shadda al-mizr): Tightened his waist-wrapper, a metaphor for exerting oneself in worship and avoiding marital relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) regarding Laylat al-Qadr?
A) It could be any night of the year
B) It is in the last ten nights of Ramadan
C) It is exclusively the 27th night
D) It is only in Sha'ban

Key Takeaway
Seek Laylat al-Qadr in the last ten nights of Ramadan, especially the odd, as this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

The Recommendation to Revive the Last Ten Nights of Ramadan
Ruling with proof for reviving last ten nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for reviving the last ten nights of Ramadan and identify the Quranic and Hadith proofs that establish this recommendation.

Core Idea
Reviving the last ten nights is a strongly recommended sunnah to seek Laylat al-Qadr.

The Hanafi school places great emphasis on the last ten nights of Ramadan, urging believers to intensify worship. This lesson examines the legal ruling and its primary textual evidence, showing why this practice is not merely optional but a cherished sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the key phrase 'نُدِبَ إحياء ليالي العشر الأخير' in the Arabic text. This tells you the ruling: it is 'nudiba' (recommended). In Hanafi fiqh, this falls under sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended).
The verb 'nudiba' is used for recommended acts; it is not wajib.
2
Recognize the primary hadith proof
The text cites the hadith from Aisha (رضي الله عنها) describing the Prophet's practice: raising his waist-wrapper, staying awake, and waking his family. This is the main dalil for the recommendation.
The hadith is 'متفق عليه' (agreed upon) — found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the purpose: Laylat al-Qadr
The commentator states: 'والقصد منه إحياء ليلة القدر' — the purpose of reviving these nights is to seek Laylat al-Qadr. This connects the act to the greater reward promised for that night.
The Quranic verse (97:3) is quoted: ليلة القدر خير من ألف شهر.
4
Note the supporting proofs
The text adds another hadith from Ahmad and Muslim emphasizing the Prophet's extra effort, and the famous hadith on Laylat al-Qadr's merit: 'من قام ليلة القدر إيماناً واحتساباً غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه'. These reinforce the recommendation.
The hadith on Laylat al-Qadr is also in Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Conclude the ruling
All proofs point to the same conclusion: it is a meritorious sunnah to revive these nights, especially for the purpose of encountering Laylat al-Qadr.
This ruling is undisputed among the Hanafi imams, though the exact night varies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونُدِبَ إحياء ليالي العَشْرِ الأخير من رمضان؛ لما روي عن عائشة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا دخل العشر الأخر أحيا الليل وأيقظ أهله وشد المئزر متفق عليه. ولأحمد ومسلم: كان يجتهد في العشر الأواخر ما لا يجتهد في غيره. والقصد منه إحياء ليلة القدر. قال تعالى: ليلة القدر خير من ألف شهر. قال المفسرون: أي قيامها والعمل فيها خير من العمل من ألف شهر خالية منها. وفي الصحيحين عن أبي هريرة مرفوعاً: من قام ليلة القدر إيماناً واحتساباً غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه. زاد أحمد: وما تأخر. وقال: تحروا ليلة القدر في العشر الأواخر من رمضان متفق عليه. فلذا قال معظم الأئمة: هي مختصة بالعشر الأواخر من رمضان فتطلب فيه. وقال ابن مسعود: هي في كل السنة. انتهى. وبه قال الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة في المشهور عنه، لما قاله في البحر عن قاضي خان أن المشهور عن أبي حنيفة أنها تدور في السنة، وقد تكون في رمضان وقد تكون في غيره. انتهى. وفي المبسوط للسرخسي من الاعتكاف أن المذهب عند أبي حنيفة أنها تكون في رمضان لكن تتقدم وتتأخر، وعندهما لا تتقدم ولا تتأخر. انتهى. وفي الفتاوى الصغرى: ليلة القدر في رمضان عندهم بلا خلاف أي عند أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه. وعبارتها في الأيمان: لو ذكر أي الحالف ليلة القدر، فإن كان لا يعرف اختلاف العلماء في ليلة القدر، فهو على ليلة السابع والعشرين من رمضان، وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث، وإن كان يعرف لا ينصرف إلى ذلك، والاختلاف فيه معروف. عندهما أي عند أبي يوسف ومحمد إن كان الحلف في نصف شهر رمضان فيمينه إلى النصف من رمضان القابل، وعنده أي الإمام أبو حنيفة إلى أن يمضي كل ليالي رمضان القابل وعليه الفتوى. والاختلاف بناء على أن ليلة القدر في رمضان عندهم بلا خلاف، لكنه يقول: عسى تتقدم أو تتأخر، وعندهما في ليلة بعينها لا تتقدم ولا تتأخر، ولكن لا تعرف. فإذا جاء من رمضان القابل ذلك الوقت الذي حلف فيه علم أنه جاء ليلة القدر فيحنث. انتهى. وفي شرح الإقناع للحنابلة: أنها تنتقل في العشر الأخير من رمضان وليست معينة. وحكي ذلك عن الأئمة الأربعة وغيرهم. انتهى.
It is recommended to revive the last ten nights of Ramadan; because it is narrated from Aisha that when the last ten (nights) entered, the Prophet (peace be upon him) would revive the night, wake his family, and tighten his waist-wrapper. Agreed upon. And from Ahmad and Muslim: He would strive in the last ten (nights) as he did not strive in others. The intent of that is to revive Laylat al-Qadr. Allah said: Laylat al-Qadr is better than a thousand months. The commentators said: meaning standing in prayer and acting in it is better than acting in a thousand months empty of it. And in the Two Sahihs, from Abu Hurairah, raised (to the Prophet): Whoever stands (in prayer) Laylat al-Qadr with faith and hope for reward, his past sins are forgiven. Ahmad added: and his future (sins). And he (the Prophet) said: Seek Laylat al-Qadr in the last ten (nights) of Ramadan. Agreed upon. Therefore, most imams said: It is specific to the last ten nights of Ramadan, so it is sought in them. And Ibn Mas'ud said: It is throughout the entire year. End. And the Greatest Imam Abu Hanifah (held) that, according to the well-known (report) from him, as was said in al-Bahr from Qadi Khan: The well-known from Abu Hanifah is that it rotates throughout the year, and it may be in Ramadan or in other than it. End. And in al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi, from the chapter on i'tikaf: The madhhab according to Abu Hanifah is that it is in Ramadan, but it may come early or late; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it neither comes early nor late. End. And in al-Fatawa al-Sughra: Laylat al-Qadr is in Ramadan according to them without dispute, i.e., according to Abu Hanifah and his two companions. And its expression in the chapter on oaths: If (the swearer) mentions Laylat al-Qadr, then if he does not know the difference of scholars about Laylat al-Qadr, it applies to the night of the 27th of Ramadan, and this is what Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted; and if he knows, it does not refer to that, and the difference about it is known. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if the oath is made in the middle of Ramadan, his oath applies to the middle of the next Ramadan; and according to him (Imam Abu Hanifah), it applies until all the nights of the next Ramadan have passed, and upon that is the fatwa. The difference is based on the fact that Laylat al-Qadr is in Ramadan according to them without dispute, but he says: it may come early or late, while according to them it is on a specific night that neither comes early nor late, but it is not known. So when from the next Ramadan that time in which he swore comes, he knows that Laylat al-Qadr has come, and he breaks his oath. End. And in Sharh al-Iqna' of the Hanbalis: It moves within the last ten nights of Ramadan and is not fixed. And this has been related from the four imams and others. End.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Imdad al-Fattah, expanding upon the matn of Nur al-Idah which states: 'It is recommended to revive the last ten nights of Ramadan.' The commentator begins by citing the hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would intensify worship in the last ten days. This is the primary proof for the recommendation. The passage then clarifies that the purpose of this revival is to seek Laylat al-Qadr, supported by the Qur'anic verse 'Laylat al-Qadr is better than a thousand months' and the hadith 'Whoever stands in prayer on Laylat al-Qadr with faith and hope...'. The text then notes that most imams hold that Laylat al-Qadr is specific to the last ten nights of Ramadan. However, a significant portion is dedicated to the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its exact timing. The well-known (mashhur) view of Imam Abu Hanifa is that Laylat al-Qadr rotates throughout the year and may occur even outside Ramadan. This is opposed by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) who hold that it is definitely in Ramadan, on an unspecified night that does not move. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa that it is in Ramadan but may shift. The text further cites the Fatawa al-Sughra affirming that all three agree it is in Ramadan, but the difference emerges in the context of oaths: if someone swears an oath involving Laylat al-Qadr, the ruling on when the oath is fulfilled differs. The fatwa is given on Abu Hanifa's view regarding the oath. The passage concludes by noting that even the Hanbalis hold that it moves within the last ten nights. Thus, while the ruling to revive the last ten nights is undisputed, the precise night of Laylat al-Qadr remains a matter of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, with the practical fatwa often referencing the 27th night for those unaware of the dispute.

Key Terms
إحياء (ihya): To stay awake during the night engaging in worship (prayer, dhikr, recitation of Quran) as a recommended act.
ليلة القدر (Laylat al-Qadr): The Night of Decree, a blessed night in Ramadan in which the Quran was revealed and worship is better than a thousand months.
العشر الأواخر (al-ashr al-awakhir): The last ten nights of Ramadan, counted from the 21st night onwards, following the Islamic calendar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary purpose of reviving the last ten nights?
A) To complete the Quran.
B) To seek Laylat al-Qadr.
C) To make up missed fasts.
D) To prepare for Eid.

Key Takeaway
Reviving the last ten nights is a strongly recommended sunnah, proven by the Prophet's practice and the promise of Laylat al-Qadr.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Laylat al-Qadr and Its Effect on Oaths
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Laylat al-Qadr timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the timing of Laylat al-Qadr and apply the ruling to a case of an oath involving Laylat al-Qadr.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa holds Laylat al-Qadr rotates; the Sahibayn hold it is fixed; the fatwa follows Abu Hanifa for oaths.

While all Hanafi imams agree Laylat al-Qadr is in Ramadan, they differ on whether it moves or is fixed. This subtle difference has a real consequence: how an oath involving Laylat al-Qadr is fulfilled. The text presents the views and settles on Abu Hanifa's position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of ikhtilaf
The dispute is about the nature of Laylat al-Qadr: does it rotate throughout the year or is it fixed within Ramadan? Abu Hanifa reportedly holds it can occur even outside Ramadan, while a narration says it is in Ramadan but shifts. The Sahibayn hold it is a specific unknown night that does not move.
The text quotes from al-Bahr and al-Mabsut to clarify the narrations.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
The well-known (mashhur) view of Abu Hanifa is that Laylat al-Qadr rotates throughout the year, possibly in Ramadan or other months. Another narration puts it in Ramadan but allows advancement or delay.
This is attributed to Qadi Khan in al-Bahr and to al-Sarakhsi in al-Mabsut.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that Laylat al-Qadr is definitely in Ramadan, on a specific night that neither moves nor changes, but its exact identity is unknown.
They agree it is in Ramadan but differ from Abu Hanifa on fixity.
4
Understand the practical consequence: oaths
If someone swears an oath concerning Laylat al-Qadr, the duration of the oath differs. According to Abu Hanifa, the oath extends until all nights of the next Ramadan have passed. According to the Sahibayn, if the oath is made in the middle of Ramadan, it applies to the middle of the next Ramadan.
The text explicitly states 'وعليه الفتوى' for Abu Hanifa's view in oaths.
5
Note the mufta bihi
In the context of oaths, the fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view. For the common person unaware of the dispute, the practice of seeking the 27th night is recommended.
This is from al-Fatawa al-Sughra and the text.

Reviving the Two Eid Nights
States the recommendation and provides the hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommendation to revive the two Eid nights and cite the hadith proof from al-Daraqutni.

Core Idea
Reviving the Eid night earns divine protection on the Day of Judgment.

The night before Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha are blessed times for worship. This lesson covers the strong recommendation to spend these nights in devotion and the prophetic promise for doing so.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text uses 'nudiba' (it is recommended) for reviving the two Eid nights. Determine the hukm level (mustahabb/sunnah).
Hanafi school: this is sunnah muakkadah, a strongly recommended act.
2
Cite the dalil
The proof is a hadith reported by al-Daraqutni: 'Whoever revives the night of Eid, Allah will revive his heart on the day when hearts die.'
The hadith is a sahih (sound) hadith, though mursal? It is considered acceptable for fada'il al-a'mal.
3
Understand the meaning of 'ihya'
Reviving the night means spending it in worship—prayer, dhikr, Qur'an, and other acts of obedience from maghrib to fajr.
It is not limited to prayer; any good deed counts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإحياءُ لَيْلَتَي العيدين: الفطر والأضحى لحديث: ( من أحيا ليلة العيد أحيى الله قلبه يوم تموت القلوب ) رواه الدارقطني. ويستحب الاستغفار بالسحر والإكثار منه لقوله تعالى: ﴿وبالأسحار هم يستغفرون﴾ وسيد الاستغفار: اللهم أنت ربي لا إله إلا أنت خلقتني وأنا عبدك، وأنا على عهدك ووعدك ما استطعت أعوذ بك من شر ما صنعت، أبوء لك بنعمتك علي وأبوء بذنبي، فاغفر لي فإنه لا يغفر الذنوب إلا أنت. والدعاء فيها مستجاب.
And (it is recommended) to revive the two nights of the two Eids: al-Fitr and al-Adha, due to the hadith: 'Whoever revives the night of Eid, Allah will revive his heart on the day when hearts die.' Reported by al-Daraqutni. And istighfar is recommended at dawn (sahar) and doing much of it, because of Allah's saying: 'And at dawn they seek forgiveness.' And the sayyid al-istighfar (the master of seeking forgiveness) is: 'O Allah, You are my Lord, there is no god but You, You created me and I am Your servant, and I am upon Your covenant and promise as much as I am able. I seek refuge in You from the evil of what I have done. I acknowledge before You Your favour upon me and I acknowledge my sin, so forgive me, for none forgives sins except You.' And supplication in them (these nights) is answered.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage continues the section on recommended acts of worship. The commentator presents two distinct recommendations. First, reviving the two Eid nights (the night before Eid al-Fitr and the night before Eid al-Adha) is a sunnah act supported by the hadith reported by al-Daraqutni: 'Whoever revives the night of Eid, Allah will revive his heart on the day when hearts die.' This indicates that such a person will be protected from the terror of the Day of Judgment. Second, it is recommended (mustahabb) to engage in istighfar (seeking forgiveness) during the sahur (dawn) time, based on the Qur'anic verse describing the righteous: 'And at dawn they seek forgiveness.' The passage then quotes the sayyid al-istighfar, a comprehensive supplication taught by the Prophet (peace be upon him). The text concludes by noting that supplication (du'a) is answered during these nights (likely referring to the Eid nights and the last ten nights previously mentioned, as the pronoun 'fiha' connects to the context).

Key Terms
إحياء ليلة العيد (ihya laylat al-Eid): Spending the night of Eid in worship (prayer, dhikr, etc.) from maghrib to fajr.

Seeking Forgiveness at Dawn and Sayyid al-Istighfar
States the recommendation of istighfar at dawn with Qur'an proof, and presents sayyid al-istighfar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended time for istighfar and recite sayyid al-istighfar with understanding of its meaning and virtue.

Core Idea
Dawn is a time for forgiveness; the best supplication acknowledges Allah's favor and one's own sin.

This lesson focuses on the dawn period (sahar) as a time for seeking forgiveness, a practice of the righteous. It includes the prophetic formula known as sayyid al-istighfar and notes that supplications are accepted at this hour.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time and act
The text recommends istighfar at 'sahar' (the last part of the night before fajr). Determine the hukm (mustahabb) and the time.
Sahar is specifically the pre-dawn time, including tahajjud and du'a.
2
Cite the Qur'anic proof
The verse 'And at dawn they seek forgiveness' (Surah adh-Dhariyat 51:18) is used as evidence. Understand how it proves recommendation.
The verse describes the righteous; their actions imply desirability for the ummah.
3
Memorize and understand sayyid al-istighfar
The text provides the full wording. Break down its meaning: acknowledgement of Allah's lordship, servitude, covenant, seeking refuge, confession of sin, and asking for forgiveness.
This is considered the 'master of supplications' due to its comprehensive nature.
4
Note the acceptance of du'a
The passage concludes that 'supplication in them is answered'—referring to these blessed times.
This applies to the last part of the night and possibly to the Eid nights.

Source Text

وإحياءُ لَيْلَتَي العيدين: الفطر والأضحى لحديث: ( من أحيا ليلة العيد أحيى الله قلبه يوم تموت القلوب ) رواه الدارقطني. ويستحب الاستغفار بالسحر والإكثار منه لقوله تعالى: ﴿وبالأسحار هم يستغفرون﴾ وسيد الاستغفار: اللهم أنت ربي لا إله إلا أنت خلقتني وأنا عبدك، وأنا على عهدك ووعدك ما استطعت أعوذ بك من شر ما صنعت، أبوء لك بنعمتك علي وأبوء بذنبي، فاغفر لي فإنه لا يغفر الذنوب إلا أنت. والدعاء فيها مستجاب.
And (it is recommended) to revive the two nights of the two Eids: al-Fitr and al-Adha, due to the hadith: 'Whoever revives the night of Eid, Allah will revive his heart on the day when hearts die.' Reported by al-Daraqutni. And istighfar is recommended at dawn (sahar) and doing much of it, because of Allah's saying: 'And at dawn they seek forgiveness.' And the sayyid al-istighfar (the master of seeking forgiveness) is: 'O Allah, You are my Lord, there is no god but You, You created me and I am Your servant, and I am upon Your covenant and promise as much as I am able. I seek refuge in You from the evil of what I have done. I acknowledge before You Your favour upon me and I acknowledge my sin, so forgive me, for none forgives sins except You.' And supplication in them (these nights) is answered.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage continues the section on recommended acts of worship. The commentator presents two distinct recommendations. First, reviving the two Eid nights (the night before Eid al-Fitr and the night before Eid al-Adha) is a sunnah act supported by the hadith reported by al-Daraqutni: 'Whoever revives the night of Eid, Allah will revive his heart on the day when hearts die.' This indicates that such a person will be protected from the terror of the Day of Judgment. Second, it is recommended (mustahabb) to engage in istighfar (seeking forgiveness) during the sahur (dawn) time, based on the Qur'anic verse describing the righteous: 'And at dawn they seek forgiveness.' The passage then quotes the sayyid al-istighfar, a comprehensive supplication taught by the Prophet (peace be upon him). The text concludes by noting that supplication (du'a) is answered during these nights (likely referring to the Eid nights and the last ten nights previously mentioned, as the pronoun 'fiha' connects to the context).

Key Terms
سيد الاستغفار (sayyid al-istighfar): The 'master of seeking forgiveness,' a specific supplication that is the most comprehensive form of istighfar.
السحر (al-sahar): The dawn period, specifically the last portion of the night before fajr.

Key Takeaway
Seeking forgiveness at dawn is a Qur'anically recommended practice, and sayyid al-istighfar is its most comprehensive form.

Reviving Recommended Nights in Worship
Listing nights for ihya with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the nights recommended for ihya in the Hanafi school and state the proofs for each.

Core Idea
Reviving specific nights is mandub; the reward includes forgiveness and a living heart on the Day of Judgment.

The Hanafi school encourages reviving certain nights through worship. This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah lists those nights with their proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding these recommendations helps you prioritize acts of worship and deepen your connection with Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Determine the legal status of reviving these nights. The text uses the term 'yustahabb' (recommended), placing them under the category of mandub (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
The ruling is not wajib; it is a virtuous act.
2
List the recommended nights
Go through the passage and extract each night mentioned: the two nights of Eid, the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah (including Tarwiyah, Arafah, Nahr), and the night of mid-Sha'ban. Also note the mention of Jumu'ah and Laylat al-Qadr, though the focus is on the former.
Each night has its own specific virtue and proof.
3
Examine the proofs for each night
For each night, locate the hadith or Quranic verse cited. Note the source (e.g., Daraqutni for Eid, Tirmidhi for ten days, etc.) and the promised reward.
The proofs vary in strength; all are ahad hadith with zanni thubut.
4
Note any exceptions or additional details
Observe the comment on fasting the day of Arafah for pilgrims: it is disliked due to the need for strength. This shows that recommendations can be modified by circumstances.
This exception does not negate the virtue of the night itself.
5
Summarize the intended practice
Conclude that reviving these nights means engaging in prayer (qiyam), dhikr, du'a, and seeking forgiveness. The goal is to earn the rewards mentioned and avoid having a dead heart.
The hadith 'his heart will not die' is interpreted as protection from love of this world.

وَجَلَّ يَنْزِلُ فِيهَا لِغُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَيَقُولُ: أَلا مِنْ مُسْتَغْفِرِ لِي فَأَغْفِرَ لَهُ، أَلا مُسْتَرْزِقٌ فَأَرْزُقَهُ، حَتَّى يَطْلُعَ الْفَجْرُ ) وروى الحافظ أبو نعيم، عن فيهِنَّ الجَزِيلَ: ليلةُ القَدْرِ وصَبَاحَهَا، وليلةُ النَّصْفِ مِنْ شَعْبَانَ ، وصَبَاحُها، وليلةُ عَرَفة وصَبَاحُهَا وَلَيْلَةُ الجُمُعَةِ وَصَبَاحُهَا » (). وروى الأصفهاني في ( الترغيب» عن معاذ بن (And) it is recommended to revive the two nights of the two Eids: Fitr and Adha, because of the hadith: 'Whoever revives the night of Eid, Allah will revive his heart on the day when hearts die' related by al-Daraqutni. And seeking forgiveness at dawn and doing it abundantly is recommended because of His statement: 'And in the dawns they seek forgiveness' [51:18]. And the master of seeking forgiveness is: 'O Allah, You are my Lord, there is no deity but You, You created me and I am Your servant, and I am upon Your covenant and promise as much as I am able. I seek refuge in You from the evil I have done. I acknowledge Your favor upon me and I acknowledge my sin, so forgive me, for none forgives sins but You.' And supplication in them is answered, as we will mention if Allah wills. (And) it is recommended to revive the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah because of his saying: 'There are no days more beloved to Allah that He be worshipped in them than the ten days of Dhul Hijjah. Fasting each day of them equals the fasting of a year, and standing in prayer each night of them equals standing in the Night of Qadr.' Related by al-Tirmidhi and others. And in Sahih Ibn Hibban from Jabir raised to the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There are no days more virtuous before Allah than the days of Dhul Hijjah.' And from Abu Qatada: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Fasting the day of Arafah expiates two years: past and future, and fasting Ashura expiates one past year.' Related by the group except al-Bukhari and al-Tirmidhi. And from Abu Hurayra: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade fasting on the day of Arafah at Arafat.' Related by Ahmad and Ibn Majah. The meaning is so that the pilgrim can devote himself to standing with energy and strength, but fasting would weaken him, so it is disliked for him. (And) it is recommended to revive the night of the middle of Sha'ban because it expiates the sins of the year, and the night of Friday expiates the sins of the week, and the Night of Qadr expiates the sins of a lifetime, mentioned by al-Taqi al-Subki in his tafsir. And because it is a night in which provisions and lifespans are decreed, and enrichment and impoverishment, and honor and humiliation, and life and death, and the number of pilgrims. And from Aisha: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Allah pours out goodness in four nights abundantly.' He mentioned among them: 'The night of the middle of Sha'ban.' And because it is the night of response, as narrated from Ibn Umar: 'Five nights in which supplication is not rejected: the night of Friday, the first night of Rajab, the night of the middle of Sha'ban, and the two nights of Eid.' And Abd al-Razzaq narrated from Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When it is the night of the middle of Sha'ban, stand in prayer during its night and fast its day, for Allah, Mighty and Majestic, descends at sunset to the heaven and says: Is there anyone seeking forgiveness so I forgive him? Is there anyone seeking provision so I provide him? Until dawn breaks.' And al-Hafiz Abu Nuaym narrated from Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Four nights, their nights are like their days and their days are like their nights: Allah fulfills oaths in them, frees souls in them, and gives abundantly in them: the Night of Qadr and its morning, the night of the middle of Sha'ban and its morning, the night of Arafah and its morning, and the night of Friday and its morning.' And al-Isfahani narrated in al-Targhib from Muadh ibn Jabal: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever revives the five nights, Paradise becomes obligatory for him: the night of Tarwiyah, the night of Arafah, the night of Nahr, the night of Fitr, and the night of the middle of Sha'ban.' And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever stands in prayer on the night of the middle of Sha'ban and the two nights of Eid, his heart will not die on the day when hearts die.' And in another narration: 'Whoever revives the two nights of Eid and the night of the middle of Sha'ban, his heart will not die on the day when hearts die.' And the meaning of 'standing' in the hadith is standing in obedience, as Allah said: 'And stand before Allah, devoutly obedient' [2:238]. So it is a legal reality for it. And the meaning of 'his heart does not die' is that it does not die with love of this world such that it turns him away from the Hereafter, as it came: 'Do not sit with the dead,' meaning the people of this world. And some said: did not...
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage details the nights recommended for staying awake in worship (ihya). The author, commenting on the matn, lists several nights with their proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. The ruling is mandub (recommended). The nights include the two nights of Eid (Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha), the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah (including the nights of Tarwiyah, Arafah, and Nahr), and the night of mid-Sha'ban. The author also notes the night of Friday and Laylat al-Qadr as virtuous, but the main focus is on the specific nights mentioned. Proofs are provided for each night, including hadith on the virtue of reviving these nights, the rewards of forgiveness and answered supplications, and the practice of seeking forgiveness at dawn. The passage also clarifies that fasting on the day of Arafah at Arafat is discouraged for pilgrims due to the need for strength. The commentary emphasizes that the recommended practice is based on sound traditions, and the meaning of 'reviving' is engaging in acts of obedience such as prayer, dhikr, and du'a.

Key Terms
إحياء الليل (ihya al-layl): Staying awake during the night in acts of worship such as prayer, dhikr, recitation, and supplication.
ليلة العيد (laylat al-eid): The night preceding the day of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Reviving specific nights like Eid, the ten of Dhul Hijjah, and mid-Sha'ban is a recommended act with proven rewards, but not obligatory.

Dislike of Communal Night Revival in Mosques
Ruling on gathering for revival of specific nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gathering for night revival in mosques for specific nights and explain the proof from the Sunnah and the consensus of scholars.

Core Idea
Communal revival of mid-Sha'ban and Eid nights in mosques is disliked because it is an innovation not practiced by the Prophet or Companions.

The revival of certain nights, such as mid-Sha'ban and the two Eids, is a commendable act when done individually. However, gathering in congregations in mosques for this purpose has been deemed disliked by the Hanafi school and many early scholars. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the ruling, cites the proof from a hadith in Sahih Muslim, and clarifies the scholarly disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is gathering (الاجتماع) in mosques for the revival of specific nights (mid-Sha'ban, Eid nights). The ruling is disliked (makruh).
The text begins with 'ويُكره الاجتماع على إحياء ليلة من هذه الليالي'.
2
Understand the definition of 'revival'
Revival (إحياء) is defined as engaging in prayer, Quran recitation, dhikr, and sending blessings upon the Prophet, individually without a fixed number.
This individual revival is recommended; the objection is to the communal gathering.
3
Analyze the proof from the Sunnah
The hadith from Sahih Muslim is cited: whoever prays Isha and Fajr in congregation is like having stood half or the whole night in prayer. This shows that regular congregational prayers already fulfill night revival, making extra communal gatherings unnecessary.
The hadith is used to support that the Prophet's practice was sufficient.
4
Examine the scholarly disagreement and conclusion
Some later Tabi'un considered it recommended, but the majority of early scholars (especially Hijazi and the Syrian al-Awza'i) considered it disliked (innovation). The Hanafi school follows the dislike view as mufta bihi.
The text quotes al-Ghayti and mentions the two opinions among Syrian scholars.

Source Text

ويُكره الاجتماع على إحياء ليلة من هذه الليالي في المساجد. بصلاة يمت قلبه، أي: لا يتحير قلبه عند النزع، ولا في القبر، ولا في القيامة، ويحصل القيام بالصلاة نفلاً فرادى من غير عدد مخصوص وبقراءة القرآن، والأحاديث وسماعها، وبالتسبيح والثناء، وبالصلاة والسلام على النبي الله والحاصل ذلك في معظم الليل، وقيل: ساعة منه، وعن ابن عباس العشاء جماعة والعزم على صلاة الصبح جماعة، كما قالوا في إحياء ليلتي العيدين. وفي صحيح مسلم: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (من صلى العشاء في جماعة فكأنما قام نصف الليل، ومن صلى الصبح في جماعة فكأنما قام الليل كله). ويُكره الاجتماع على إحياء ليلة من هذه الليالي المتقدم ذكرها في المساجد وغيرها؛ لأنه لم يفعله النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا الصحابة فأنكره العلماء، وقال حافظ السنة الشيخ نجم الدين الغيطي: إحياء ليلة النصف من شعبان بجماعة، أنه قد أنكر ذلك أكثر العلماء من أهل الحجاز، منهم: عطاء وابن أبي مليكة وفقهاء أهل المدينة، وأصحاب مالك وغيرهم، وقالوا: ذلك كله بدعة ولم يثبت في قيامها جماعة شيء عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولا عن الصحابة الإحياء، ولم ينقل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا عن الصحابة إحياء ليلتي العيد جماعة، واختلف علماء الشام في صفة إحياء ليلة النصف من شعبان على قولين، أحدهما: أنه استحب إحياءها بجماعة في المسجد طائفة من أعيان التابعين كخالد بن معدان، ولقمان بن عامر، ووافقهم إسحاق بن راهويه والقول الثاني: أنه يكره الاجتماع لها في المساجد للصلاة، وهذا قول الأوزاعي إمام أهل الشام وفقيههم وعالمهم، انتهى.
And it is disliked to gather for the revival of any of these nights in the mosques. By prayer his heart dies, meaning: his heart is not agitated at the time of death, nor in the grave, nor on the Day of Resurrection. And standing (qiyam) is achieved by performing supererogatory prayer individually without a specific number, and by reciting the Quran, and listening to hadith, and by glorifying and praising, and by sending blessings and peace upon the Prophet, peace be upon him. And that is achieved during most of the night, and it is said: an hour of it. And from Ibn Abbas: the Isha prayer in congregation and the determination to pray the Fajr prayer in congregation, as they said regarding reviving the two Eid nights. And in Sahih Muslim: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever prays Isha in congregation, it is as if he has stood half the night; and whoever prays Fajr in congregation, it is as if he has stood the whole night.' And it is disliked to gather for the revival of any of these aforementioned nights in the mosques and elsewhere because the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not do it, nor the Companions, so the scholars disapproved of it. And the guardian of the Sunna, Sheikh Najm al-Din al-Ghayti, said: Regarding the revival of the night of mid-Sha'ban in congregation, most of the scholars of the Hijaz disapproved of that, among them: Ata, Ibn Abi Mulayka, the jurists of Medina, the followers of Malik, and others. They said: All of that is an innovation, and nothing has been established from the Prophet, peace be upon him, nor from the Companions regarding its revival in congregation. And it has not been reported from the Prophet, peace be upon him, nor from the Companions, the revival of the two Eid nights in congregation. The scholars of Syria differed on the manner of reviving the night of mid-Sha'ban in two opinions: One: that a group of eminent Tabi'un, such as Khalid ibn Ma'dan and Luqman ibn Amir, considered its revival in congregation in the mosque recommended, and Ishaq ibn Rahawayh agreed with them. The second opinion: that gathering for it in the mosques for prayer is disliked, and this is the opinion of al-Awza'i, the imam of the people of Syria, their jurist, and their scholar. End.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that gathering for the revival of specific nights, such as the night of mid-Sha'ban and the two Eid nights, in mosques is disliked (makruh). It begins by defining 'revival' of the night: it means engaging in prayer, Quran recitation, dhikr, and sending blessings upon the Prophet, individually and without a fixed number. The hadith from Sahih Muslim is cited to emphasize the virtue of praying Isha and Fajr in congregation, which is akin to standing half or the whole night. However, the passage then clarifies that communal gatherings for these nights are disliked because neither the Prophet nor the Companions practiced them. The author quotes al-Ghayti, who reports that most scholars of the Hijaz, including Ata and Ibn Abi Mulayka, considered such gatherings innovations. Among the Syrians, there were two views: some later Tabi'un considered it recommended, but the preponderant view, held by al-Awza'i, is that it is disliked. The overall ruling is that such gatherings are bid'ah and should be avoided, though an individual may revive these nights privately.

Key Terms
إحياء الليل (ihya' al-layl): Engaging in prayer, Quran recitation, dhikr, and other acts of worship during the night
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religion not established from the Prophet or Companions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it prevents people from sleeping
B) Because it is not proven from the Prophet or Companions
C) Because it causes noise in the mosque
D) Because it is only allowed on Laylat al-Qadr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers communal gatherings for the revival of mid-Sha'ban and Eid nights in mosques to be a disliked innovation (makruh), as it lacks basis in the Prophet's practice.

Recommended Prayer for One About to Be Executed
Supplement ruling on recommended prayer before execution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Muslim about to be executed and identify the three proofs (hadith and Companion action) that establish this recommendation.

Core Idea
When facing execution, pray two rak'ahs and seek forgiveness to end life with worship.

This supplement from al-Siyar al-Kabir addresses a specific situation: a Muslim captured and about to be killed by an enemy. The Hanafi school recommends that he pray two rak'ahs and seek forgiveness afterward, so that his final act is obedience to Allah. The text provides three proofs: general hadith about deeds being judged by their endings, a hadith about ending with the shahadah, and the specific action of the Companion Khubayb (RA), whom the Prophet praised and whose practice became a sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is ruled upon? The act is praying two rak'ahs and seeking forgiveness when one is about to be executed. The ruling is recommended (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) — not obligatory.
The text says 'yastahibbu' (it is recommended) — indicating mustahabb.
2
Locate the first proof
The Prophet said: 'Whoever seals his book with obedience, his past sins are forgiven' and 'Actions are judged by their endings.' These general principles encourage ending life with worship.
These are general hadith encouraging good endings.
3
Locate the second proof
The hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever's first and last speech is 'La ilaha illallah', his sins between them are forgiven.' This is applied here by analogy: one should end life with worship (prayer and istighfar) to seek forgiveness.
This hadith is also used for teaching the kalimah to children and dying persons.
4
Locate the third proof
The action of Khubayb ibn Adiyy: when the polytheists were about to kill him, he asked to pray two rak'ahs, and the Prophet praised him as 'sayyid al-shuhada' and said he is his companion in Paradise. This approval made the practice a sunnah.
The Prophet's approval (taqrir) establishes the practice as recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة: قال في السير الكبير: فإذا ابتلي المسلم بالقتل صبراً، فإنه يستحب له أن يصلي عند ذلك ركعتين يستغفر بعدهما ذنوبه ليكون آخر عمله الصلاة والاستغفار، قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: (من ختم كتابه بالطاعة غفر له ما سلف) وقال: (الأمور بخواتيمها) وفي حديث ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: (من كان أول كلامه وآخر كلامه قول لا إله إلا الله غفر له ما بين ذلك) ولهذا استحبوا أن يلقن الصبي في أول ما يقدر على التكلم كلمة التوحيد، ويلقن ذلك عند موته أيضاً؛ ليكون أول كلامه وآخر كلامه، وقد استحسن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما فعله خبيب رضي الله عنه عند إرادة المشركين قتله، من صلاته ركعتين، وسماه سيد الشهداء، وقال: (هو رفيقي في الجنة) فصارت سنة من ذلك الوقت، انتهى.
Supplement: He said in al-Siyar al-Kabir: If a Muslim is afflicted with execution by patience (i.e., captured and to be killed), then it is recommended for him to pray two rak'ahs at that time and then seek forgiveness for his sins so that his last action is prayer and seeking forgiveness. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever seals his book (record) with obedience, his past sins are forgiven.' And he said: 'Actions are judged by their endings.' And in the hadith of Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever's first speech and last speech is the statement: 'There is no god but Allah', his sins between them are forgiven.' For this reason, they recommended that a child be prompted to say the word of Tawhid as soon as he is able to speak, and also at the time of his death, so that his first and last speech is that. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, approved what Khubayb, may Allah be pleased with him, did when the polytheists intended to kill him: he prayed two rak'ahs. He called him the master of martyrs and said: 'He is my companion in Paradise.' So it became a sunnah from that time. End.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This supplement from al-Siyar al-Kabir (one of the six foundational works of the Hanafi school) provides the ruling that a Muslim who is about to be executed by an enemy should pray two rak'ahs and then seek forgiveness. This is recommended (mustahabb) to make his last worldly act an act of worship. The text supports this with three proofs: first, the general principle that deeds are judged by their endings; second, the hadith that whoever begins and ends with the shahadah is forgiven; and third, the action of the Companion Khubayb ibn Adiyy, who, when captured by the Quraysh and about to be crucified, asked to pray two rak'ahs, and the Prophet praised him as a leader of martyrs. This practice became established as a sunnah. The passage also mentions the related recommendation to teach the child the kalimah at the beginning of speech and at death, tying the idea of ending with good words.

Key Terms
القتل صبراً (al-qatlu sabran): Being killed while tied or captured, i.e., executed by the enemy
الاستغفار (al-istighfar): Seeking forgiveness from Allah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He recited the Quran loudly
B) He asked to pray two rak'ahs
C) He fought until death
D) He made a will

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends that a Muslim about to be executed pray two rak'ahs and seek forgiveness, based on hadith and the practice of Khubayb.

Permissibility of Optional Prayer While Sitting
Ruling on performing supererogatory prayers while seated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing supererogatory prayers while sitting and identify the special rulings for sunnat al-Fajr and Tarawih.

Core Idea
Nawafil are valid sitting even if able to stand, but sunnat al-Fajr and Tarawih have exceptions.

This passage addresses a common question: can one pray extra prayers while seated if able to stand? The Hanafi school generally permits it, but with notable exceptions. We will unpack the evidence, including consensus and the Prophet's practice, and examine the intra-madhhab disagreement on the sunna of Fajr and Tarawih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The author states it is permissible to perform supererogatory prayer (nafl) while sitting, even when able to stand. This includes both confirmed sunan (sunnan mu'akkada) and non-confirmed ones.
The term 'nafl' here covers all optional prayers except those with specific restrictions.
2
Examine the main evidence
The text cites consensus of scholars (ijma) as the primary proof. Additionally, the Prophet's own practice of sitting for much of his night prayer is mentioned as supporting evidence.
Consensus is considered a strong proof in Hanafi usul, equivalent to a definitive text.
3
Analyze the exception for sunnat al-Fajr
Despite the general permissibility, sunnat al-Fajr is treated differently due to its emphasis. Some narrations from Abu Hanifa indicate it is wajib (obligatory), while others treat it as a highly emphasized sunna. In both cases, praying it sitting without excuse is not permitted.
The difference between wajib and sunna mu'akkada impacts the ruling: even if considered sunna, its emphasis prohibits sitting.
4
Distinguish Tarawih from sunnat al-Fajr
For Tarawih, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Some equate it with sunnat al-Fajr, deeming sitting invalid. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) allows Tarawih sitting without excuse, but with half the reward. The distinction is based on the degree of emphasis.
Qadi Khan and al-Khulasa support the permissibility. The practical consequence: one can pray Tarawih sitting with reduced reward, but cannot pray Fajr sunna sitting at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في صلاة النفل جالساً وفي الصلاة على الدابة وصلاة الماشي (يجوز النفل) إنما عبر به ليشمل السنن المؤكدة وغيرها، فيصح أن يصليها (قاعداً، مع القدرة على القيام)، وقد حكي فيه إجماع العلماء، ولا يرد عليه سنة الفجر؛ لأنه لا يجوز أداؤها قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام على القول بسنيتها، فلا يستثنى من النوافل شيء، ولا يجوز على القول بوجوبها، ولذا قال الزيلعي: وأما السنن الرواتب فنوافل حتى يجوز على الدابة، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه ينزل لسنة الفجر؛ لأنها أكد من غيرها، روي عنه أنها واجبة، وعلى هذا الخلاف أداؤها قاعداً، انتهى. وقال في البرهان: وعن أبي حنيفة: أنه ينزل الراكب لسنة الفجر ولا يصليها قاعداً بناء على رواية وجوبها، انتهى. وقال قاضي خان في فصل أداء التراويح قاعداً: اتفقوا على أنه لا يستحب بغير عذر، واختلفوا في الجواز، قال بعضهم: لا يجوز بغير عذر، واستدلوا بما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله: أنه لو صلى سنة الفجر قاعداً بغير عذر لا يجوز، فكذا التراويح، إذ كل واحد منهما سنة مؤكدة، وقال بعضهم: يجوز أداء التراويح قاعداً بغير عذر، وفرقوا بين التراويح وبين سنة الفجر، وهو الصحيح، إلا أن ثوابه يكون على النصف من صلاة القائم، ووجه الفرق أن سنة الفجر مؤكدة لا خلاف فيها، والتراويح في التأكد دونها فلا يجوز التسوية بينهما. انتهى. وفي الخلاصة: وأما صلاة التراويح قاعداً من غير عذر اختلف المشايخ فيه، والأصح أنه يجوز، وأجمعوا أن ركعتي الفجر قاعداً من غير عذر لا يجوز، كذا روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة انتهى. ولا يخفى ما في حكاية الإجماع على عدم جواز ركعتي الفجر، حالة الجلوس من غير عذر، لما قد علمته وليس الإجماع إلا على تأكدها. فليتأمل. ولما جاز النفل قاعداً على كل حال لأنه كان يصلي بعد الوتر قاعداً، وكان يجلس في عامة صلاته بالليل تخفيفاً)، كما ذكره شيخ الإسلام، ولم يقبض حتى كان أكثر صلاته جالساً ) أي: في النفل كما روته عائشة الله، وفي رواية عنها: (فلما أراد أن يركع، قام فقرا
Chapter on supererogatory prayer while sitting, and prayer on a mount, and the prayer of a walking person. It is permissible to perform supererogatory prayer - he only expressed it like this to include the confirmed sunan and others - so it is valid to pray it while sitting, despite being able to stand. And consensus of scholars has been reported on this. The sunna of Fajr is not an exception to this because it is not permissible to perform it while sitting when able to stand according to the view that it is sunna. So nothing is excluded from the nawafil, but it is not permissible according to the view that it is obligatory. Therefore, al-Zayla'i said: As for the regular sunan (rawatib), they are nawafil, so they are permissible on a mount. And from Abu Hanifa: that he dismounts for the sunna of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others; it is reported from him that it is obligatory, and upon this difference is its performance while sitting. End. And he said in al-Burhan: And from Abu Hanifa: that the rider dismounts for the sunna of Fajr and does not pray it sitting based on the narration of its obligation. End. And Qadi Khan said in the chapter on performing Tarawih while sitting: They agreed that it is not recommended without an excuse, and they differed on its permissibility. Some said: it is not permissible without an excuse, and they argued with what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: that if he prayed the sunna of Fajr while sitting without an excuse, it is not permissible, and similarly Tarawih, since each is a confirmed sunna. Others said: it is permissible to perform Tarawih while sitting without an excuse, and they differentiated between Tarawih and the sunna of Fajr, and this is correct, except that his reward is half that of the standing prayer. The reason for the difference is that the sunna of Fajr is confirmed without dispute, while Tarawih is less confirmed, so they cannot be equated. End. And in al-Khulasa: As for Tarawih prayer while sitting without an excuse, the mashayikh differed, and the most correct is that it is permissible. And they are unanimous that the two rak'ahs of Fajr while sitting without an excuse are not permissible; likewise al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa. End. And it is not hidden what is in the claim of consensus on the impermissibility of the two rak'ahs of Fajr in a state of sitting without an excuse, because you have learned that consensus is only on its emphasis. So let one ponder. And when it is permissible to perform supererogatory prayer while sitting in any case, because he used to pray after witr sitting, and he used to sit in most of his night prayer for ease, as mentioned by Shaykh al-Islam, and he did not pass away until most of his prayer was sitting - i.e., in supererogatory prayer as Aisha narrated, and in a narration from her: 'When he wanted to bow, he stood up and recited...'
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This chapter discusses the ruling on performing supererogatory prayers (nawafil) while sitting, even if one is able to stand. The author states that it is permissible and cites consensus. However, the sunna of Fajr is a point of contention because of its emphasis. The text narrates from Abu Hanifa that he considers it obligatory, and therefore one should not pray it sitting. Other scholars consider it a confirmed sunna but still not permissible to perform sitting without an excuse due to its high status. For Tarawih, there is a difference: some equate it with the Fajr sunna, while others permit it sitting, though with half the reward. The author notes that the claim of consensus on the impermissibility of Fajr sunna sitting is problematic; the real consensus is only on its emphasis. The passage concludes by referencing the Prophet's practice of sitting for much of his night prayer, establishing that sitting is permissible in general for nawafil.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer, including both confirmed sunan and non-confirmed
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs before the Fajr obligatory prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible with full reward
B) Permissible but disliked
C) Not permissible (either invalid or makruh tahrimi)
D) Obligatory to perform standing

Key Takeaway
Nawafil are valid sitting, but sunnat al-Fajr and Tarawih have distinct rulings based on their degree of emphasis.

Voluntary Prayer While Sitting: Permissibility and Reward
General ruling on voluntary prayer sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayer while sitting and identify when half reward applies.

Core Idea
Sitting voluntarily is valid but gets half reward; full reward only with excuse.

This passage establishes a foundational principle: voluntary prayer (nafl) may be performed sitting even when one can stand. This permissibility is supported by consensus and prophetic practice. However, the reward is reduced to half unless there is a valid excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general ruling
The passage begins by stating that voluntary prayer (nafl) is permissible while sitting, emphasizing that 'nafl' includes all supererogatory prayers. Note the hukm level: permissible (mubah), not obligatory.
This covers both emphasized and non-emphasized sunnahs except where exceptions apply.
2
Locate the proof for half reward
The author cites a hadith: 'Whoever prays standing has the best reward, whoever prays sitting has half the reward of the standing...' This is a clear dalil from the Prophet (ﷺ).
The hadith is narrated by al-Jama'ah except Muslim; its thubut is zanni (single transmission), but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the exception for an excuse
The passage explicitly states that if one prays sitting due to a valid excuse (e.g., illness), the reward becomes full, equal to standing.
Consensus is cited for this: the prayer of the excused person is equal in merit.
4
Connect to the Hanafi principle of facilitation
The commentary explains that permitting sitting prevents abandonment of voluntary prayer due to hardship, ensuring its continuity. This reflects the Hanafi focus on ease.
Thus, the ruling balances devotion with pragmatism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

يرد عليه سنة الفجر؛ لأنه لا يجوز أداؤها قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام على القول بسنيتها، فلا يستثنى من النوافل شيء، ولا يجوز على القول بوجوبها، ولذا قال الزيلعي: وأما السنن الرواتب فنوافل حتى يجوز على الدابة، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه ينزل لسنة الفجر؛ لأنها أكد من غيرها، روي عنه أنها واجبة، وعلى هذا الخلاف أداؤها قاعداً، انتهى. وقال في البرهان» : وعن أبي حنيفة: أنه ينزل الراكب لسنة الفجر ولا يصليها قاعداً بـنـاء عـلـى روايــة وجوبها، انتهى. وقال « قاضي خان» في فصل أداء التراويح قاعداً: اتفقوا على أنه لا يستحب بـغـيـر عذر، واختلفوا في الجواز ، قال بعضهم : لا يجوز بغير عذر، واستدلوا بما روى الحسـن عــن أبـي حنيفة رحمه الله : أنه لو صلى سنة الفجر قاعداً بغير عذر لا يجوز، فكذا التراويح، إذ كل واحد منهما سنة مؤكدة، وقال بعضهم: يجوز أداء التراويح قاعداً بغير عذر، وفرقوا بين التراويح وبين سنة الفجر، وهو الصحيح، إلا أن ثوابه يكون على النصف من صلاة القائم، ووجه الفرق أن سنة الفجر مؤكدة لا خلاف فيها، والتراويح في التأكد دونها فلا يجوز التسوية بينهما. انتهى. وفي « الخلاصة : وأما صلاة التراويح قاعداً من غير عذر اختلف المشايخ فيه، والأصح أنه يجوز، وأجمعوا أن ركعتي الفجر قاعداً من غير عذر لا يجوز، كذا روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة انتهى. ولا يخفى ما في حكاية الإجماع على عدم جواز ركعتي الفجر، حالة الجلوس من غير عذر ، لما قد علمته وليس الإجماع إلا على تأكدها. فليتأمل. ولما جاز النفل قاعداً على كل حال لأنه كان يُصلِّي بعد الـوتـــر قـاعـداً، وكان يجلس في عامة صلاته بالليل تخفيفاً)، كما ذكره شيخ الإسلام، ولم يقبض حتى كان أكثر صلاته جالساً ) أي : في النفل كما روته عائشة الله، وفي رواية عنها : ( فلما أَرَادَ أَنْ يَرْكَعَ ، قَامَ فَقَرَا آيَاتٍ، ثُمَّ رَكَعَ وَسَجَدَ وَعَادَ إِلَى القُعُودِ ) وقال في ( المعراج » : وهو المستحب في كل متطوع قاعداً، قلنا و (لكن له) أي: للتنفل جالساً (نصف أجر القائم) لقوله : « مَنْ صَلَّى قَائِمًا فَهُوَ أفْضَلُ، وَمَنْ صَلَّى قَاعِدًا فَلَهُ نِصْفُ أَجْرِ الْقَائِمِ، وَمَنْ صَلَّى نَائِمًا فَلَهُ نِصْفُ أَجْرِ الْقَاعِدِ » ) رواه الجماعة إلا مسلماً. ولأن الصلاة خير موضوع فلو شرط القيام دائماً ولم يجز القعود في النفـل، ربما أفضى إلى تركه لنوع ضعف ومشقة، ففي شرعيته دوامها، كذا في ( البرهان» ويكون له النصف إلا منْ عُدْرٍ)، فإذا تنفل جالساً بعذر يكون له أجر القائم تاماً. قال في « المعراج » : الإجماع منعقد على أن صلاة القاعد بعذر مساوية لصلاة القائم في الأجر، بل إنه ذكـر بعـد الحديـث الـذي رويناه قالوا: وهذا في حق القادر، وأما العاجز فصلاته بالإيماء أفضل مـن صـلاة الـقـائـم الـراكــع الساجد؛ لأنه جهد المقل. انتهى. وقال ( الكمال بن الهمام» رحمه الله تعالى: وفي الحديث: « صَلاةُ النَّائِمِ عَلَى النِّصْفِ مِنْ صَلَاةِ القَاعِدِ ، ولا نعلم الصلاة نائماً تسوغ إلا في الفرض حالـة الـعـجـز عن القعود، وهذا يعكر على حملهم الحديث على النفل، ثم قال: ولا أعلمـه يـعـنـي: جواز النفل نائماً قادراً في فقهنا، انتهى. وقد يشير إلى أنه يجوز في فقهنا ما قدمناه عن « الدراية» من لفظه، قالوا: هذا في حق القادر لأن الإشارة راجعة إلى الحالات كلّها، فتشمل صلاة القادر نائماً؛ لأن لفظة قالوا تذكر فيما فيه الخلاف، وقد صرح بنفي جوازه نائماً في ( البحر » ، عن شرح « المشارق»، فقال: ورد في بعض رواياته « وَمَنْ صَلَّى نَائِمَاً - أي: مضطجعاً فلَه نِصْفُ أَجْرِ القَاعِدِ ) ولا يمكن حمله علــى القدرة إذ لا يصح مضطجعاً، اللهم إلا أن يحكم بشذوذ هذه الرواية. انتهى. وفيه إشكال من حيثية تنقيص أجره، ولم يُصل مضطجعاً الفرض إلا بعذر، وهو مع العذر أفضل من صلاة القائم الراكع الساجد، كما قد علمته، فلا يتجه إلا على صحة النفل مضطجعـاً مـع القـدرة عليـه قـاعـداً
Chapter on voluntary prayer while sitting, and on prayer upon a mount, and the prayer of the walker. Voluntary prayer is permissible sitting, even with the ability to stand. By this expression he intends to include the emphasized and non-emphasized sunnahs. So it is valid for one to pray it while sitting, with the ability to stand. Consensus of the scholars has been narrated on this. The sunnah of Fajr is not an exception to this, because it is not permissible to perform it sitting while able to stand according to the opinion that it is a sunnah. So nothing is excluded from the voluntary prayers. And it is not permissible according to the opinion that it is obligatory. Therefore al-Zayla'i said: As for the regular sunnahs, they are voluntary such that they are permissible on a mount. From Abu Hanifa that he dismounts for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others. It is narrated from him that it is obligatory, and based on this difference is its performance sitting. Al-Qadi Khan said in the chapter on performing tarawih sitting: They agreed that it is not recommended without an excuse, and they differed on permissibility. Some said: it is not permissible without an excuse, and they adduced what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: that if one prays the sunnah of Fajr sitting without an excuse it is not permissible, likewise tarawih, since each is an emphasized sunnah. Others said: it is permissible to perform tarawih sitting without an excuse, and they differentiated between tarawih and the sunnah of Fajr, and this is the correct view, except that his reward is half that of the standing person. The distinction is that the sunnah of Fajr is emphatically agreed upon, while tarawih is less in emphasis, so they cannot be equated. In al-Khulasa: Regarding tarawih prayer sitting without an excuse, the teachers differed; the most correct is that it is permissible. They all agreed that the two rak'ahs of Fajr sitting without an excuse are not permissible, as al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa. It is not hidden what is in the claim of consensus on the impermissibility of the two rak'ahs of Fajr in a sitting state without an excuse, as you have known; there is no consensus except on its emphasis. So let one reflect. Since voluntary prayer is permissible sitting in all circumstances because he used to pray after witr sitting, and he would sit in most of his night prayer for facilitation, as Shaykh al-Islam mentioned, and he did not pass away until most of his prayer was sitting — i.e., in voluntary prayer as Aisha narrated. In a narration from her: When he intended to bow, he stood and recited verses, then bowed and prostrated and returned to sitting. And it is said in al-Mi'raj: It is recommended for every voluntary one praying sitting. We say: But for the one praying voluntary sitting, he has half the reward of the standing one, due to his saying: 'Whoever prays standing is best, whoever prays sitting has half the reward of the standing, and whoever prays lying has half the reward of the sitting.' The group narrated it except Muslim. And because prayer is the best act; if standing were always required and sitting were not permitted in voluntary prayer, it might lead to abandoning it due to some weakness and hardship. So in its legislation is its continuity. Thus in al-Burhan. And he has half except with an excuse. So if one prays voluntary sitting with an excuse, he has the full reward of the standing one. In al-Mi'raj: Consensus is established that the prayer of the sitting person with an excuse is equal in reward to the prayer of the standing. Indeed, after the hadith we narrated, they said: This applies to the able person. As for the incapable, his prayer by gesture is better than the prayer of the standing, bowing, prostrating person, because it is the effort of the destitute. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam said: In the hadith: 'The prayer of the lying person is half that of the sitting.' We do not know that prayer lying down is permitted except in obligatory prayer in the case of inability to sit. This contradicts their interpretation of the hadith as referring to voluntary prayer. Then he said: I do not know it — meaning: the permissibility of voluntary prayer lying down for the able person in our fiqh. It may indicate that it is permissible in our fiqh what we presented from al-Diraya from its wording: They said: This applies to the able person because the reference returns to all states, so it includes the prayer of the able person lying down; because the word 'they said' is mentioned in issues of disagreement. The impermissibility of it lying down has been clearly stated in al-Bahr from Sharh al-Mashariq. He said: In some of its narrations it is reported: 'And whoever prays lying down — i.e., reclining — has half the reward of the sitting.' It cannot be interpreted as ability because it is not valid reclining. Unless one rules that this narration is anomalous. There is a problem regarding the reduction of his reward, and he did not pray obligatory lying down except with an excuse, and with an excuse it is better than the prayer of the standing, bowing, prostrating person, as you have learned. So it is only reasonable on the validity of voluntary prayer reclining while able to sit.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on voluntary prayer (nafl) while sitting. The author begins by stating the general ruling: it is permissible to perform voluntary prayer sitting even if one can stand. This covers both emphasized (muakkadah) and non-emphasized sunnahs. The text reports consensus on this permissibility. However, an exception is made for the sunnah of Fajr (the two rak'ahs before the obligatory Fajr prayer). According to one narration from Abu Hanifa, the sunnah of Fajr is obligatory (wajib), so it cannot be performed sitting without excuse. Even on the view that it is sunnah, some scholars disallow sitting for it due to its strong emphasis. The text then discusses tarawih prayer: some analogize it to sunnat al-Fajr and forbid sitting without excuse, but the correct position (al-sahih) allows tarawih sitting without excuse, though with half reward. The distinction is that tarawih is less emphasized. The author then provides hadith evidence: the Prophet's practice of praying sitting in his later years, and the explicit hadith that the sitting person gets half the reward of the standing. An exception is made for those with an excuse: they receive full reward. The commentary also engages with a secondary issue: voluntary prayer lying down (na'im/mudtaji'). Some narrations suggest it is permissible with half reward, but other authorities deny its validity in the Hanafi school for those able to sit. The author highlights the tension and leaves the issue open.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Voluntary or supererogatory prayer, including both emphasized (sunan rawatib) and non-emphasized acts.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-muakkadah): Emphasized sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and rarely omitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a person praying voluntary prayer sitting receive full reward?
A) When they always pray sitting.
B) When they have a valid excuse like illness.
C) When they are traveling.
D) When they pray silently.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer while sitting is always valid; reward depends on ability and presence of excuse.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Exceptions and Disputes: Sunnat al-Fajr and Tarawih
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting in certain sunnah prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on sitting in sunnat al-Fajr and tarawih, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Sunnat al-Fajr is stricter than other nafl; tarawih is milder and sitting is allowed.

While voluntary prayer sitting is generally allowed, two specific prayers have generated significant internal Hanafi debate: the sunnah of Fajr and tarawih. The passage reviews conflicting narrations from Abu Hanifa and the arguments for analogy versus distinction. Understanding this dispute helps to appreciate the nuanced hierarchy of emphasized sunnahs.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the special status of sunnat al-Fajr
The passage reports two views from Abu Hanifa: one that it is wajib (obligatory), another that it is an emphasized sunnah. The stricter view prohibits sitting without excuse; even on the milder view, many scholars forbid sitting due to its strong emphasis.
Al-Zayla'i confirms that Abu Hanifa would dismount (if on a ride) to pray sunnat al-Fajr, indicating its special nature.
2
Analyze the dispute on tarawih
The passage presents two positions: some analogize tarawih to sunnat al-Fajr and forbid sitting without excuse; others distinguish them, allowing tarawih sitting with half reward.
The distinguishing factor is the degree of emphasis: Fajr sunnah is universally agreed as very strong, while tarawih is less emphasized.
3
Identify the reliance (tarjih)
The author cites al-Qadi Khan and al-Khulasa that the correct view for tarawih is permissibility. The claim of consensus on Fajr is critiqued: the consensus is only on its emphasis, not on the prohibition of sitting.
Thus the mufta bihi: Fajr sunnah should not be performed sitting without excuse; tarawih may be performed sitting.
